# **LET'S GET ORGANIZED** 

---

# **CHAPTER ONE: THESE MIST COVERED MOUNTAINS**

---

## **INT.  GILLEY’S GARAGE – NIGHT – SUMMER 1990**

A **box fan** drones in the corner, moving hot air like a punishment. The **garage door’s open** but it barely helps. It’s one of those Ohio nights where everything sticks—**drumsticks**, **T-shirts**, **opinions**.

**[[4.4 JIM BROWN character bible|JIM]]** is coiling a cable with militant precision.  **[[4.6 JEREMY EVANS character bible|JEREMY]]** is sweating, glowering, and winding a guitar cord into *knots*, not loops.

**JEREMY**
I’m just saying… the last practice? You sounded like someone trying to impress a girl in a jazz elective.

**JIM** (flatly)
Cool. Thanks.

**JEREMY**
It’s like you were afraid to actually hit anything. You played that last verse like it was modern dance.

**JIM**
You mean with **control**?

**JEREMY**
No, I mean with… like… **perfume.**

**JIM** (sets the cable down)
You don’t know what the fuck you’re talking about.

**JEREMY**
Oh, I absolutely do. You used that hi-hat like it was whispering secrets to you. I thought we were playing punk.

**JIM**
We *are* playing punk. Just not *your* version of it.

**JEREMY**
Yeah, because mine doesn’t come with eyeliner and a pillow.

**JIM** (standing up)
You want to know who plays like a pillow? Bonham. That dude hit hard but he *dragged* like his sticks were full of soup.

**JEREMY**
Don’t do that. Don’t act like you’re cool just because you hate Zeppelin.

**JIM**
I’m not trying to be cool. I’m trying to not be lazy. Every fill he did was like “I guess I’ll swing my arm now.” That’s not timekeeping. That’s bowling.

**JEREMY** (genuinely shocked)
Okay, you just compared John Bonham to a *bowling ball.* What the fuck.

**JIM**
I stand by it. You want speed? You want clarity? You call the Ramones. You want emotional lift? Talking Heads. You want muscle memory precision? **Larry. Mullen. Junior.**

**JEREMY**
He’s Irish.

**JIM** (shrugging)
Emotionally American.

**JEREMY**
That’s not how that works!

**JIM** (ignoring him)
I like guys who know how to drive the tempo *forward*, not show off their fucking blood alcohol content.

**JEREMY**
And Phil Collins?

**JIM**
Yes. Phil Collins. That gated reverb sound? That’s a **door slamming on God’s face.**

**JEREMY**
He’s also British.

**JIM**
He’s exempt. He sounds like thunder in a tuxedo.

**JEREMY**
You want this shit to be *danceable*, don’t you?

**JIM**
I want it to **hit**, Jeremy. I want the low end to feel like an *apology*. Have you ever heard fIREHOSE? Ever hear Minutemen? George Hurley didn’t play to impress people. He played like he was communicating with seismic fault lines.

**JEREMY**
You’re making shit up now.

**JIM**
Okay. Bruce Slesinger. Dead Kennedys. The dude played like his kit owed him money.

**JEREMY**
You just like him because his name sounds like a fake ID.

**JIM**
He had a surf-punk snare and fascist timing. *Perfect.* You can’t even play to a metronome.

**JEREMY**
Because the metronome can’t *feel*, Jim.

**JIM**
Neither can you, apparently.

(They stare at each other. The fan whirs louder. A moth suicides into the hi-hat.)

**JEREMY**
One day, we’re gonna play CBGB. And I’m gonna unplug your entire kit mid-set.

**JIM**
You do that, I’m plugging in the drum machine.

**JEREMY**
You’re a fascist.

**JIM**
You’re a tourist.

**[[4.2 JEREMY GILLEY character bible|GILLEY]] (O.S.)**
Will you two idiots shut the fuck up and help me carry the amp? Or are you getting married?

(Beat. They both grab the amp.)

**JIM**
I’m naming my next snare “Jeremy.” Just so I can beat it with a stick.

**JEREMY**
That’s the most romantic thing you’ve ever said to me.

**They carry the amp out together, still muttering.**

*Fade out with the sound of a cymbal getting bumped. And a snort-laugh that neither of them will admit came from themselves.*

---

## **EXT. GILLEY’S DRIVEWAY – LATE NIGHT – MID-SUMMER 1990**

The **sky is deep blue velvet**, flecked with stars. **Fireflies blink** like tiny signal lights across the grass and gravel.  The **garage door is open**, spilling warm yellow light and the faint echo of reverb and amp buzz. **Bill Davenport** walks past, holding a **sweating plastic gas station cup** with **ice water**. He’s got **two mic stands tucked under one arm**, and a **tangle of cords looped around his neck** like he’s preparing for battle.

He doesn’t stop walking.

**[[4.1 BILL DAVENPORT character bible|BILL]]** (quiet, factual)
Dead Kennedys are pretty fucking cool.

(He disappears into the garage.)

**JEREMY** (blinking)
See? Even Bill knows what time it is.

**JIM**
Yeah, and Bill also listens to Tangerine Dream when he’s stoned, so forgive me if I don’t recalibrate everything.

**JEREMY**
Tangerine Dream has *vibes*, man.

**JIM**
Tangerine Dream has *no drums*.

(Beat. The fireflies blink. Gravel crunches underfoot.)

**JEREMY**
Okay. Serious question.

**JIM**
God help me.

**JEREMY**
That dude you named. Larry Mullins.

**JIM**
A goddamn genius.

**JEREMY**
Yeah. Is he, like… Larry Mullen’s dad? Like… Larry Mullen *Senior*?

**JIM** (freezes)
Are you *seriously* asking me that?

**JEREMY**
I’m just saying. Both named Larry. Both drummers. One’s got a Jr. The math checks out.

**JIM**
Jesus Christ.

**JEREMY**
What?

**JIM**
You think Swans and U2 had *Thanksgiving together*?

**JEREMY**
Could’ve been a rough dinner. Bono would cry. Michael Gira would knock over the gravy and scream in Latin.

**JIM**
Jesus *Christ*, Jeremy.

(The fireflies blink again. Someone in the garage drops a cymbal.)

**JEREMY**
One day, this is all gonna matter. All this. Your little drummer obsession, my future platinum hair, Gilley’s inability to hold a tuner.

**JIM**
Yeah?

**JEREMY**
Yeah. One day, some poor asshole’s gonna have to *catalog all of it.* And I just want to say right now: you’re welcome, dude.

**JIM** (snorts)
Tell it to remember you as the guy who confused Larry *fucking* Mullen Jr. with Toby Dammit.

**JEREMY**
*Toby Dammit* sounds like a cartoon character.

**JIM**
Sounds like a threat.

**JEREMY**
Sounds like my next alias when I rent gear while underage.

(They both laugh, involuntarily. A long, stupid, adolescent cackle into the summer night.)

**JIM**
God, we’re idiots.

**JEREMY**
We’re artists.

**JIM**
We’re idiots *with sticks and wires.*

**JEREMY**
And fireflies.

(Beat. The night hums around them.)

**GILLEY (O.S.)**
Anytime now, assholes. This amp’s not going to levitate itself.

They both sigh, then move toward the garage.

**JIM**
Don’t touch my snare.

**JEREMY**
Which one? “*Jeremy*”?

**JIM**
You touch it, it gets renamed “*Shithead*.”

**JEREMY**
Dude. That’s my *Dad’s* name.

(The fireflies blink again. The summer hum carries them forward.)

---

## **EXT. GILLEY’S DRIVEWAY – LATER – NIGHT**

The amp’s been hauled. The tension’s cooled.  Jim and Jeremy sit on opposite ends of the tailgate of **Gilley’s rusting pickup**, drinking flat root beer from cans that were cold **hours ago**. Fireflies still blink in the tall grass. A porch light flickers across the street.

**JEREMY**
Okay. Hypothetical.

**JIM**
God help me.

**JEREMY**
Let’s say we make it big.

**JIM**
“Big” like *regional success*, or “big” like *Gilley finally stops stealing mic cables*?

**JEREMY**
Like Bono big.

**JIM** (pause)
Jesus.

**JEREMY**
I mean it. We hit stadiums. We're wearing sunglasses indoors. We get one-word names. Stage names.

**JIM**
I already have a name.

**JEREMY**
Yeah. *Jim.*

**JIM**
It’s a classic.

**JEREMY**
It’s a tire salesman. “Come on down to Jim Brown’s Used Pontiac Warehouse. We’ll beat the tax man to death.”

**JIM**
You wanna go? Let’s hear yours.

**JEREMY** (offhand)
*Thresher.*

**JIM**
That’s a *shark.*

**JEREMY**
Exactly. Or a wheat-harvesting machine. Either way: *efficient, terrifying, metal as hell.*

**JIM**
You’re gonna get sued by a John Deere dealership.

**JEREMY**
Better than *Jim.*

**JIM**
Fine. Then I’m… *Vector.*

**JEREMY**
Oh shit. Vector. Like math?

**JIM**
Like a trajectory. Like *intent.*

**JEREMY**
Like… a guy who owns 3 synthesizers and no deodorant.

**JIM**
Okay, *Thresher*.

**JEREMY**
I sound like a weapon. You sound like an art student who says “liminal” too much.

(Beat.)

**JIM**
Alright. Best stage name we’ve ever heard?

**JEREMY**
Toby Dammit. No contest.

**JIM**
Told you it sounds like a warning label.

**JEREMY**
Ha. Or a punchline.

**JIM**
Or a lawsuit waiting to happen.

**JEREMY**
Exactly. That’s the vibe.

**JIM**
Okay. *Real talk.* If you had to wear leather pants and eyeliner and go onstage tomorrow with a single-name identity, what is it?

(Jeremy stares off at the blinking fireflies. Then…)

**JEREMY**
*Ruin.*

**JIM**
*Jesus!*

**JEREMY**
No one forgets a guy named Ruin.

**JIM**
You’re sixteen. What have you ruined?

**JEREMY**
A geometry quiz. Two relationships. One lawnmower. I’m building my résumé.

**JIM**
I’m gonna be “*Crater*.”

**JEREMY**
Why?

**JIM**
Because every time I drop a fill, something explodes.

**JEREMY**
I like that. Ruin and Crater.

**JIM**
We sound like villains from a Mad Max sequel.

**JEREMY**
Better than “Jeremy and Jim.”

**JIM**
…Actually, yeah.

(They sit in silence. A firefly lands on Jim’s wrist. He watches it blink once. Then it flies off.)

**JEREMY**
Good practice tonight.

**JIM**
Terrible fight.

**JEREMY**
Great fight.

**JIM**
Yeah. Great fight.

---

## **EXT. GILLEY’S DRIVEWAY – NIGHT – CONTINUOUS**

The fireflies blink. The air smells like asphalt and crushed grass. Jeremy lies stretched across the tailgate of the pickup, arms behind his head, staring up at the stars like they owe him something. Jim sits nearby, picking at the label of a now-lukewarm root beer can.

**JEREMY**
Crater would be a whole lot better than your actual name.

**JIM**
Here we go.

**JEREMY**
Seriously—*James Brown?* That name was taken *before your dad even met your mom*. By the *Godfather of Soul*. There’s a cape involved.

**JIM**
I’ve thought about it.

**JEREMY**
And?

**JIM**
I’ll go by Jim. Just Jim. Clean. No cape.

**JEREMY**
Still sounds like the guy who fixes my brakes.

**JIM**
I *like* my brakes.

**JEREMY**
Crater sounds like someone who doesn’t even *have* brakes. Just momentum and regret.

**JIM**
Crater sounds like a rash.

**JEREMY**
Crater sounds like *legend.* If Phil Collins had gone by Crater? Nobody would’ve laughed. They’d have evacuated the arena.

**JIM**
You’re not branding me, Jeremy.

**JEREMY**
We could solve this democratically.

**JIM** (shoots him a look)
You want to *vote* on my name?

**JEREMY**
It’s the American way.

**JIM**
How many people even qualify to vote?

**JEREMY**
Six.

**JIM**
Six?

**JEREMY**
Me, you, Kathy, Bill, Gilley, and Jeff. That’s six. Boom. Full electorate.

**JIM**
Kathy’s not really 100% in the band yet.

**JEREMY**
But she’s on the path. She’s seen things. She plays things. That counts.

**JIM**
You are not dragging me into a band government.

**JEREMY**
Why not? Band democracy! Think about it. Term limits. Motions. Vetoes. Parliamentary snare rolls.

**JIM**
You’re making it sound worse.

**JEREMY**
One man, one vote. One amp, one grievance. We all pick your stage name and it goes on the first t-shirt.

**JIM**
If I see “Crater” on merch I didn’t authorize, I will personally rip your tuning pegs out with my teeth.

**JEREMY**
You’re proving my point. *Crater energy.*

(Beat. A firefly lands on Jeremy’s shirt and blinks. He doesn’t move.)

**JIM**
Jim Brown isn’t flashy. But it’s mine. It’s real.

**JEREMY**
Crater Brown sounds like a funk bassist from a forgotten Earth, Wind & Fire timeline.

**JIM**
You say that like it’s a bad thing.

**JEREMY**
One day, when they ask us how we got our names, I’m gonna say: *We voted. I lost. But I planted the seed.*

**JIM**
One day, when we’re famous, I’m gonna say: *I almost beat that kid to death with a hi-hat stand, but he made me laugh, so I didn’t.*

(The fireflies blink again. A dog barks in the distance. Someone inside the garage is arguing with a kick drum.)

**JIM (CONT’D)**
Let’s go load the rest of the gear before Bill declares himself treasurer and starts taxing us for mic cables.

**JEREMY**
Band democracy, baby. *Power to the people.*

(They slide off the truck bed and head back toward the garage, still talking, still grinning, still arguing.)

*Fade out on two silhouettes framed by sodium light and teenage confidence.*

---

## **EXT. GILLEY’S DRIVEWAY – NIGHT – CONTINUOUS**

The fireflies glow steady now. The laughter’s still echoing faintly, but the mood's drifting—calmer, more reflective.

From the shadows near the street, **KATHY** appears.  She’s trudging up the driveway, her **jeans dark with sweat**, **work boots scuffed**, and a **long-sleeved flannel shirt** pulled awkwardly over a **black band tee** that’s clinging to her back. Her bangs are stuck to her forehead. She looks like she just finished fighting her way out of a basement gig and lost a round to a box fan.

**JEREMY** (over his shoulder)
Oh shit. It’s Kathy.

**JIM**
Careful. She’s got that *about to murder the sound guy* energy.

**JEREMY**
Or she’s hiding a dagger in that flannel.

**[[4.5 KATHY ESPICH character bible|KATHY]]** (overhearing)
Or I’m hiding the fact that it’s 1990 and *dudes* still think it’s hilarious to comment on what girls wear.

(Jeremy holds up his hands in mock surrender. Kathy walks right past him, straight up to Jim.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
You okay?

**JIM** (quiet, but honest)
Yeah. Just the usual existential crisis about naming rights and stage legacy.

**KATHY** (eyebrows raised)
So, a Tuesday.

(She turns to Jeremy. Locks eyes. Doesn’t blink.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
You don’t get to talk shit about Jim. Not like that. Not in front of me.

**JEREMY**
Whoa—hang on—

**KATHY**
Nah. I’m serious.

(She gestures vaguely at her sweat-drenched, shapeless outfit.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
You think I show up like this for fun? You think I dress like I lost a bet because it’s comfortable?

(Beat. Neither of them speaks.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
I show up like this so I don’t get treated like a *girl in a band.* I show up like this so I can *be in the band.* Just like Jim. Just like Bill. Just like you. But Jim? He’s the only one who never made me feel like I had to prove it.

(Jeremy looks down. Gravel crunches under his sneaker.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
So next time you wanna throw some weak-ass, “you sound soft” bullshit around?  Throw it at me.  Or don’t throw it at all.

(Jim watches, quietly stunned. Jeremy scratches the back of his neck.)

**JEREMY**
I didn’t mean it like—

**KATHY**
Doesn’t matter how you meant it. You *said* it. Now un-say it, or own it.

(Jeremy exhales. Then, with a half-smile—one part apology, one part teenage dumbass reflex:)

**JEREMY**
I think Crater softened your brain.

(Kathy snorts.)

**KATHY**
Crater’s gonna crater your effing skull if you keep talking.

(She bumps Jim on the shoulder as she walks past, heading for the garage.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Don’t let him name you. You’re not a mascot.

**JIM**
Thanks, Kathy.

**KATHY** (half turning)
You’re Jim. That’s enough.

(She disappears into the garage. A cymbal crashes inside a second later—either on purpose or out of spite.)

**JEREMY** (pause)
She scares the hell out of me.

**JIM**
That’s why she’s here.

(The fireflies blink once. Then again.)

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – CONTINUOUS**

**KATHY** vanishes through the side door into the Gilley residence proper. The screen door bangs behind her. Inside, somewhere, a floor fan whines and a faucet runs. She’s gone to cool off—physically, mentally, emotionally.

Outside, **JIM** starts loading mic stands into the van, leaving **JEREMY** and **BILL DAVENPORT** alone in the soft yellow garage light.  **BILL** is sitting on an amp case, finishing his ice water. The cup is half-melted. He looks like he’s aged six years in the last two hours.

**JEREMY**
Hey. Hypothetical.

**BILL** (grunts)
Dangerous opening.

**JEREMY**
What if—like, *just what if*—we handled more stuff in the band *democratically*?

**BILL** (skeptical)
Like what? Voting on songs?

**JEREMY**
Maybe. Or names. Branding. Setlists. Rehearsal schedules. Naming Jim something other than Jim.

**BILL** (squinting)
Did he finally cave and accept “*Crater*”?

**JEREMY**
He caved in spirit. Not on paper. Yet.

**BILL**
And you think voting on it would go well?

**JEREMY**
We’re a band. We’ve got a headcount. It’s inherently governmental. Like a really loud city council.

**BILL**
City council with no budget and too many opinions.

**JEREMY**
Exactly.

**BILL**
I mean, in theory… democracy sounds kinda nice. Better than letting Gilley make all the decisions just because he owns the PA.

**JEREMY**
That’s what I’m saying. We *empower the masses*.

**BILL**
You mean you.

**JEREMY**
The masses start with me. Then they grow.

**BILL** (flatly)
Fascism also starts with one guy and a megaphone.

**JEREMY** (ignores him)
We could have bylaws. Like: no ballads without a supermajority.

**BILL**
Or: all songwriting disputes go to Kathy for arbitration.

**JEREMY** (eyes lighting up)
Yes! She’s scary *and* fair. She’d make an excellent Supreme Court.

**BILL**
Or executioner.

**JEREMY**
Sometimes both.

(Beat. They listen to the sound of **Jim slamming the van door shut** outside.)

**BILL**
So what’s the first thing you’d vote on?

**JEREMY**
Stage names.

**BILL** (laughs)
Jesus. You’re on a mission.

**JEREMY**
Crater must rise!

**BILL**
Then let the ballots fall.

(He raises his cup like a toast. Jeremy clinks it with his root beer.)

**JEREMY**
To band democracy.

**BILL**
To constitutional chaos.

(They drink. The screen door creaks again, but it’s not Kathy yet. Just the summer night breathing back.)

*Fade out with the sound of the fridge humming inside and someone—probably Gilley—arguing with a tuning pedal.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – MOMENTS LATER**

The door creaks again. **JIM** walks in from outside, shirt clinging to him, hair damp with sweat. He’s holding a half-empty bottle of Gatorade that’s lost the will to be cold. His drum key is still clipped to his back pocket like a sidearm.

**JIM**
Okay, I heard “ballots,” “Kathy as executioner,” and “Crater must rise.”
What fresh hell did I walk into?

**BILL**
Jeremy's been radicalized. We’re talking band democracy.

**JEREMY**
It’s time, Jim. Power to the people.

**JIM**
I *am* the people.

**JEREMY**
Not if we outvote you.

**JIM**
Oh good. So we’re not a band anymore, we’re a condo board with power chords.

**BILL**
He’s got a point. Democracy’s messy.

**JIM**
It’s a rock band, not the French Revolution. You start handing out ballots, next thing you know someone’s suggesting a referendum on hi-hat placement.

**JEREMY** (snapping fingers)
Ooo, good idea. I’ve always felt your left-side crash is a little dictatorial.

**JIM**
And your pedalboard looks like someone vomited RadioShack coupons.

**BILL**
This is going well.

**JIM** (sits on the nearest amp case)
Look. I get the appeal of voting. I do. Equal voices. Shared blame. Sounds noble.

**JEREMY**
Because it is.

**JIM**
But have you ever watched a band vote on setlist order? It’s like watching five cats try to draft a tax policy.

**BILL**
Gilley would filibuster with a tambourine solo.

**JIM**
Exactly. I'm not saying no votes ever. I'm saying—pick your battles. If it’s about *who we are*? That should come from the gut, not the ballot box.

**JEREMY**
But “Crater” *feels* like the gut.

**JIM**
Then write a campaign jingle. I’m still not running.

**BILL**
What if it’s not a vote? What if it’s… a *ceremony*?

**JIM**
God, no. There will be robes. I can feel it.

**JEREMY**
There will absolutely be robes.

**JIM**
No robes! No scrolls. No sacred fire. No animal bones. Just let me be Jim.

**BILL** (sipping his drink)
Still think Crater’s got legs.

**JIM**
If Crater shows up on one flyer, one poster, one bootleg cassette… I will personally overdub your guitar solos with kazoo.

**JEREMY**
You’d have to get to the master first.

**JIM**
I’ll bribe Gilley with frozen burritos and do it in his basement.

**BILL**
Gentlemen, please. The republic is young.

(The fan buzzes louder. Someone farts in the next room. Democracy lives, but barely.)

*Fade out with the glowing light of the porch, and three boys sitting in the heat, arguing over the birthright of stage names and the limits of governance.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – CONTINUOUS**

The heat hangs like a damp curtain.  **Jim**, **Jeremy**, and **Bill** are still lounging in various degrees of sprawl—Jim half-perched on a flight case, Jeremy stretched across a drum rug, Bill nursing the last inch of melted ice water.

From the edge of the garage light, **GILLEY** appears, coming up the porch steps. Shirtless. Flip-flops. Eating something that might be a slice of cold pizza folded like a taco. He walks straight past the garage without breaking stride.

**JEREMY**
Yo, Gilley—hold up.

**GILLEY** (with his mouth full)
Can’t. There’s an episode of *The A-Team* I haven’t finished not watching.

**BILL**
Just a sec. Real talk.

**GILLEY**
Dangerous phrase.

**JIM**
We’re thinking about how we wanna run the band. Like… operationally.

**GILLEY** (pause)
Operationally?

**JEREMY**
Voting. Roles. Maybe a constitution. We’re brainstorming.

**GILLEY** (grinning)
Oh yeah? You guys gonna have a little band parliament?

**BILL**
Could call it The House of Treble.

**GILLEY** (genuinely amused)
You nerds.

(He takes a slow bite of pizza and keeps walking.)

**JEREMY**
Wait—what do *you* think? Should we do votes? Maybe like, limited democracy?

**GILLEY** (still walking)
Nah, nah, nah.

**JIM**
Seriously?

**GILLEY**
No government. No voting. No rules. Just vibes and volume, baby.

(He slides the screen door open with his foot and disappears inside.)

**SCREEN DOOR**
*whap-SNAP.*

(Beat. Silence.)

**BILL**
I feel like we just got vetoed by a man holding pizza like a harmonica.

**JIM**
That’s not a veto. That’s abstention with style.

**JEREMY**
Band democracy just lost its swing vote.

**JIM**
Correction: Band democracy was just told to get a job.

(The fan hums. A distant laugh from inside. Gilley’s older brother yells something unintelligible.)

**BILL**
So… back to oligarchy?

**JIM**
Oligarchy in theory. Anarchy in practice.

**JEREMY**
Sounds like a band name.

**JIM**
We already have one.

**JEREMY**
For now.

(They all laugh. Or maybe groan. The fireflies blink. The republic sleeps.)

---

## **EXT. GILLEY’S PORCH – MOMENTS LATER – NIGHT**

The porch light casts a soft yellow cone over the cracked steps and warped floorboards. The fan in the garage buzzes. Someone inside the house laughs—but it's just the **TV**, not a person.

The screen door creaks open briefly, then bangs shut behind **GILLEY**.

A few moments later, **JEFF CREMEANS** appears at the end of the driveway, walking slow, shoulders slouched, shoes scuffing gravel. His T-shirt is damp from walking and *probably older than he is*. Bass strap imprint still faintly visible across his shoulder.

He trudges up the porch steps and drops onto the second one with a sigh.

**[[5.2. JEFF CREMEANS MODERN REVIEW|CREMEANS]]** (gruff, curious)
What’s going on?

From the garage, a voice drifts out:

**JEREMY (O.S.)**
Band democracy failed.

**BILL (O.S.)**
Jim resisted the will of the people.

**JIM (O.S.)**
I *am* the people.

**CREMEANS** (blinking)
…Okay.

He pulls a crumpled cigarette from his back pocket, then remembers he doesn’t smoke anymore, and tucks it behind his ear instead. Stares out at the fireflies.

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**
You guys figure out who’s in charge yet?

**JEREMY (O.S.)**
Yes. Gilley. By refusing power, he seized it.

**CREMEANS**
Yeah. That sounds about right.

(Beat.)

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**
You know he’s eating cold pizza and watching *Knight Rider* reruns, right?

**BILL (O.S.)**
It was *The A-Team.*

**CREMEANS**
Jesus. Even worse.

**JIM (O.S.)**
We tried to get him to vote on something. He said “nah” three times and vanished like a wizard.

Jeff grins. Leans back on his hands. Lets the night air settle.

**CREMEANS**
Your band is a mess.

**JIM (O.S.)**
Yeah, but we’re *our* mess.

**JEREMY (O.S.)**
You want a Mountain Dew?

**CREMEANS**
Only if it’s chilled and emotionally complicated.

**JEREMY (O.S.)**
You came to the right garage.

*Fade out with Jeff still on the porch step, the fireflies blinking like Morse code from another universe, and the laughter of Mr. T punching someone drifting faintly through the screen door.*

---

## **EXT. GILLEY’S PORCH – NIGHT – CONTINUOUS**

**JEFF EVANS** hasn’t moved from the second step. He’s leaning forward now, elbows on knees, eyes narrowed in that specific way that means he’s **about to intellectualize something that absolutely did not need it.**

From inside the garage, the others are still sprawled across amps and drum mats, the mood somewhere between summer-night mellow and **“please, no more conversation.”**

**[[4.3 JEFF EVANS character bible|JEFF]]** (earnest)
Look, if you’re talking about internal voting structures, I think it’s important to define the *type* of democracy you want.

**JEREMY (O.S.)**
Oh god.

**JEFF**
Are we talking about simple majority rule? Unanimity? Or maybe a council of rotating chairmen?

**BILL (O.S.)**
He’s doing it again.

**JIM (O.S.)**
Let him finish. He’s halfway to writing our constitution.

**JEFF**
I’m just saying: a band is a micro-state. You’ve got resources, leadership tensions, artistic direction—this is fertile ground for civic modeling.

**JEREMY (O.S.)**
He said *civic modeling*. I’m going to eat my own shoe.

**JEFF**
What if we instituted a bicameral structure? Like—instrumentalists on one side, vocalists on the other?

**JIM (O.S.)**
So now we’ve got a *House of Riffs* and a *Senate of Screaming?*

**JEFF**
Exactly. And we’ll need a judicial branch for gear disputes.

**BILL (O.S.)**
Can the judicial branch throw things?

**JEFF**
Only in the case of constitutional percussion.

(From inside the house, the TV blares: *“I ain’t gettin’ on no plane, Hannibal!”*)

**JEREMY (O.S.)**
I vote to dissolve the entire band and form a shadow government that only releases mixtapes.

**JIM (O.S.)**
I second that. Motion passed. Bill, light something on fire in celebration.

**BILL (O.S.)**
Already done.

(A faint *poof* and a hiss. Something smells like melted gaffer tape.)

**JEFF**
You’ll all regret mocking this when we’re arguing over merchandising rights and tour bus hierarchies.

**JIM (O.S.)**
When we get a tour bus, you can be *Secretary of the Interior.*

**JEFF**
I accept.

**JEREMY (O.S.)**
I want a cabinet post.

**JIM (O.S.)**
You can be Minister of Destruction.

**BILL (O.S.)**
I claim the Department of Vibes.

(Beat. The garage falls quiet again.)

**JEFF**
Band democracy. It begins tonight.

**JIM (O.S.)**
God help us all.

*Fade out on the glow of porch light, TV laugh track, and the sound of teenage government forming like mold in a basement.*

---

## **EXT. GILLEY’S PORCH – NIGHT – CONTINUOUS**

The air buzzes with fireflies, unresolved legislation, and **minor acts of arson**. Everyone’s either talked too much or not enough. **JIM** appears at the threshold of the garage, wiping his hands on a rag that used to be a T-shirt.

**JIM**
Alright. Truce for now. I’ve got beers in an ice chest in my trunk.

**JEREMY (perking up)**
Cold?

**JIM**
Colder than this democracy.

**JEREMY**
Let’s go.

**JIM**
But—Jeremy?

**JEREMY**
What?

**JIM**
You have to pretend it’s not beer.

**JEREMY**
I can lie. I lie all the time. I’ve been lying since rehearsal started.

**JEFF** (flatly, from the porch)
We’re *all* underage, Jim.

**JIM**
Then we’re all *pretending,* Jeff.

**JEREMY**
We’re drinking *root beer.* *Artisanal root beer.* From Oregon.

**BILL (O.S.)**
I heard it’s brewed in the same basement as the Constitution.

**JEFF**
And aged in barrels carved from the original Bill of Rights.

**JIM**
Perfect. Come on, Founding Fathers.

(He leads the way toward his rust-flecked hatchback, parked slightly crooked under the dying porchlight. The **ice chest clinks** faintly as he pops the trunk.)

**JEREMY**
Do we toast to the Republic?

**BILL**
We toast to the band.

**JEFF**
We toast to the fiction.

**JIM**
We toast to fireflies, fake IDs, and the fact that Kathy didn’t kill us.

(They each grab a beer—*root beer*, of course—and crack them open in near-unison.)

**JEREMY**
Gentlemen. To Commuted.

**ALL**
To Commuted.

(And for once—briefly—they’re not arguing, not roasting, not running from their own immaturity. Just **boys in the night**, surrounded by gravel, music gear, and a dream stupid enough to work.)

*Fade out on the hiss of cans, the flick of fireflies, and the quiet hum of destiny pacing itself.*

---

## **EXT. GILLEY’S DRIVEWAY – NIGHT – CONTINUOUS**

Four half-drunk cans of *“root beer”* glint in the open trunk light. The fireflies blink slower now. The night’s grown quieter—like the scene is shifting *down* a gear.  **JIM** is leaning against the car, beer in hand, squinting upward through the porch light glare.

**JIM**
Hey. Look.

(The others turn.)

**JIM (CONT’D)**
Gilley’s bedroom light just went out.

(Second-floor window: dark now. Still. No flicker of TV glow. No silhouetted chaos.)

**JEREMY**
That can’t be right. Gilley doesn’t sleep. Gilley just goes into low-power mode.

**BILL**
Nah. Gilley sleeps with his eyes open and his amp turned to three.

**JEFF**
Maybe he’s dreaming about Cold War weaponry and Totino’s pizza rolls again.

**JIM**
Or maybe he’s just gone. Like… gone-gone.

(Beat.)

**JIM (CONT’D)**
And Kathy’s not here either.

(They all look around instinctively, like she might just emerge from behind the garage with a critique and a coil of XLR cables.)

Nothing.

**BILL** (quietly)
They both ghosted us.

**JEFF**
Didn’t even say goodbye. Brutal.

**JEREMY**
Or strategic. They’re forming a counter-coup. Probably upstairs drafting the Espich-Gilley Alliance Treaty of 1990.

**JIM**
And it starts with locking the garage door from the inside.

(They all look at the garage door—still open, humming with the low buzz of a floor amp left on.)

**BILL**
We should probably pack the rest of this up before they declare martial law.

**JEFF**
Or before Gilley rewires the mics to only work with his harmonica input.

**JEREMY**
Or before Kathy returns and *names* us something worse than “Crater.”

**JIM** (quiet, half-smiling)
Is there worse than “Crater”?

(They don't answer. Not right away.)

The porch light flickers once, like it’s thinking about turning off too.  And then—just the sound of **gravel under sneakers** as the boys head back to work.

*Fade out on silhouettes in motion, the soft clack of metal gear, and one night deeper into the strange, formative chaos that would one day become Commuted.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – LATER – NIGHT**

The drums are packed. The cables are mostly coiled. **The worst of the mess is handled,** which means the boys are circling back to the one thing they *haven’t* solved: **each other**.

**BILL** sits cross-legged on the floor, leaning back against a bass amp. **JEFF** is fiddling with a snare clamp that didn’t need to be adjusted. **JEREMY** is holding a Sharpie like it’s a baton. **JIM** stands with arms crossed, the last can of *“root beer”* in hand.

**JEREMY**
Okay. So screaming doesn’t work.

**JEFF**
It’s fun. It’s emotionally honest.

**BILL**
It’s loud. Doesn’t solve shit.

**JIM** (quietly)
It *can’t* be how we run things. Not long-term. If this becomes a thing—if this actually *matters* someday—we’re gonna need something stronger than whoever yells last.

(Beat.)

**JEREMY**
So we vote?

**JEFF**
We already tried democracy. Got laughed out of our own garage.

**JIM**
Then we sharpen it. Set terms. Rules.

**BILL**
Like what?

**JIM**
Supermajority.

**JEFF**
Define it.

**JIM**
If we can get—what—four out of six?

**JEREMY**
That’s two-thirds.

**BILL**
That’s math. I like math.

**JEREMY**
So anything we want to change—setlist, name, money, tour decisions, anything major—we need four out of six members to say yes?

**JIM**
Yeah. That way nobody gets steamrolled, but nobody gets gridlocked either.

**JEFF**
And who counts as “six”? Gilley and Kathy?

**JIM**
Of course. If they show up, they vote.

**BILL**
If not?

**JIM**
Then it defaults to whoever’s present—but the rule still holds. Four votes minimum to pass anything big.

**JEFF**
No shouting. No mutiny. Just structure.

**JEREMY**
I like it.

**BILL**
You only like it because you think you can get four votes to name Jim “Crater.”

**JEREMY**
Not wrong.

**JIM**
But now I know your strategy. And I know the rules. Which means I can *win.*

(Beat. The room settles. Something real has just been constructed.)

**JEFF**
We’re a band with a supermajority clause.

**BILL**
That’s either noble… or hilarious.

**JEREMY**
Both.

**JIM**
That’s Commuted.

(They all look around the garage. It’s still a mess. But it’s *their* mess.)

*Fade out with the sound of a Sharpie scribbling something onto the back of a half-folded setlist—“SUPERMAJORITY = 4 of 6” underlined twice.*

---

## **EXT. GILLEY’S PORCH – LATE NIGHT – CONTINUOUS**

The supermajority clause has been drafted in Sharpie on a scrap of folded paper—“**SUPERMAJORITY = 4 of 6**”—and the boys have just finished debating it. The fireflies continue their silent dance in the humid, sticky Ohio night; the air is heavy with unresolved tension and the lingering taste of “root beer.”

As the conversation dies down, a sudden, soft noise cuts through the ambient hum of the garage and the distant murmur of an open TV inside the house.  A faint sound—like the low murmur of pleasure—drifts up from inside the Gilley residence. It is unmistakable: a sultry, unmistakable cadence that, despite the oppressive heat and chaos outside, carries with it all the familiar meaning of history repeated.

**JEREMY** (with a half-smile, half-grin)
You hear that?

**BILL**
That sound… It's like déjà vu on a loop.

**JEFF**
It always means one thing.

**JIM** (grinning softly, eyes narrowing)
It means someone’s *making love* inside. Again.

For a moment, they all fall silent. Their expressions—Jim’s contemplative, Jeremy’s cocky, Bill’s resigned, and Jeff’s amused—speak volumes: they all know exactly what this means. It’s a reminder of every time before, every time the boundaries between rebellion, desire, and band politics blurred into the ether of a hot summer night.

**JEREMY** (quietly, almost to himself)
The rhythm of the night… it calls.

**BILL**
Yeah. And sometimes, that rhythm comes from behind closed doors.

**JIM** (with a touch of pride and wistfulness)
It's our nightly affirmation—a reminder that in all this chaos, something real still *pulses*.

**JEFF**
Or maybe it’s just a reminder that the night belongs to everybody.

They exchange knowing glances. No one speaks further—no need. In that single, fleeting sound, their shared lives—full of anger, music, disagreement, and unexpected tenderness—resonate with the same honesty as any epic drum fill.  Slowly, the conversation shifts back to plans—gear, setlists, and the promise of tomorrow’s rehearsals. But for one shining moment, as the sound fades into the night, the boys remain united in their silent acknowledgment.

*Fade out on the porch, where the buzz of insects and the distant hum of voices blend with the pulse of the night—a subtle soundtrack marking another chapter in their unwritten, yet deeply felt, band democracy.*

---

## **EXT.  GILLEY’S DRIVEWAY – NIGHT – CONTINUOUS**

The Sharpie-scrawled supermajority clause rests on a drumhead. The boys are sprawled across the open garage and porch—tired, sticky, finished. **JIM** is still leaned up against the trunk, sipping the last of his not-beer.  **BILL** has claimed a cinderblock as a throne.  **JEFF** sits on the porch step, arms looped around his knees.  **JEREMY** is lying flat on the gravel, eyes at the stars.  Then… they hear it. Louder. Rhythmic. Undeniably **female**. A sound of passion.  It cuts through the summer hum like a needle through vinyl. All four of them go very still.

**JEREMY** (no emotion)
Naw.

**JIM**
Goddammit.

**BILL**
Seriously?

**JEFF**
We just established a parliamentary order.

**JIM**
The light was off. The house was quiet. I *thought we were safe.*

**JEREMY**
We should’ve known. Gilley ghosted. Kathy disappeared. It’s been, what—thirty minutes?

**BILL**
Plenty of time to light a candle and sin against God.

**JEFF**
Didn’t they call a truce last week?

**JIM**
They’ve called fifteen truces since Memorial Day. Every one ends with that sound.

(Another faint moan. Higher pitch. They all wince.)

**JEREMY**
Can we just go on record and say: *this is gross.*

**JIM**
Seconded.

**BILL**
Motion carries.

**JEFF**
Unanimous. Supermajority achieved. Our first real vote.

(They sit in silence. Another moan wafts through the night. Jeremy tosses a small rock toward the porch.)

**JEREMY**
You think they’re doing it in his *bed* or on his *floor*?

**BILL**
Don’t. Just—don’t.

**JIM**
Floor. Gilley doesn’t believe in sheets.

**JEFF**
Or emotional connections.

**JEREMY**
I swear to God, if they used my hoodie for a blanket again—

**JIM** (stands up)
I’m going home.

**BILL**
Yeah. Night’s over.

**JEFF**
Democracy survived. Morality didn’t.

**JEREMY**
That’s the real band motto.

They all begin moving, slowly gathering cables, bags, instruments. No urgency. Just **resigned teenage misery**. Behind them, the moaning continues—faint, regular, and impossibly awkward.

**JIM**
I’m never going to be able to hear Gilley’s bedroom door creak again without flashbacks.

**JEFF**
We’re gonna need trauma pay for this.

**BILL**
Or therapy discounts.

They finish packing in silence.

*Fade out on gravel crunching, fireflies blinking, and four young men profoundly wishing they had never learned what Kathy sounds like during sex.*

---

##  ## **EXT. GILLEY’S DRIVEWAY – NIGHT – IMMEDIATELY**

**JEFF** slams the van door shut a little harder than needed.  **JIM** drops the last cymbal bag with a grunt.  **BILL** wipes his hands on his shorts like he’s just performed field surgery.  **JEREMY** is still processing the sounds from upstairs with the expression of someone who’s been spiritually poisoned.

The night is too quiet now. And then—

**JIM** (flat, decisive)
Let’s fuckin’ go to Taco Bell.

**JEREMY**
Yes. Yes. Thank you. God. Yes.

**JEFF**
Something unholy happened here. I need a Crunchwrap to forget.

**BILL**
I need five. And a Baja Blast IV drip.

**JIM**
I’m not even hungry. I just need *distance*.

**JEREMY**
I need something greasy and radioactive and legally edible.

**JEFF**
We vote on this?

**JIM**
Supermajority. Lock it.

**BILL**
Unanimous.

**JEFF**
Where’s Gilley’s keys?

**JIM**
We’re not taking Gilley’s car. God knows what fluids are in there.

**JEREMY**
…Don’t say fluids.

**JIM**
Sorry.

They pile into **Jim’s hatchback**, shoving gear aside, stepping on cables, making space between amps and snare cases. The trunk doesn’t fully latch. Jeremy calls shotgun and no one fights him. As the car pulls out of the driveway, someone—probably Bill—yells out the window:

**BILL**
Have fun with your sweat communion, sinners!

From the second floor: **nothing**.

Just the blink of the porch light and a humid summer night that now smells faintly of regret and ambition. The hatchback peels out. Gravel sprays.  The road ahead is dark and sticky.  The Bell beckons.

**FADE OUT on four boys chasing salvation in 1,200 calories or less.**

---

# **CHAPTER TWO: WRITTEN IN STARLIGHT**

---

## **INT. TACO BELL – UPPER VALLEY MALL – 1:04 A.M.**

The dining room is fluorescent, half-cleaned, and utterly devoid of other patrons. A **“Caution: Wet Floor”** sign leans against the pop machine like it gave up halfway through its shift.

The boys occupy a booth in the back—**a graveyard of wrappers and half-drained Mountain Dews**. All four look sunburnt by fluorescent light and spiritually scuffed from the last three hours.

**JEREMY** is chewing on something he can’t identify. **BILL** is deconstructing a quesadilla like it wronged him. **JEFF** is sipping from a straw with dead eyes. **JIM** is just staring into the void, full of Crunchwrap and fury.

**BILL** (quietly, with the tone of a man who’s seen things)
It’s unprofessional.

**JIM**
It’s worse than that. It’s *stupid.*

**JEFF**
It’s performative chaos. They do it so we’ll know. Like… *we’re supposed to hear it.*

**JEREMY**
It’s punk.

**JIM**
It’s *not* punk. It’s lazy boundary violations wrapped in a flannel blanket of narcissism.

**BILL**
I’d be okay with it if they at least *left the house.*

**JEFF**
You’re not supposed to do foreplay within earshot of your bass amp.

**JEREMY**
You think they did it on the amp?

**JIM**
Don’t finish that sentence.

**BILL**
Gilley’s never washed that amp. It smells like low voltage and Axe body spray.

(Beat. They all visibly recoil.)

**JIM**
Okay. Real talk. Just so it’s on record: I am adamantly, *absolutely* against having sex with anyone in this band.

**JEFF**
Clarity noted.

**BILL**
Seconded.

**JEREMY**
Define “in this band.” Like full-time? Touring members?

**JIM**
Shut the fuck up, Jeremy.

**JEREMY**
Just asking. For legal purposes.

**BILL**
I mean… What even are they? Gilley and Kathy? It’s like a war that occasionally devolves into Frenching.

**JEFF**
It’s 1970’s-era NATO diplomacy.  *Kiss, fight, ghost, repeat.*

**JIM**
It compromises the work. The vibe. The process. I shouldn’t have to tune my snare while someone’s moaning in the next room like it’s a Cinemax audition.

**BILL**
Gilley once asked me to adjust his overhead mics while Kathy was still putting her shirt back on.

**JEFF**
*That’s* the line.

**JEREMY**
It was already crossed. Then burned. Then danced on.

(Beat. The room hums. A fryer spits behind the counter.)

**JIM**
We need rules. Or protocols. Or like… abstinence clauses.

**JEFF**
Asexual non-fraternization doctrine?

**BILL**
We write it up, put it next to the supermajority clause.

**JEREMY**
Let’s call it the “*Don’t Screw Your Rhythm Guitarist Act of 1990*.”

**JIM**
I don’t care what it’s called. I just want one place in this band where people *aren’t* inserting themselves into each other mid-soundcheck.

**BILL**
Let’s go full Vatican on it. Papal doctrine: No sex among the six.

**JEFF**
Band celibacy until contract.

**JIM**
Until *death.*

(Beat.)

**JEREMY**
If I start dating someone in a different band, do I have to disclose it to the committee?

**JIM**
You will submit a fucking notarized form.

**BILL**
With witnesses.

**JEFF**
And blood type.

(They raise their cups. Baja Blasts, warm and bubbly.)

**ALL FOUR**
To discipline.

(They drink. The ice machine groans. Somewhere in the distance, Kathy and Gilley are probably doing it again.)

**JIM**
*God help us when we tour.*

*FADE OUT on the glow of neon, the smell of seasoned beef, and four young men grasping for order in a band they’re not entirely sure is real yet.*

---

## **INT. TACO BELL – UPPER VALLEY MALL – 1:37 A.M.**

The place is dead quiet. Just a mop bucket, a half-lit menu board, and the low hum of fluorescent lights. The four boys have claimed the farthest booth, surrounded by the wreckage of Crunchwraps, quesadillas, and two mostly-empty Mountain Dew cups that are sweating like they just lost a fight.

**JIM** leans forward on his elbows. Still wired. Still agitated.

**JIM**
I’m saying it for the record, so there’s no confusion: I won’t sleep with bandmates. Period.

**JEREMY**
You said that already.

**BILL**
Twice.

**JEFF** (frowning)
And now he’s legislating it.

**JIM**
I’m not joking. No hookups. No crushes. No weird subtext that gets people kicked out or stops the song halfway through a bridge. I don’t care if it’s five years from now and we’re famous—I’m not doing it.

**JEREMY** (raising an eyebrow)
You mean… you’re not doing *Kathy*.

Jim pauses. Long enough for everyone to feel it.

**JEFF**
Let’s not pretend this is a blanket rule. There’s only one girl in the band. This isn’t a general policy. This is… *you don’t want to sleep with Kathy*.

**JIM** (tight)
It’s not about her.

**JEFF**
But it kind of is.

**BILL**
And she’s not even here to weigh in.

**JIM**
She doesn’t have to. I’ve made up my mind.

**JEREMY**
Why? Because of Gilley?

**JIM**
Because it’s chaotic. Every time they hook up, practice dies. Focus dies. We’re tuning guitars while someone’s moaning in the hallway. That’s not music. That’s amateur hour.

**BILL**
He’s not wrong.

**JEFF**
Still doesn’t answer the question.

**JIM**
What question?

**JEREMY**
Do you *want* to sleep with her, but you won’t?

**JIM** (beat)
Doesn’t matter.

**JEFF**
Of course it does.

**JIM**
No. What matters is that I don’t. That’s the boundary. That’s the line.

**BILL**
You think Gilley crossed it?

**JIM**
Repeatedly. With no brakes.  And now that line’s got tire marks and someone’s bra tangled in the guitar stands.

**JEREMY**
Could’ve been anyone’s bra.

**JEFF**
Only if someone else here shops at the Limited.

(Beat.)

**JIM**
I don’t want this band to blow up because someone couldn’t keep it in their pants. This thing we’ve got—it’s fragile. We’re good. We’re *almost* something. One wrong move and we’re a memory with receipts.

**BILL**
So what do we do?

**JIM**
We don’t screw it up.

**JEREMY**
Literally.

**JEFF**
Got it. Abstinence clause. Supermajority to override?

**BILL**
No override. Carved in stone. Jim’s Law.

**JIM**
Good.

(Beat.)

**JEFF**
You know Kathy’s gonna find out you said this, right?

**JEREMY**
And she’s gonna light your kit on fire.

**JIM**
Then I’ll start over. But at least I’ll have my principles.

**BILL**
And a melted hi-hat.

(They all raise their drinks. Sticky. Warm. Gross.)

**ALL FOUR**
To professionalism.

(They drink. Outside, the parking lot is empty. The night hums with the weight of knowing *what not to do*, even if it doesn’t yet tell them *what to become.*)

---

## **INT. TACO BELL – UPPER VALLEY MALL – LATE NIGHT – CONTINUOUS**

They’ve just finished one of the rare moments of adolescent self-governance: sober, mature, heartfelt. For about eight seconds. **JIM** has laid down the law. **BILL** has nodded solemnly. **JEFF** is sipping from his straw, quiet but present.

Then—

**JEREMY** (out of nowhere, casual as napkin lint)
Jeff, you wanna bone Kathy, don’t you?

**JEFF** (chokes on his drink)
What the fuck.

**JIM** (laughing)
Oh *my God.*

**BILL** (palms face)
Democracy was fun while it lasted.

**JEFF**
Jeremy, I swear to Christ, I will smother you with a Chalupa wrapper.

**JEREMY**
I’m just saying, you’ve been *awfully quiet* during all this principled moralizing.

**JEFF**
Because I don’t need to broadcast my entire sexual decision matrix over nachos.

**JIM** (laughing harder)
“Decision matrix.” You *are* into her.

**JEFF**
I’m into my quesadilla. That’s it.

**BILL**
Nope. Too late. The defense rests. The brother knows.

**JEFF**
You’re all idiots.

(stern)
And *no,* I don’t “want to bone Kathy.”

**JEREMY**
You just wanna sit next to her during setlist meetings and smell her shampoo.

**JEFF** (still deadpan)
It’s coconut. And that’s between me and God.

**JIM**
Unbelievable. The abstinence clause *just passed* and we’re already violating the spirit of it.

**JEFF**
*I* am not violating anything.  Jeremy’s just trying to deflect from the fact that he’s still in love with that barista from the Kmart snack bar.

**JEREMY**
Shelby was special. She knew how to make a Coke Icee with precision.

**BILL**
She also had a mustache.

**JEREMY**
*You’re jealous.*

(Beat.)

**JIM**
Okay, okay. Let’s reset.

**JEFF**
Please.

**JIM**
Nobody’s boning Kathy.

**BILL**
Nobody’s boning anyone in this band.

**JEREMY**
Especially not Jeff.

**JEFF**
Jeremy, I’m going to write a diss track about you and perform it live at your wedding.

**JEREMY**
Then I’ll dedicate my vows to Kathy just to mess with you.

(Everyone groans.)

**JIM**
Can we go home before this becomes legally binding?

*Fade out on four boys laughing too hard, too tired, too stupid to realize they’re about to remember all of this forever.*

---

## **INT. TACO BELL – UPPER VALLEY MALL – STILL TOO DAMN LATE**

The fluorescent buzz hums louder as if it, too, is judging them.

**JEREMY** has just lobbed the grenade.  **JEFF** is still red in the face.  **JIM** is trying very hard not to enjoy this.  **BILL** is halfway through peeling the label off his cup in perfect spirals.

**JEFF** (firmly)
I’m not gonna limit myself, alright?

**JIM** (leans in, grinning)
*You do want to bone her.*

**JEFF**
I didn’t say that.

**JIM**
You didn’t have to.

(mocking)
“I refuse to limit myself.” Jesus, Jeff. That’s like the horniest sentence ever written in the English language.

**JEREMY** (laughing)
You sound like a guy trying to get tenure at Hustler University.

**JEFF**
I’m saying I’m not locking the door on anything. Philosophically.

**JIM**
You *do* want to bone her. You *do*. Just say it. Get it out of your system. We’ll all feel better.

**JEFF** (flat)
I want her to respect me. That’s it.

**JEREMY**
Respect you… shirtless?

**JEFF**
You’re going to die in this Taco Bell, Jeremy.

**BILL**
From what, awkwardness or blunt force trauma?

**JEFF**
Whichever comes first.

**JIM**
Dude. Look me in the eye and tell me you don’t ever think about her—y’know—*Kathy-style.*

**JEFF** (guilty)
I think about what it would be like to play bass and not have the hi-hat fall over because she kicked the cymbal stand mid-argument.

**JEREMY**
Deflection. Classic.

**JEFF** (sighs)
I’m just saying… I admire her. A lot. She’s smart. She’s talented. She’s tougher than all of us. She’s… a mess. And yeah, that mess? It’s magnetic sometimes.

**JIM**
There it is.

**JEFF**
But I also know it’s dangerous. So no, I’m not trying to bone her.

**JIM** (softly, with a grin)
But you *would.*

**JEFF**
Only if she asked really nicely.

**JEREMY**
And probably even if she didn’t.

**BILL**
I’m putting “Jeff wants Kathy to ask nicely” in the minutes.

**JIM**
Make it an amendment to the Abstinence Clause.

**JEFF**
Shut up and pass the hot sauce.

(They pass it. Silently. Respectfully. Like a ceasefire.)

*Fade out with Jeff silently cursing the invention of language, Jeremy beaming, Bill scribbling fake laws on a napkin, and Jim quietly basking in the knowledge that he’s finally gotten Jeff to crack.*

---

## **INT. TACO BELL – UPPER VALLEY MALL – WINDING DOWN**

The garbage has been gathered into one giant burrito wrapper tomb. Jeff’s cooled off. Jim’s still smug. Bill has finally stopped peeling his cup. Jeremy leans back in the booth, arms folded behind his head, **full of too much sodium and a sliver of wisdom.**

**JEREMY**
Okay, real talk for a second.

**JIM**
God, no.

**JEREMY**
Hear me out. I think…

(beat)
We should try talking to them.

**JEFF**
Who’s “them”?

**JEREMY**
Kathy and Gilley. Before next practice.

**BILL**
That’s ambitious.

**JEREMY**
I’m serious. We talk to them. Like, actual words. No yelling. No drumsticks thrown at heads. No door slamming, no stalking each other across the yard like it’s a horror movie.

**JIM**
So we schedule a summit?

**JEFF**
Like Camp David, but with more distortion and fewer functioning boundaries.

**JEREMY**
Exactly. Just… lay it out. Say what we need from them. Ask what they need from us. Try to… *de-escalate* before we end up rehearsing in a murder scene.

**BILL**
So instead of cold wars and occasional screaming sex intermissions, we get… like, civility?

**JIM**
You’re forgetting one thing.

**JEREMY**
What?

**JIM**
They’re *Kathy* and *Gilley.*

**JEFF**
We’d have better luck negotiating a ceasefire between possum in a dumpster.

**JEREMY**
Still. We’re a band. Or we’re supposed to be. And we can’t keep writing songs around their meltdowns. It’s exhausting.

(Beat.)

**BILL**
I’ll support it. But I want it in writing that if they start throwing things again, I get to hide behind the bass cab.

**JIM**
I’ll support it as long as nobody calls it an “intervention.” Gilley hears that word and he starts swinging.

**JEFF**
Let’s just… approach it as a band check-in. Casual. Light. Political in nature, but informal in tone.

**JEREMY**
Band democracy. Chapter Two.

**JIM**
God help us.

**JEREMY**
If it works, we save the band.

**JEFF**
If it doesn’t?

**JIM**
We go back to fire axes.

**BILL**
Better pack a helmet.

*They rise. Trash is dumped. Cups are tossed. The door chimes as they step into the humid black of the parking lot, each carrying the weight of potential peace in a band that was born from noise.*

**FADE OUT.**
A plan has been formed. A summit awaits.  Chaos, for the first time in weeks, is on notice.

---

## **EXT. GILLEY’S DRIVEWAY – 4:45 A.M. – JUST BEFORE DAWN**

The sky is still dark, but it’s **thinning at the edges**—that gray-pink smear that comes before birds remember they exist. The house is silent. The porch light flickers once, then gives up.

**KATHY** stumbles across the gravel in heavy boots, still wearing her **jeans, band tee, and long-sleeve flannel**, now damp with sweat, sleep, and shame. Her keys jangle like accusations in her hand. She **doesn’t slam the car door**—but she closes it with the weight of someone trying to **punish themselves quietly**.

### **INT.KATHY’S CAR – MOMENTS LATER**

She turns the key. The engine coughs. The dashboard light flares up like a hungover eye. The air inside the car is stale and unforgiving. She sits still for a second, hands on the wheel, staring at her own reflection in the rearview mirror.

Then—

**KATHY** (low, to herself)
God. Fucking. Dammit.

She pounds the wheel once—not rage, not drama. **Self-directed disgust.**

### **EXT.US-40 – EASTBOUND – CONTINUOUS**

The car merges onto the empty two-lane road. The road stretches ahead, **straight and endless**, like a belt of regret laid flat across the state. She doesn't put on music. She doesn't crack the window.  She drives. Face set. Eyes hot. **Jaw locked with disappointment.** Every streetlight she passes makes her look a little more **like someone realizing too late that she gave too much away**—again.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
You said you wouldn’t do it again.  You said it last time. You fucking *promised* yourself.

Another mile. Another sigh. Her fingers tap the steering wheel in irregular, agitated bursts.
She knows they know.  And she knows they *heard.*  And that’s the part that stings. She drives east, chasing a sun she’s not ready to see.

The band’s about to shift.  And so is she.

### **EXT.US-40 – APPROACHING DOWNTOWN DONNELSVILLE – 4:53 A.M.**

The sky is lightening just enough to reveal the outline of **the auction house, telephone wires, and two-story homes slumped into themselves like old men**. The road slopes gently **downhill** into **downtown Donnelsville**—if “downtown” is the right word for a street with more ghosts than businesses.

### **INT.KATHY’S CAR – CONTINUOUS**

The **yellow blinking light** suspended above the intersection glows like a tired eye. Kathy eases off the gas. She doesn’t speed in Donnelsville. Nobody does. Not unless they want to end up in the backseat of a Crown Vic with a **lecture about small-town decency and radar guns hidden behind grain trucks.**

**She taps the brakes. Checks the speedometer.** **35. On the dot.** Her jaw flexes.  Her eyes burn.

**KATHY (muttering)**
Goddamn place hasn’t changed in twelve years. Neither have I.

She passes the **old elementary school**, red-bricked and proud, the year **“1928”** still etched over the lintel like it matters. One light is on inside. Probably the janitor. Or a ghost.

Up ahead, the **Evans residence**. Second story porch. Flowers in the yard. Jeff and Jeremy, sleeping through the aftermath. She **does not honk.** Not because she’s polite, but because **she doesn’t want to start something she’d have to finish.**  The **fire station** looms on the left—metal doors down, the radio tower blinking red. A single SUV in the lot. Volunteer hours.

She clears the last mailbox, crosses the painted “SPEED LIMIT 35” line on the pavement, and **exits the village.**

Back to 55.  Back to the middle of nowhere. She floors it.  Not because she’s late.  Because she’s tired of *feeling* anything.

### **INT.KATHY’S CAR – CONTINUOUS**

The yellow line blurs. The sun isn’t up yet.  And she still hasn’t forgiven herself.

### **EXT.KATHY’S MOM’S HOUSE – 5:00 A.M. – JUST EAST OF DONNELSVILLE**

A tired split-level, porch light still on, **white paint curling** off the siding. One plastic lawn chair on the stoop, flipped by last week’s storm and never righted.  Kathy pulls into the **gravel side lot**, kills the engine, and just sits for a second—sweat cooling under her flannel, stomach sour from shame and sugar.

No one is awake.

### **INT.BASEMENT – MINUTES LATER**

She creeps through the back door, down the narrow steps. The basement smells like **concrete, laundry detergent, and old books**. Half the lightbulbs are out.

She doesn’t care.

Kathy tosses her bag down. Pulls off the flannel, throws it across a broken weight bench. Pulls a spiral notebook out of her backpack like she’s drawing a weapon.  **Sits.** **Slams the pen to paper.** She doesn’t write lyrics.  She **scrawls them.**  She carves them.  All-caps. Crossed-out phrases. Half-sentences that sound like accusations.

I SAW YOU
AGAIN
I LET YOU
AGAIN
YOU TAKE AND
YOU TALK AND
YOU TASTE LIKE
REGRET

The ink is smudged where her palm dragged through a verse. One page crumples under her grip. Another tears at the spine. She doesn’t pause. Doesn’t edit.  This isn’t for **structure.**  It’s for **release.** Thirty minutes. Forty-five. An hour. When the sun’s coming up and the basement window starts to glow pink—She stops. Looks down.

And all she sees is **rage spaghetti.** **Unreadable. Unusable. Raw. Ugly.** She flips back through the pages.  Her throat tightens.

**KATHY** (quiet, bitter)
It’s all shit.

She closes the notebook. Hugs it to her chest for a second. Then tosses it across the room. It hits a stack of milk crates. Doesn’t fall. She leans back in the chair, eyes on the ceiling, lungs full of concrete air, and mind full of **nothing but fire and noise**.

---

## **INT. KATHY’S BASEMENT – 7:12 A.M. – SHORTLY AFTER SUNRISE**

The sun pushes a dull amber glow through the high basement window. Kathy didn’t sleep. She’s on her second bowl of dry cereal, spoon clinking loudly in the quiet. The spiral notebook sits on the table again. She hasn’t picked the pen back up.  She just keeps staring at the pages like they insulted her mother.

Eventually, she exhales. Long and low. Like she’s letting go of the idea that this was going to work *alone.*

**KATHY** (flat, to herself)
I’m not the best writer.

She stares a little longer.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
And Gilley won’t. Jim won’t. Bill doesn’t have time.  Gilley *might*… but he won’t sit still long enough to finish a stanza.

She spins the spoon in the bowl. Slowly.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
*Jeff*.

The name lands in the room like a dropped amp cord. She hates how right it sounds.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
That motherfucker can write.

She flips to a fresh page in the notebook. Scribbles a header: **LYRIC ROOM – IDEA FRAMEWORK?**

Then underneath:

* Let Jeff write first draft
* Group reviews together
* Sit around table
* No phones
* No ego
* One rule: “yes, and…”
* Build, not burn

She chews her lip.  Wipes cereal dust from the corner of her mouth.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Maybe we don’t write lyrics like poets. Maybe we write them like scenes. Like fights. Like we’re all in it.

She underlines:  **PLUSSING UP**. Then circles it three times.  She leans back in the chair. Stares at the ceiling.  Eyes red, mind sharp.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
We don’t need a genius.  We need a table.

*FADE OUT on Kathy closing the notebook—not angry anymore, not inspired exactly, but focused.*  It’s no longer about what she has to say. It’s about **what they can say together.**

---

## **INT. KATHY’S BEDROOM – 7:36 A.M. – MOMENTS LATER**

The spiral notebook now rests on the edge of her desk, closed but **anchored with intention**. The ideas are there. They’re not perfect, but they’re **alive**.  Kathy shuffles upstairs like she’s walking underwater.  Her boots are still on. Her flannel’s stuck to her back.  The **jeans she’s been wearing for nearly 24 hours** feel like denim glue.  She doesn’t care.

She pushes open the bedroom door. The bed is a **bare mattress with a sheet twisted in the corner** and a fan on the dresser that oscillates like it’s sighing for her. She drops onto the mattress face-first. Doesn’t kick off her boots. Doesn’t peel off her socks.
Doesn’t even flip the light off. Just collapses. Her last conscious thought is barely a flicker:

**KATHY (V.O.)**
*Get them to the table. Just once. Just once.*

Then—Gone.

*FADE OUT on Kathy, fully clothed, dirt under her nails, lyrics under her skin, passed out in the summer heat of a girl trying to make the next day better than the last.*

---

## **INT. BILL’S BASEMENT – MORNING – SAME DAY**

A low-ceilinged basement. Carpet that’s seen better decades. Posters half-taped to cinderblock walls. **An old Casio keyboard sits next to a disassembled amp**, and a cold mug of something that was coffee four hours ago.  **BILL** is seated on the floor, cross-legged, working on a synth patch. Wires everywhere.  **JEFF** paces in front of him with the energy of a man who’s had too much Mountain Dew and not enough sleep.

**JEFF**
Okay, okay, hear me out—*primitive Americana grunge*.

**BILL** (half-listening)
That sounds like a thrift store trying to do flannel-themed barbecues.

**JEFF**
Exactly. It’s texture. It’s fuzz. It’s broken rhythm. But it’s also **banjos, field recordings, old hymns**—like if Neil Young had grown up in a meth trailer with a distortion pedal.

**BILL**
…And this is a good thing?

**JEFF**
This is *the thing*. It’s like—we take what Nirvana’s gonna do, right? That full-chest howl from under a blanket of rot. But then we back it with sounds that feel **pre-electric.** Wood. Steel. Dirt. Grain elevators. Trains.

**BILL**
Okay, now you sound like Springsteen had a nervous breakdown and started hanging out with Sonic Youth.

**JEFF**
Yes. Good. Keep going.

**BILL**
You want me to say more insane things until you build an album around them?

**JEFF**
Exactly. You’re catching on.

(Bill sits back. Thinks. Eyes Jeff warily.)

**BILL**
Okay. Primitive Americana Grunge.

So…

* Dirt under the nails
* Guitars with too much buzz
* Stories about cornfields and uncles in jail
* Distorted hymns
* Tape hiss left in on purpose
* Songs that sound like a car engine refusing to start
* Drums that hit like a shovel in a barn fight

**JEFF**
Yes. *Yes*. Now add some harmonies that sound like they were recorded in a church kitchen at 3 a.m. during a thunderstorm.

**BILL**
Do we sample the thunder?

**JEFF**
Only if we record it ourselves. On a boombox.

**BILL**
You know, you’re dangerously close to inventing a whole new genre.

**JEFF**
That’s the goal.

**BILL**
And you're just gonna call it “primitive Americana grunge”?

**JEFF**
Until we find something worse.

(Beat.)

**BILL**
I kind of love it.

**JEFF**
Same.

**BILL**
We should write that down before we forget.

**JEFF**
Too late. It’s already part of the lore.

---

## **INT. BILL’S BASEMENT – CONTINUOUS**

Jeff is still lit up with *primitive Americana grunge* visions, practically vibrating. Bill taps a key on his synth—**low, warbling, analog as hell**—and leans back like a man about to drop a quiet prophecy.

**BILL**
Look. We’re aware the synthesizer’s coming in.

**JEFF**
It’s already here.

**BILL**
Yeah, but I mean *culturally*. It's gonna hit differently soon. It's not just New Order and soundtrack guys anymore. It’s about to get weirder. **Hotter. Dirtier. More real.**

**JEFF**
That’s why we *have* to drag it into the barn with us. Give it blisters. Let it sweat. No more synths that sound like spaceships. I want synths that sound like **divorce.**

**BILL**
Or *crop failure.*

**JEFF**
Exactly!

**BILL**
You ever hear a Juno-60 get run through a busted tape deck?

**JEFF**
Only in my dreams.

**BILL**
It sounds like God trying to send a radio signal from under a collapsed porch.

**JEFF**
That’s the sound I want. That’s what goes under the guitar. Not over it. Not instead of it. *Under.*

**BILL**
The roots. The rot. The reverb.

**JEFF**
That’s it. That’s the album.

**BILL**
Primitive Americana Grunge. Synths and snare drums. Praise and feedback.

**JEFF**
We’re gonna scare the shit out of Dayton.

**BILL**
Good.

*They look at the Casio like it’s a weapon that hasn’t been fully unsheathed yet.*

*Fade out on Bill flicking a modulation slider and smiling like he knows exactly where the future is hiding.*

---

## **INT. BILL’S BASEMENT – CONTINUOUS**

The synth lets out a ghost of a chord—*grainy, unstable, weirdly human*. Jeff raises an eyebrow.

**JEFF**
Wait…You’re not thinking like… *what Sammy Hagar did*, are you?

**BILL** (tilts his head)
Not exactly.

He flips a switch on the board, dials back a low-frequency oscillation, and lays down a **texture**—not a lead, not a riff, just a **bed of noise** that hums like wind through rusted aluminum.

**BILL (CONT’D)**
I’m not trying to *dominate* anything. This isn’t “*Jump*.”

**JEFF**
Good. Because that song’s basically a keyboard wearing sunglasses and punching you in the face.

**BILL**
Exactly. I want the synth to be like… background radiation.  You don’t hear it first.  But if it’s gone, everything falls flat.

**JEFF**
*Atmosphere*, not attention.

**BILL**
Like mood lighting for a funeral. Or duct tape holding the melody together from behind.

**JEFF**
God, yes. And if anyone ever asks you if it’s “like Van Halen,” I give you full permission to sneer and walk away.

**BILL**
Politely. But firmly.

They both nod. Agreement reached.  No “*Jump*.” No pop sheen. No **keyboard solos in spandex**. Just **grit**, **weirdness**, and **intentional restraint**.

*Fade out with Bill twisting a knob and making the air around them wobble like a haunted porch beam.*

---

## **INT. BILL’S BASEMENT – CONTINUOUS**

The synth buzz fades into silence. A moment of stillness. Bill sits back on his heels, **arms folded**, expression unreadable.

**BILL** (flat)
I’m better than everybody else.

**JEFF** (blinks)
Excuse me?

**BILL**
I am. You know it. I know it. And I’m gonna throw **everything** at this project.

**JEFF**
Define “everything.”

**BILL**
You name it. If I can get away with it, it’s going in.

**JEFF**
You’re not making sense.

**BILL**
Xylophone.

**JEFF**
What?

**BILL**
Banjo.

**JEFF**
Stop.

**BILL**
Piano!

**JEFF**
Bill.

**BILL**
If we need a really, *really* thick sound, I’ll play guitar too.

**JEFF**
You already play keys.

**BILL**
So? We stack. We layer. You’re on bass. Jeremy’s lead. We throw Gilley in there, Kathy too. And me.

(He stands now, pacing—wires tug at his ankle like vines.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
**Five guitars.** All screaming. Or whispering. Or droning. Whatever we want.  Five completely different voices. Five textures. Five moods.

**JEFF**
You’re not trying to write an album. You’re trying to **overwhelm a recording console.**

**BILL**
We work on **levels.**  We have songs that sound like bonfires.  Songs that sound like industrial accidents.  Songs that sound like *religious revelations happening during a blackout.*

**JEFF**
You’re gonna make the sound guy quit.

---

## **INT. BILL’S BASEMENT – CONTINUOUS**

Jeff is still processing the concept of **five guitars, a banjo, and a xylophone** when Bill turns back to his synth, calmly dialing in another patch.

**BILL** (flat)
I *am* the sound guy.

(Beat.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
So no. I’m not gonna quit.

**JEFF** (quiet)
Goddammit.

**BILL**
I’ve already got routing diagrams. If it fits in a quarter-inch jack, I can mix it. Hell, if it *doesn’t* fit, I’ll rewire it until it does.

**JEFF**
So there’s no one to stop you.

**BILL**
Correct. You’re catching on.

(Beat.)

**JEFF**
What happens if it sounds like garbage?

**BILL**
Then I’ll EQ the garbage until it sounds like *art.*

(They stare at each other.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
Welcome to the future, Jeff.  Bring your bass. Bring your words.  We’re making **something people have to survive.**

*Fade out with the soft, rising drone of a synth note stretching out like a power line over an open field—buzzing, imperfect, and undeniable.*

---

## **INT. KATHY’S BEDROOM – 1:13 P.M. – SAME DAY**

**KATHY** wakes with a start—**mouth dry, throat sticky, pillow soaked in drool**. Her cheek peels off the case with a sickening *fwap*. **The fan overhead spins lazily**, blowing warm air over a scene of **absolute textile carnage**. She’s still fully dressed.  **Jeans twisted. Flannel bunched into her armpit. Band tee welded to her back with old sweat.**

She shifts. **Winces.** The **underwire of her bra is trying to puncture her lung.**

**KATHY**  (gravel-voiced)
…fuck me sideways.

She swings her legs over the side of the bed—**boots still on**, socks halfway off, one inside-out. She stinks. Like **sleep, stress, and last night’s leftovers filtered through a denim refinery.   She squints toward the window. **Full sun. Too high. Too bright.**
Her eyes dart to the **red LED digits** on the **alarm clock across the room**—one of those fake woodgrain boxes that hums faintly in the silence.

**1:13**

She freezes.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
No no no no no.

**Practice started at 1.** She lurches to her feet, kicks off one boot, stumbles over the other, tries to yank her shirt off and gets tangled halfway. Rips it off over her head.  Tries to pull off the bra. Gives up.  No time for a shower.  No time for self-respect.

She grabs:
* **A hoodie from the floor. Probably Gilley’s. Doesn’t care.**
* **A pair of mostly-clean socks**
* **Her lyric notebook, covered in cereal dust**
* **A ponytail holder from a drawer full of guitar picks and battery acid**

She bursts out of her room, slapping the wall light switch without hitting it, and barrels down the hallway like she’s fleeing a hostage situation.

---
### **INT.KITCHEN – CONTINUOUS**

Her mom isn’t home. The **microwave clock confirms it: 1:14.**  The **rotary phone** on the wall just hangs there—silent, smug, and completely useless.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Should’ve burned that thing in ‘87.

She shoves her feet into mismatched boots, grabs her keys from the counter, and **books it out the door**, hoodie half on, arms flailing.

*FADE OUT on Kathy’s car peeling out of the driveway with gravel spitting behind it, driver’s window down, hair flying, and the unmistakable look of a woman who is **absolutely going to yell at someone today.***

---

### **EXT.U.S. 40 WESTBOUND – 1:21 P.M. – EN ROUTE TO DONNELSVILLE**

**KATHY’S CAR** is a streak of steel and rage—windows down, engine roaring, **dust kicking up behind her in long, angry contrails**. The speedometer needle flirts with **70 MPH**, and Kathy is leaning forward, **teeth clenched, sunglasses on crooked**, one hand on the wheel and the other death-gripping the gearshift.

### **INT.KATHY’S CAR – CONTINUOUS**

**Hair whipping into her mouth**, hoodie half-zipped, she’s muttering under her breath at every slow-moving truck and reflective road sign.

**KATHY**
I *swear* to God if anyone says a single thing about punctuality I will scream in seven keys.

The flat fields blur past her. Mailboxes. Silos. A sun-faded “Jesus Saves” billboard. Up ahead: the **green sign for Donnelsville**, and right behind it, the known-to-all **SPEED LIMIT 35** post and the dreaded **yellow blinking light**.

Kathy lifts her foot off the gas.

### **INT.SPEEDOMETER – CLOSE-UP**

The needle eases down.  **60. 50. 42. 36… 35.** On the dot. She’s seething, but not reckless.

### **EXT.DONNELSVILLE – CONTINUOUS**

She rolls into town like a slow-motion explosion. Passes the **elementary school**, the **Evans residence**, the **fire station**, all at a flawless 35 MPH—**chin lifted, hands at 10 and 2**, as if daring a cop to say something.

No one’s out. Just a sleepy village and one very punctual act of rage control. As soon as she clears the last white mailbox past the edge of town—

**VROOOOOOOM.**

She floors it. The tires grab gravel.  The engine howls.  She’s gone.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
If I’m gonna be late, I’m gonna be legendary.

---

## **EXT. GILLEY RESIDENCE – DRIVEWAY – 1:26 P.M.**

**KATHY’S CAR** pulls in hot, gravel crunching under her tires, engine still grumbling as she throws it into park. She cuts the ignition.  Exhales like she’s just held her breath for twenty minutes. Stares at the garage.

**Door shut.**  **No amps humming.**  **No sounds of tuning or bickering or anyone giving half a shit.**  The driveway is **empty.**  **No Jeff. No Bill. No Jim. No Jeremy. No Gilley.**

**KATHY** (through gritted teeth)
You have got to be kidding me.

She checks the clock on her dash—**1:26.**  Almost thirty minutes past the agreed time.  She grabs her lyric notebook off the passenger seat, slings her bag over her shoulder, and **slams the door** with a little more force than necessary. Walks toward the garage. Stops. Turns around. Looks at the empty street.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
I *sped* here. I *slept* in denim. I *smell* like transmission fluid and regret. And I’m **still the first one here.**

She looks at the garage again. Dead quiet.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Unbelievable.

(Beat.)

She marches over to the side of the garage, pulls out the folding lawn chair they all pretend not to use, plants it in the shade, and **sits like a queen surveying a kingdom of idiocy.**

She cracks open the lyric notebook. Eyes the top of the page where it says **PLUSSING UP – IDEAS.**

**KATHY** (muttering)
First item on the agenda:  *Yell at everybody.*

*Fade out on Kathy fanning herself with a lyrics page, furious, sweaty, and still, somehow, the most professional person in the band.*

---

## **EXT. GILLEY’S DRIVEWAY – 2:00 P.M. – 34 MINUTES LATER**

The folding chair **sags beneath Kathy**, creaking every time she shifts her weight. Her **notebook is open on her lap**, its pages flapping slightly in the breeze like they’re also sick of waiting.  Her **hair is tied up**, half-damp from sweat. Her **socks are rolled down**, boots unlaced. Her **deodorant gave up twenty minutes ago.**

She checks her watch. **2:00 p.m.**  She blinks. Then looks again.  No new cars. No sounds. No excuses rolling up in the gravel. Her jaw tightens. She flips to a clean page in her notebook and **writes in all caps**:

WHERE
THE
FUCK
IS
EVERYBODY

Then underneath: This is so incredibly unprofessional.  Even though we’re not professional.  I DON’T CARE.  She throws the pen across the driveway. It skips once, twice, and then disappears under the side of the garage. She doesn’t get up to retrieve it.

**KATHY** (aloud, to the empty street)
Cool. Awesome. No big deal. I only *rushed here* like an *idiot* and skipped a goddamn shower and tore a bra in half just to sit here in 90 degrees with a notebook full of garbage and—

(She stops. Breathes. Fumes.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
You know what?  No. No no no.  This is the last time I show up early.  This is the last time I show up on time.  Hell, this is the last time I show up *dressed.*

She stands. Kicks the chair over. Picks up the notebook and slaps it shut like it insulted her.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
They want lyrics? They can get them when I stop hallucinating from heat stroke.

She starts pacing in a tight little circle, ranting low and steady.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Unprofessional. We’re not even a band, we’re a *suggestion*. A *hallucination*. A *group project without a grade*.

*Pause. A car hums in the distance. It’s not turning in.*

She stops pacing. Looks at the road like she could set it on fire with sheer willpower.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
One more minute.

She plants herself in the middle of the driveway, arms crossed, notebook tucked under one elbow like a weapon.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Then I start naming names.

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – MOMENTS LATER – 2:03 P.M.**

The garage door creaks open with the slow, unhurried authority of someone who **has no idea he’s walking into a Category 5 emotional hurricane**.

**MR. GILLEY** enters—late 40s, khaki shorts, faded Cincinnati Reds T-shirt, socks pulled too high, holding a **cherry popsicle in one hand**, the wrapper tucked into the other like a folded-up treaty.

**MR. GILLEY**
Hey there, Kathy.

Kathy turns slowly, still mid-pacing, notebook under her arm, hair frazzled, **eyes full of napalm**.

**KATHY**
Hi, Mr. Gilley.

**MR. GILLEY**
You here for band stuff?

**KATHY**
Was supposed to start at one.

**MR. GILLEY**
Huh.

(He looks around, notes the complete absence of any other band members, amps, or even noise.)

**MR. GILLEY (CONT’D)**
Well, my Jeremy said four.

**KATHY** (exactly flat)
He *what.*

**MR. GILLEY**
Yup. Four o’clock. Said that’s when everyone agreed. He was real confident about it.  You sure it wasn’t four?

**KATHY**
I was sure it was *one*.

**MR. GILLEY** (still friendly, unbothered)
Well… it’s not four.

(Beat. Kathy doesn't speak. Her notebook creaks in her grip.)

**MR. GILLEY (CONT’D)**
You want a popsicle?

(She blinks.)

**KATHY**
What?

**MR. GILLEY**
Got a box in the freezer. Went out there for one. Brought a spare.  They’re cherry.

(He holds it out like a peace offering from a neighboring nation-state.)

**KATHY**  (still boiling)
…Sure.

(She takes it. Slowly.)

**MR. GILLEY**
Don’t bite it too fast.  Snaps your teeth right off.

(He starts to head back inside, completely oblivious to the **rage tsunami** he just walked through.)

**MR. GILLEY (CONT’D)**
Tell Gilley to mow that back corner when you see him. Grass is knee-high.

(He leaves.)

**GARAGE DOOR**
*Whap. Slam.*

**KATHY** stands in silence, popsicle in hand.  She peels the wrapper down two inches. Bites.

**KATHY** (mouth full of ice and disdain)
Four o’clock my ass.

*Fade out on Kathy standing in an empty garage, cooling off by exactly one degree—and plotting someone's public execution with a notebook and a cherry popsicle.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S DRIVEWAY – 2:17 P.M.**

The quiet is broken by the sound of **tires on gravel**, slow and uncertain, as if the driver already suspects he’s **late for something he didn’t know started early**.  A **faded blue Ford Escort** pulls into the driveway, the kind of car that smells like cassette tape plastic and dust warmed by sunlight.  **KATHY** is still in the garage, leaning against the wall, arms crossed, popsicle stick now dangling from her mouth like the world's angriest cigar.

The **car door creaks**, and **JEFF** steps out—shirt clean, bass case in hand, hair still damp from a shower, like he *knows* how to show up to rehearsal like a functioning person.

**From the passenger side: JEREMY**, wearing sunglasses indoors and out, bouncing like he *doesn’t* realize a slow-burning volcano is glaring at him from ten feet away.

**JEFF** (casual)
Hey.

**KATHY** (flat)
Practice started at one.

**JEFF**
We were told four.

**KATHY**
You were told *wrong.*

**JEREMY** (cheerfully oblivious)
Well then technically, we’re *early*.

Kathy doesn’t move. Doesn’t blink. Just **points to her notebook**, which sits on the amp stack behind her like an executioner’s scroll.

**KATHY**
I've been here for 51 minutes.  Wearing the same clothes I slept in.  In the heat.  With a bra that could double as a bear trap.  Would you like to make another joke?

(Beat.)

**JEREMY**
…No.

**JEFF** (quietly, to Jeremy)
We’re gonna set up. Calmly. Quietly.

**KATHY**
I brought my notebook.  I had a plan.  I had ideas.  I *was ready.*

**JEREMY**
