It’s not our fault Gilley said four.

**KATHY**
That’s the *problem*, Jeremy. It’s *always* Gilley saying something different, and no one checks. And I’m the one who ends up looking insane to show up when we all agreed to show up.

(Beat.)

**JEFF**
Okay.

(He puts his bass down gently, like he’s placing a baby on a church pew.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
Let’s sit. Let’s breathe. Let’s talk lyrics.

**KATHY**
No. We don’t sit until I get one answer: *Who the hell told Gilley it was four o’clock?*

(Jeff and Jeremy look at each other.)

**JEREMY**
Wasn’t me.

**JEFF**
Could’ve been Bill.

**JEREMY**
Could’ve been Gilley making it up.

**KATHY**
Well, I was told one. I showed up at one.  And unless someone invents time travel in the next five minutes, the official record now reads:  *Kathy was first.*

(Beat. Popsicle stick still dangling.)

**JEFF**
For the record…You’re right.

Kathy **crunches the popsicle stick between her teeth.**
Spits it out into a nearby trash can without looking.

**KATHY**
Damn right I am.

---

## **EXT. GILLEY’S DRIVEWAY – 2:23 P.M.**

A **two-door Honda Civic** pulls up, its muffler slightly louder than necessary, a **snare case strapped in the back seat** with a bungee cord and blind optimism.

**JIM BROWN** steps out, drum key clipped to his belt loop, holding a cooler that probably contains root beer, actual beer, or one of each. He’s wearing sunglasses, and the **look on his face says “I nailed the timing.”**

He spots **Jeff and Jeremy near the garage**, both unnaturally still.

Then he sees **Kathy**, standing on the concrete like an executioner in Converse, arms crossed, **popsicle stick clenched between her teeth like a blade.**

Jim freezes mid-step.

**JIM**
What’s going on?

**KATHY** (clearly)
Band practice was at *one o’clock*.  I was early.  I’ve been here for over **an hour.**

**JIM** (confused)
No, it was four.

**KATHY** (snarling)
It was **not.**

**JIM**
Yeah it was. Gilley said four. Everyone knew that.

**KATHY**
Apparently *not everyone.*

**JIM**
Okay, well… *I* showed up early.  So I get bonus points.

(Jim smiles. Nobody else does.)

**JEFF** (gently)
Jim, buddy…

**KATHY** (arms crossed tighter)
You think you get **bonus points**?

**JIM**
Look, I didn’t *make the schedule*, I just *nailed it.*

**JEREMY**
You nailed the *wrong* schedule.

**JIM**
But I nailed it.

**KATHY**
You nailed *nothing*.

(She picks up her lyric notebook like she might use it as a bludgeon.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
The only person who was here at the agreed time was **me.**  Which means either I’m a liar, or the rest of you are living in a parallel timeline where punctuality is a war crime.

**JIM**
I’m just saying—if someone told you one, and someone told me four, maybe we both got bad info.

**KATHY**
Did you **ask** anyone what time we agreed on?

**JIM**
I asked Gilley.

**KATHY**
Oh, perfect. Great. *Fantastic.*

(She flips the notebook open.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Let’s start today’s agenda:

1. Confirm who’s in charge of scheduling
2. Invent a time machine
3. Possibly strangle Gilley with a quarter-inch cable
4. Work on lyrics

(Beat.)

**JIM**
What happened to three guitars and a dream?

**JEFF**
Now it’s three guitars, a notebook, and a hostage crisis.

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S DRIVEWAY – 2:24 P.M. – CONTINUOUS**

Kathy's notebook is open like a war ledger. Jeff is standing like a guy who knows the blast radius of a pending explosion. Jeremy is trying to melt into the siding of the house. And Jim—**Jim decides to go there.**

He sets his cooler down.  Wipes his hands on his shorts.  Stretches his neck like a man preparing for impact.

**JIM** (grinning)
Look—there’s only *one* of us here getting nailed, Kathy.

(Beat. Silence. Gravel settles.)

**JEREMY**
Jesus Christ, man.

**JEFF**
Oh no.

**KATHY** (dead quiet)
Say that again.

**JIM** (half-laughing, instantly regretting it)
Just—I'm saying, like—*statistically speaking*, there’s only one of us who’s been getting—okay no, I’m going to shut up now.

**KATHY**
You should.

**JEFF**
He should.

**JEREMY**
He really, really should.

**KATHY**
Jim.

(She takes one deliberate step forward. Popsicle stick still clenched in her hand like a shiv.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
You're here. That's great.  You're late. That’s fine.  You make *one more comment* like that and I swear to God, I will write a song called "*Your Drumset Is Compensating*" and perform it live in front of your extended family.

(Beat.)

**JIM**
Fuck off!

**KATHY**
You’re not clever. You’re not subtle.  You’re **wet mulch with a floor tom.**

**JIM**
…I don't deserve that from you.

(She takes a deep breath. Flips the notebook shut.)

**KATHY**
Let’s write some fucking lyrics.

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 2:25 P.M. – CONTINUOUS**

The room has gone still. Kathy’s already seething, and Jim—tight-jawed, tired, done—**murmurs it under his breath**:

**JIM**
Fucking bitch.

She hears it. **Immediately.**

**KATHY** (squared up)
Say it again. Louder.

**JIM** (raising his voice, no hesitation)
*Fucking bitch.*

**JEFF** (under his breath)
Jesus Christ.

**JEREMY**
Dude—

**KATHY** (to the others)
You get that? Jeff? Jeremy?  Go ahead. Write it down in your little diaries.

**JIM** (staring her down)
I meant it.

**KATHY** (stops cold)
Uh.

Beat. She drops the notebook onto the amp stack with a slap. **She does not walk away. She walks forward.**

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
You don’t like my temper? Then don’t test it.  You don’t like how I talk? Then fucking lead.  You don’t like how I show up early, get my shit done, and start writing because *nobody else will*?

**JIM**
That’s not what this is about and you know it.

**KATHY**
No? Then what’s it about, Jim?

**JIM**
It’s about how you treat people like they’re beneath you the second you feel cornered.  It’s about how you blow up every time something doesn’t go your way.  It’s about how *everyone else* becomes the problem whenever *you’re not in control.*

**KATHY**
You think I’m trying to control this band?

**JIM**
You don’t try. You do. You dominate. You yell. You shove. You pick fights with Gilley, sleep with him, throw fits at us, and still want a fucking trophy for showing up on time.

**JEFF**
Guys—

**JIM**
You don’t lead, Kathy. You *bully.*  And I’m sick of it.

(Beat.)

Kathy steps back. Wind knocked out of her for a moment—not by guilt, but by *contact.* She glares at Jeff, then Jeremy. Neither of them says a word. She nods once. Sharp. Controlled.

**KATHY**
Fine.

**JIM**
Not asking you to agree.

**KATHY**
You think this is about being a woman?  You think I’m playing some kind of feminist card?

**JIM**
No. I think you’re acting like an asshole. Same as I would if it were Gilley or Jeremy pulling this shit.

**KATHY**
So that’s it. I’m the bitch and you’re the voice of reason?

**JIM**
Today? Yeah.  You’re wrong, Kathy.

(Beat. Her breathing is fast. Furious. But the comeback never lands.)

**KATHY** (quiet)
Then I guess I’ll leave you geniuses to figure out the lyrics.

She turns. Picks up her notebook. Walks out—**no explosion. No flourish. Just gone.**

Silence.

**JEREMY** (very small)
So, uh…We still doing band democracy?

**JEFF**
Not today.

*FADE OUT on the garage, thick with heat, ego, and the unmistakable tension of a group that may have just crossed a line they can’t walk back from.*

---

## **EXT. GILLEY’S DRIVEWAY – MOMENTS LATER**

Kathy storms out into the sun, notebook clenched under her arm like a blade. She doesn’t head to her car. She **walks the perimeter**—around the side of the house, boots loud in the gravel, shoulders hunched.

**JEFF** steps out of the garage. No words yet. He waits until she’s near the fence line before following, slowly. Not chasing—**shadowing.**

### **EXT.BACK OF GILLEY’S PROPERTY – SHADE LINE**

Kathy’s by the tree line now, standing where the light breaks against the edge of the field. She doesn’t turn when he approaches.

**JEFF** (soft)
You okay?

**KATHY**
Don’t ask me that.

(Beat.)

**JEFF**
I’m coming out here because I respect you.  So I’m gonna be honest.

She stops. Still facing away.

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
You’re not crazy.  But you are wrong.

That gets her attention. She turns, slow, eyes narrowing.

**KATHY**
Excuse me?

**JEFF**
Practice was at four.  I’m sure of it.  That’s what I was told.  That’s what *everyone* was told.

**KATHY**
Then why the hell did you show up early?

**JEFF**
To clean the garage.  To prep gear.  So the rest of you wouldn’t have to drag amps around in ninety-degree heat before rehearsal.  Not because I thought it started at one.

(Beat.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
You got the time wrong, Kathy. You messed up. And instead of admitting it, you came in swinging—again.

**KATHY**
I was—

**JEFF**
—Loud. Demeaning.  You talked to us like we were idiots. Like you were the only one who cared.

**KATHY**
I *do* care.

**JEFF**
No. You care when it gives you power.  You care when it lets you lead.  But when things don’t go your way? You blow up. You rage. You burn everything in reach.  And then you act like we’re lucky to survive it.

(Beat.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
You call yourself professional, but your temper is the most *amateur* thing in the band.

**KATHY** (snaps)
Don’t talk to me about professionalism when Gilley—

**JEFF**
*You* chose that.  You’re the one sleeping with someone who can’t keep his head on straight for more than three days at a time.  You think that’s not affecting the rest of us?

**KATHY** (quiet, shaken)
That’s not fair.

**JEFF**
No, what’s not fair is standing there, acting like we’re the ones who don’t care because you wrote something in a notebook and showed up sweaty.

**KATHY**
I thought we were starting at one.

**JEFF**
And when it was clear we weren’t, you *still* turned it into a war.

(Silence.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
You want to be the heartbeat of this band? Great.  Then stop trying to be the engine, the steering wheel, and the gas pedal too.  Because right now? You’re wrecking it.

(She looks down. The notebook presses tighter under her arm.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
The problem isn’t the time.  It’s that you don’t trust us enough to carry this thing with you.  You’d rather explode than ask for help.

(Beat.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
I’m not mad.  But I’m tired.  And I’m not going to sit in that garage and get barked at by someone who won’t admit when she’s wrong.

(He takes a step back.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
So when you’re ready to be in a band again—*a real one*—we’ll be inside.

He turns and walks off. Kathy doesn’t follow. She just stares at the horizon, the heat shimmering off the field, her mouth tight and dry. She looks at the notebook. And for the first time, **it doesn’t feel like a weapon.**  It feels like a mirror.

---

## **EXT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 2:41 P.M. – LATER**

The sun has shifted. The shadows are longer. The tension is still lingering—but the garage door is open again.  **JEFF, JIM, and JEREMY** are inside, mostly silent, tuning, rewrapping cables, fidgeting with gear. No one's talking much.  Then—**KATHY walks in.**  Still red-faced.  Still braless.  Still not backing down.  She’s holding the **shop vac** like a sword. Everyone looks up.

**KATHY**
I’m not going to apologize.

(Silence.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
But I’m gonna clean.

(They blink.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
I’m gonna use this thing, and I’m going to vacuum every inch of this rat-trap barn of a garage.  I’m going to get the **straw**, the **dust**, the **dead bugs**, the **snapped guitar strings**, and whatever the hell else has been decomposing in the corners since Easter.

(She plugs in the shop vac. Doesn’t flinch. Looks around.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
And if *any* of you so much as *whispers* the word “domestic” while I’m doing it—
I.
Will.
End you.

**JIM** (nods)
That’s at least an improvement.

**JEREMY**
Respectfully muted.

**JEFF**
Then let’s clean.

Kathy hits the power.  The shop vac screams to life. **It’s not an apology.**  It’s a reset.

*Fade out on the garage slowly transforming—still imperfect, still loud—but finally moving forward again, one dusty corner at a time.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 2:45 P.M. – 3:30 P.M.**

The others have drifted off for now—inside for drinks, out to the yard, pretending to tinker with mic stands. They know better than to hover.

**KATHY** is alone with the **shop vac**, the **buzz** of it loud and steady, **the hum of something she can control**. She works corner to corner. Not rushed. Not distracted.  **Deliberate.**

She hits the corners first. **Straw wadded behind the kick drum. Crumbs ground into old carpet.**  Then the **ceiling**—slowly jabbing the nozzle into the **rafters**, dislodging dust webs and tiny brown spiders who had claimed squatters’ rights in the insulation.  She finds a **lost pick**, a **broken pencil**, and **a dried-out Sharpie** she doesn’t remember throwing.  Each pass of the vacuum is mechanical. **Like breathing.**

She stops to wipe sweat from her forehead with the hem of her shirt. Sits for a second on the amp case. Then stands and keeps going.  Every movement is small—but it matters.  **It’s not forgiveness.**  It’s not surrender.  It’s her way of **putting the rage away**.  Not denying it. Just… **packing it back into its box**. For now.

By the time the clock reads **3:30**, the floor is cleared, the walls are dusted, the corners are reclaiming their shape.  **The air smells like dust and rubber and muscle.**  She kills the power on the vac.  The sudden silence is deafening.  And… kind.  She stands in the quiet garage, hair clinging to her neck, hands on her hips, face flushed—but **eyes clear again**.

**KATHY (quietly, to herself)**
Okay.

She closes the lid on the shop vac.  **Pandora’s box, sealed.** For now.

*FADE OUT.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 3:33 P.M.**

The shop vac is unplugged, coiled neatly in the corner. The floor is clear. The air feels lighter.  **JEFF, JIM, and JEREMY** are trickling back in—holding cables, drinks, half-finished thoughts. Nobody quite knows where things stand, but **the tension has dropped by a few decibels.**

**KATHY** walks in from the back door, **hair damp**, arms crossed lightly over her notebook.

She speaks—not loudly, not softly. **Level.**

**KATHY**
Okay.  Here’s what’s happening.  We’re going to have a discussion.  A real one.  Once the rest of the band gets here.

(Beat.)
But I’m not leading it. Not this time.

(She looks around the room, meets each of their eyes.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
I’ll listen.  That’s it.

She sits down on the amp case, pulls the cap off her pen, and opens the notebook to a fresh page.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Say what you need to say.

She waits.

*FADE OUT on the boys exchanging looks—uncertain, surprised, and maybe a little impressed—as the air in the garage shifts from volatile to possible.**

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 3:34 P.M. – CONTINUOUS**

Kathy sets her notebook down on an amp case like she’s placing it on a desk.  She’s calm. She’s seated. But she’s **not passive.**

**KATHY**
Once the rest of the band gets here, we’re going to talk.  Real stuff.  Direction. Writing. How this is going to work moving forward.

(Beat. Looks around.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
And—I’ll listen.  For real. Not just waiting to talk.

(There’s a moment. The others nod, still feeling the shift in the air.)

Then she adds, casually, without losing her grip on the room:

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Also… if one of you could scrounge up a card table or something?  Chairs?  Anything flat and vaguely horizontal?

(Beat.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Kind of hard to build consensus when we’re all crouched like ostriches on milk crates.

**JEFF** (quiet smile)
I’ll check the basement.

**JIM**
Gilley’s got a folding table under the porch. I’ll grab it.

**JEREMY**
I can find chairs. Probably not matching ones. Possibly stolen ones.

**KATHY**
Fine. As long as none of them smell like Gilley’s gym socks.

(The guys scatter into motion—**not because they’re told**, but because the room now has **purpose.**)

Kathy picks up her pen. Scribbles something at the top of a new page:

**Lyric Room – Version 1.0**
*No yelling. No posturing. Just sound.*

*FADE OUT on a garage slowly becoming a war room—not for conflict, but for creation.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 3:55 P.M.**

The garage is almost civilized now.

* A **folding table** has been set up.
* **Four mismatched chairs** are scattered around it—one milk crate, one rusty lawn chair, one real dining chair, and a beanbag no one trusts.
* Kathy sits at the head of the table with her notebook open, Jeff to her left, Jim to her right, Jeremy Evans leaning back in the lawn chair, feet on a cable reel.

The **garage refrigerator door swings open**, and in walks **JEREMY GILLEY**—a **12-pack of bottled water** under each arm, big grin on his face like he’s arriving at a barbecue he forgot he was hosting.

**JEREMY GILLEY**
Heyyyy, look at this—band meeting *in session!* I like it.

(He walks past Kathy without noticing the storm cloud behind her eyes, drops the water into the fridge, and immediately starts glad-handing.)

**JEREMY GILLEY (CONT’D)**
Jeff! Jimmy! Jeremy!

(Knuckle-bumps each of them.)
Look at this setup! Folding table and *everything?* What are we, professional now?

**JEFF**
You’re five minutes early.

**JIM**
Which means you’re thirty minutes late, depending on which Kathy you asked.

**JEREMY GILLEY** (chuckles)
Well damn, I brought water. That buys me ten, right?

He turns to Kathy at last, arms open like he's about to give her a church camp hug.

**JEREMY GILLEY (CONT’D)**
Kath! Look at this place! You cleaned it up! It’s practically habitable.

(Beat. Kathy stares at him.)

**KATHY**
Hi, Gilley.

(She does not get up. She does not smile.)

**JEREMY GILLEY** (still sunny)
Right. We’re being serious. Got it. Band mode.

(He plops into the beanbag. It squeaks in protest.)

**JEREMY GILLEY (CONT’D)**
Alright. Who’s got an agenda? And does it involve yelling at me, or are we on the “forgiveness and harmony” part of the program?

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
One of those, yeah.

**JEFF**
Sit tight, Gilley. The meeting hasn’t started yet.

**KATHY**
We’ll begin when Bill gets here.

**JEREMY GILLEY** (throws hands up, grinning)
Look at that—*structure*. This band’s growing up.

*FADE OUT on Gilley sipping bottled water, completely unaware that the chair of the meeting plans to **grill him like a hamburger the minute the quorum is met.***

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 4:00 P.M. ON THE DOT**

The table is set. Everyone but one is present. Kathy sits with her arms folded, notebook open, pen uncapped. Gilley is cross-legged in the beanbag, radiating confidence. Jeff and the two Jeremys are halfway through cracking their knuckles and making peace with whatever comes next.

Then: **the sound of Bill’s car door shutting outside.**

### **INT.GARAGE – MOMENTS LATER**

**BILL DAVENPORT** walks in, **synth patch bag in one hand**, a **loose coil of cables over the other shoulder**. He’s calm. He’s exactly on time. He’s always exactly on time.

**BILL**
Hey. Four o’clock. I’m on the dot. We good?

**JEFF** (flat)
Being early is on time.

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
Being on time is late.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
Being late is rude.

**JIM**
Being Gilley is a federal offense.

**JEREMY GILLEY**
Hey, I brought water. That clears at least one misdemeanor.

**BILL** (sighs, setting his stuff down)
Okay. I’m late.

**KATHY**
Glad you’re here. Sit.

**BILL**
Where?

**KATHY**
Avoid the beanbag. It’s already claimed.

(Gilley waves like a proud possum.)

Bill grabs the remaining milk crate and sits down. Looks around. Takes in the table, the tone, the silence.

**BILL**
Okay, so are we doing an intervention, a lyric meeting, or a tribunal?

**JEFF**
Little of all three.

**KATHY**
This is the first time we’ve all been in a room at the same time with the intention of **building something together**. So we’re gonna do just that. But first, we talk.

*FADE OUT as the band finally—**fully**—assembles at the table. Seven folding legs, five mismatched chairs, six stubborn people, and the absolute possibility of a future.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 4:03 P.M. – AROUND THE TABLE**

Everyone is seated. The popsicle stick is gone.  The shop vac is quiet.  The notebook is open.

**KATHY**
Alright. We’ve been messing around long enough.  Covers are fine. Practicing tone is fine. But if we’re gonna be a real band—We need to start writing our *own* material.

(Beat.)

**JEFF** (grinning, quick)
That sounds so, uh…so cool.

**JIM**
So scary.

**JEREMY GILLEY** (disinterested)
I couldn’t be arsed to write.

**KATHY**
Then sit quiet and let the rest of us work.

**JEREMY EVANS**
But wait—wait—before we go too far: What about our sound?  Like, if we’re writing songs, what *are* they? What do we sound like?

**KATHY** (holding up a hand)
Hold on.  Stay with me.  Let’s start at the base level: lyrics.  Words. Themes. Stuff that matters.  The rest—the arrangement, the sound, the genre tag—*we’ll get there.*  But right now?

**We start with stories.**

(Beat.)

**BILL**
So this is the lyric room now?

**KATHY**
Yeah. It is.

**JEFF**
Ground zero.

**JIM**
If I have to rhyme “pain” with “rain” I’m leaving.

**KATHY**
You won’t. Not if we do it right.

**JEFF**
So who’s got the first idea?

(Silence.)

**KATHY**
We all do.  We just haven’t written it down yet.

*FADE OUT as pens are uncapped, backs straighten, and six kids in a cleaned-out garage lean forward like they might actually be building something permanent.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 4:05 P.M. – LYRIC ROOM IN SESSION**

The card table is covered in open notebooks, scattered pens, two uncapped highlighters, and a paper plate someone used as a coaster.  Everyone is bracing for the first creative step.

**JEREMY GILLEY**
Okay, so—if I *have* to contribute… can someone else just write my shit down for me?

(Beat.)

**KATHY** (squinting)
Seriously?

**JEREMY GILLEY**
I like spitballing! I’m good at it. Big ideas. Concepts. Phrases that *punch.*  But sitting still with a pen? That’s like torture.

**JEFF**
You want a stenographer?

**JEREMY GILLEY**
I want a court recorder with a sense of rhythm.

**JIM**
Jesus.

**JEREMY EVANS** (leaning back)
To be fair, he’s good at dropping lines.  Like… he’ll walk by your amp, say something insane, and it’s suddenly a chorus.

**GILLEY**
Thank you.  Let me pace. Let me riff. I’ll punch up. I’ll veto bad lines. I’ll drop hooks like bricks.  Just… don’t ask me to sit.

**BILL**
So you’re a creative consultant?

**GILLEY**
Exactly. I’m your in-house devil. With vision.

**KATHY** (sighs)
Fine. But someone better keep up with him. Because if he says something brilliant while pacing, and no one writes it down, it’s gone forever.

**JEFF**
I’ll track him.  Like a weird, wiry deer that smells like sweat and teenage ego.

**GILLEY**
You're welcome.

(Gilley stands. Starts pacing. Instantly in rhythm with nothing.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
Okay—okay—imagine a song that feels like *falling off a bike into a baptismal font.*  That’s the energy.

**BILL**
Writing that down.

**JIM**
We’re all going to hell.

**KATHY**
Only if the first verse sucks.

*FADE OUT on Gilley circling the garage like an escaped poet while the others scramble to catch the pieces as they fall.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 4:07 P.M. – CARD TABLE ROUNDUP**

Gilley’s pacing. Jeremy (Evans) is half-reclined with a pencil balanced across his upper lip. Kathy is scribbling words like she’s defusing a bomb. Jeff’s leaning back in the folding chair, arms crossed, watching the room breathe.

**BILL** (casual, direct)
We all know who’s gonna do the heavy lifting here.

(Beat.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
It’s gonna be you two.

(nods at Kathy and Jeff)

**KATHY** (flat)
Gee, thanks.

**JEFF** (shrugs)
Don’t sound so sure.  Everybody’s got a voice here.  Mine’s not gonna be the loudest.

**JEREMY (EVANS)** (snorts)
*Bullshit.*

(Everyone looks over.)

**JEREMY (EVANS) (CONT’D)**
Come on, man. You’ve had a notebook in your back pocket since junior high.  You’re built for this.  You’re not *trying* to dominate, but you’re gonna fill the page before any of us open our mouths.

**JEFF**
That’s not the point.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
I know.  But you might as well own it.

(Beat. The air gets real honest.)

**KATHY**
He's not wrong.

**JEFF** (small smile)
I hate when you're both right.

**BILL**
Doesn’t matter. You write, we plus. That’s the model.

**GILLEY**
I’ll shout slogans from the perimeter.

**JIM**
If I write anything it’s gonna be about how much I hate writing lyrics.

**KATHY**
Then start with that. That’s at least honest.

(Beat.)

**JEFF**
Alright. No heroes. No passengers.  We start simple. A phrase. A theme. A line.
And we build.

*FADE OUT on pencils scratching, Gilley pacing, and the first glimmer of a band writing itself into existence, one sentence at a time.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 4:12 P.M. – MOMENTS LATER**

The table’s buzzing—ideas floating, pencils scribbling, Kathy underlining something with force. But **Gilley has gone quiet mid-pace**. He’s watching Jeff. **Really** watching him. Then, without breaking stride, he stops and levels his voice—not loud, not joking. Just *true*.

**GILLEY**
Look, man. The only way we ever get anywhere—*really get anywhere*—is if *you* put your heart and soul, if you even have one, deep into that little computer of yours. Onto paper. Into tape. *Out.*

(Beat. Jeff doesn’t look up yet.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
I know you. I’ve known you since before we knew how to fake confidence.  And I *know* you’re brilliant.  But you don’t have the balls to actually go where you need to go.

**JEFF** (lifting his eyes, deadpan)
Gee, thanks.

**GILLEY**
I’m not insulting you.  I’m daring you.

(He steps closer, into Jeff’s space—but not hostile. *Intimate.*)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
Grab your balls, man.  Drag yourself into the 90s.  And **fucking dominate it**. Say something real.  Say something you *don’t* want people to hear. Be fearless.

(Beat.)

The room is quiet. Nobody laughs. Not even Jeremy.

**KATHY** (quietly)
He’s right.

**BILL**
Yeah.

**JIM**
First time for everything.

**JEFF** (slow nod)
Alright.

(He clicks his pen. Flips to a blank page.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
Let’s see if I can scare myself.

*FADE OUT on the first line being written—long, looping, unedited. Gilley smiles. He’s not mocking. He’s just waiting for the next line.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 4:13 P.M. – CONTINUOUS**

Jeff has just uncapped his pen, the first blank page in front of him, the room holding still like it’s waiting for thunder.  Jeff leans forward. Focused. Tension in his wrist like he’s about to start a confession instead of a chorus. And then, from across the table—

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
If Jeff actually put his mind to it?

(long pause)
He could scare the *piss* outta the very Devil.

(Beat.)

Jeff doesn’t look up.  But a crooked grin twitches at the corner of his mouth.

**JEFF**
Good.  Let’s hope the fucker’s listening.

*FADE OUT on ink meeting paper, a page slowly filling with something sharp, and six kids inching their way into their own myth.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 4:15 P.M. – A FEW LINES LATER**

Jeff’s written something.  He’s halfway down the page.  It’s *good*.  He knows it’s good.  That’s the problem. The room’s quieter now—everyone leaning over their own notebooks, heads down, pens scratching. Jeff sets his pen down and leans back. Hands on his thighs. Breath slow.

**JEFF**
Alright, so—just putting this out there…I don’t want my name on the lyrics.

(Everyone looks up.)

**KATHY**
Why?

**JEFF**
Because I don’t want to be *that guy*.  The one who hoards credit.  The one whose name shows up in bold while the rest of you are still tuning.

**JIM**
Then don’t hoard it. Just own it.

**JEFF**
I want this to be collaborative. Open.  We all build it together, right? So why put *my* name at the bottom of the page?

**GILLEY**
Because you wrote it.

**JEFF**
I *started* it.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
That’s called writing.

**BILL**
If you want to erase your name from your own work, fine.  But don’t pretend it’s noble.  It’s fear.

(Beat. Jeff flinches just a bit.)

**KATHY**
You said you didn’t want to be the loudest voice.  That’s fine. But don’t pretend you’re not a voice at all.  You *are.*  Loud or not, people are gonna hear it.  Might as well make sure they know it’s *yours.*

(Beat.)

**JEFF**
I just…I want people to like the song. Not think about who wrote it.

**GILLEY**
Then make them like it *because* you wrote it.

(Jeff doesn't respond. Not right away.)

He glances at the page again.  The lyrics are staring back—**raw, real, sharp as anything he's ever dared to say out loud.**  He presses the pen back to paper.

**JEFF**
Fine.  But no bold print.  Just… in the liner notes. Small.  Same size as everyone else.

**JIM**
Deal. But if it’s a hit, we’re writing “*Scared the Devil* – Words by Jeff Evans” on your gravestone.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
Seconded.

*FADE OUT on the page filling again—lines gaining shape, voice finding courage, and Jeff finally stepping forward, not to lead, but to own what he started.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 4:17 P.M. – CONTINUOUS**

Jeff still has the pen in his hand. The page in front of him holds something *close* to finished. Everyone’s watching him like a fragile wire might snap. He’s not looking for applause—but he’s visibly uncomfortable being *seen* this clearly.

Then Kathy speaks—calm, measured.

**KATHY**
Okay.  How about this—Instead of saying “lyrics by” and sticking one name under it…We just say: *By the Band.*

(Beat. She looks around the room.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Because even if one person starts it, the rest of us shape it.  Even if someone writes the first verse, someone else changes a word, adds a harmony, cuts a line.  So… let’s credit it that way. Not to hide.  Not to avoid ownership.  Just to make clear: *this is ours.*

**JEFF** (quietly)
Band as author.

**KATHY**
Yeah.

(Beat.)

**BILL**
I can live with that.

**JIM**
I prefer it.  Saves room on the tape sleeve.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
Also sounds kind of badass.

**GILLEY**
It does! Like a gang tag.  “Lyrics: The Band.”  Says everything. Says nothing. Mysterious. Powerful.

(Jeff nods. Finally lets himself smile.)

**JEFF**
Alright. By the Band it is.

(He scribbles it across the top of the page in the margin.)

**“BY THE BAND”**

**KATHY**
Now let’s keep going.  We’re barely one page in.

*FADE OUT as pens uncap again, the table buzzes with life, and six people write under a single name—not because they’re hiding, but because they’re finally building it together.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 4:28 P.M. – LYRIC MOMENTUM IN FULL SWING**

Jeff is writing again. Kathy’s scribbling in her notebook beside him. Jeremy Evans is building lines like Lego pieces, and Gilley’s tossing in weird metaphors from his endless mental furnace. For the first time in hours, **they’re humming.** Then **BILL** clears his throat—barely above a whisper. Everyone looks up.

**BILL**
Not so fast.

(Beat.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
There’s something else we need to take care of today.

(Silence.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
We need to build our democracy.

**JEFF** (sits back slowly)
You want to do that *now?*

**BILL**
Yeah. While we still like each other.  Before the first real gig. Before the first money. Before the first fight over who’s name goes where on the poster.

**JIM**
So, what, we vote on everything now?

**BILL**
Not *everything*. But the big stuff.  Songs. Setlists. Recording. Money. Touring. Decisions that affect the group as a whole.

**KATHY**
We already agreed on supermajority, didn’t we?

**BILL**
That was a start.  But we haven’t put it in writing.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
You want a *constitution*?

**BILL**
Exactly.  One page. One rule: if it affects all of us, it requires **four out of six** to pass.  Supermajority.  No yelling. No autocrats. No silent sabotage.

**GILLEY**
Can we include a clause about root beer floats and air conditioning?

**BILL**
If it gets four votes.

**JEFF** (quiet, smiling)
You really mean it. Band democracy.

**BILL**
It protects all of us. Especially when things get good. Or hard.

**KATHY**
Let’s do it.

**JIM**
Yeah. Before anyone tries to name us something like *Crater.*

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
Still a better name than *The Mustache Incident.*

**GILLEY**
I second that.

**BILL**
Alright. I’ll draft the document.  We sign it tonight.

(Beat.)

**JEFF**
Add this to the bottom: “Lyrics by the Band. Decisions by the Band.”

**KATHY**
No gods. No masters.

**JIM**
Just amps and a folding table.

*FADE OUT on the six of them, suddenly very aware they’ve taken another step—out of chaos, into something **intentional**. The Band has rules now. And just maybe, a future.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 4:49 P.M.**

A **greasy, half-flattened pizza box** has been cleared of crumbs and now sits dead center on the card table. **Bill** stands over it, **Sharpie uncapped**, brow furrowed in quiet purpose.

The band watches, a mix of reverence and suppressed laughter.

**GILLEY**
We’re really doing this on cardboard?

**BILL**
Cardboard doesn’t crash. Paper tears. Pizza box lasts forever.

**JEFF** (quiet)
It’s also already carried something holy.

**KATHY**
Just spell my name right.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
Do we need a notary?

**JIM**
We need a miracle.

**BILL** (concentrating, writing as he speaks)
*THE CHARTER OF THE BAND*

* All major decisions—creative, financial, logistical—require a **supermajority**: *four out of six*.
* All members get equal voice. No permanent leader. No executive veto.
* Songwriting credited to **“The Band.”** Anyone can contribute. Everyone is expected to.
* Every member has the right to dissent. No one has the right to sabotage.
* Conflict is resolved by vote, not volume.
* If someone breaks the spirit of this document, they’re responsible for the next pizza.

(Beat.)

He signs the bottom:  **—BILL DAVENPORT** . Then slides it forward.

**BILL (CONT’D)**
Next.

**JEFF** signs.  Then **KATHY**, slowly, carefully.  Then **JIM**, scratching hard.  **JEREMY (EVANS)** writes in looping, blocky letters.  **GILLEY** signs last, upside-down and too large.  They all look down at the cardboard.  It’s greasy. It’s uneven. It’s not legally binding.

It’s perfect.

**KATHY**
Well. We’re a band.

**JEFF**
Now we’re also a government.

**JIM**
Can we impeach Gilley?

**GILLEY**
Only with four votes.

And so it begins.  In a sweltering garage outside Donnelsville, Ohio—behind a stack of amps, around a scratched-up folding table, beneath a Charter written in Sharpie on a pizza box lid—six kids sit shoulder-to-shoulder.  The page is blank. The democracy is real.  Jeff leans forward.  Eyes sharp. Pen ready.

*FADE OUT on the pizza box propped up on the amp stack—**a monument to what they just built**, and what they’re about to try and hold together.*

---

# **CHAPTER THREE: THROUGH THESE FIELDS OF DESTRUCTION**

---
## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 4:32 P.M. – AROUND THE CARD TABLE**

The pizza box charter sits between them. A Sharpie rolls slowly to a stop. Jeff’s been quiet, watching everyone sign. He sets his pen down last, fingers tapping the edge of the box. Then he looks up.

**JEFF**
Alright. If we’re actually gonna do this— *like this*— Then two things have to be true.

(Beat.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
First—lyrics don’t belong to any one person.  If it goes into a song, it’s not “mine” or “hers” or “whoever started the verse.”  It’s *ours*.  No Lennon-McCartney, no one fighting for credit.  Just *“by the band.”*

(They nod. Even Gilley doesn't interrupt.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
Second—this band isn’t a dictatorship. Not even a quiet one.  We make decisions together. Big ones.  And we don’t move forward unless **four out of six** say yes.  No screaming. No ghosting. Just… vote.

**KATHY**
And stick to it?

**JEFF**
Yeah.  No wiggling out.  We follow the process—especially when we don’t get our way.

**JIM**
Even if the vote’s dumb?

**JEFF**
Especially then.

(Beat.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
We do it like this, or we don’t do it at all.  Because otherwise?  We’re just pretending.

*Silence. Then Kathy nods once. The others follow.*  They’ve got rules now. And Jeff just made sure they mean something.

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 4:35 P.M. – AT THE TABLE**

The charter sits in the center. Ink still fresh. The Sharpie uncapped, left beside the pizza box like a gavel after a verdict. Jeff straightens up. Looks around the table.

**JEFF**
Alright then. Where are the yeas?

(One by one, each hand goes up.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
And the nays?

(Quiet. Still. No movement.)

He nods once, slow, final.

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
Vote is six to zero.

It’s official. They’re not just a band anymore. They’re a band *with law.*

*FADE OUT on the cardboard charter in the middle of the table, sun catching its grease stains like they’re burn marks from something sacred.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 4:36 P.M. – CONTINUOUS**

Everyone’s still basking in the silence that follows the **6–0 vote**.  Jeff’s arms are folded. Kathy has her pen poised. Jeremy Evans is lightly drumming with two pens on the table. Gilley is already half-sprawled in the beanbag like it’s all been settled forever. Then **Bill speaks**. Calm. Not disruptive. Just… pointed.

**BILL**
That worked out really, really easy.

(Beat.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
Too easy, actually.

(Everyone looks over.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
So, I’m gonna kick up a little dirt here. Just to see if this thing holds.

**JEFF**
Go ahead.

**BILL**
What if we’re on the road? We’ve got a show in six hours.  Someone wants to add a new song to the setlist. It’s rough. Half-done.  We don’t have time to polish it.

**KATHY**
But it’s good?

**BILL**
Maybe.  But one person hates it. Thinks it’ll crash.  The rest say go. Does it go?

**JEFF**
What’s the vote?

**BILL**
Five to one.

**JEFF**
Then it goes on the list.

**BILL**
Even if that one person is the one who has to play it?

(Beat.)

**JIM**
Oof.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
So now we’re talking labor rights.

**KATHY**
Who’s the holdout?

**BILL**
Doesn’t matter. Pick one of us.  The point is—can we enforce a supermajority rule that *compels* a member to perform something they don’t believe in?

**GILLEY**
Oooooh. Spicy.

(They all go quiet for a moment.)

**JEFF**
Then it’s a tie between policy and conscience.

**KATHY**
You can’t force performance.  That’s not democracy. That’s conscription.

**JEFF**
But you *can* vote to cut it.  If it’s that divisive? It waits.

**BILL**
So majority rules, but no one plays under protest?

**JEFF**
Not if we want to keep functioning.

**KATHY**
We’re not just voting on sound.  We’re voting on *trust*.

**BILL**
That’s what I needed to hear.

(Beat. He leans back.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
Okay. Let’s see if it holds next time we’re tired, broke, and mad at each other.

**JEFF**
It won’t be easy then.

**BILL**
Exactly.

(He nods, satisfied. The system passed its first hypothetical.)

*FADE OUT on the band, not shaken—but tested. And maybe, just maybe, stronger for it.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 4:40 P.M. – CONTINUOUS**

Bill, still leaning forward, decides to finish the experiment. He’s calm. Controlled. Eyes on the charter pizza box like it’s the Constitution.

**BILL**
Alright. Let’s make it formal.

Motion: *Band members can be compelled to perform a song they voted against if a supermajority approves it.*

(Beat.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
Ayes?

(His own hand goes up. Jim’s follows—slow, uncertain.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
Nays?

Kathy’s hand goes up.  Then Jeff’s.  Then Jeremy Evans.  Then Gilley, grinning like he’s voting on prom decorations.

**BILL (CONT’D)**
Two to four. Motion rejected.

(He nods once. Zero emotion.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
And there it is.

**JEFF**
The system works.

**KATHY**
Barely.

**GILLEY**
But it works.

**JIM**
I hate that I agreed with Bill on principle and still lost.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
Welcome to government.

*FADE OUT on the cardboard charter in the center of the table, already stained with ink and sweat, but standing firm—their **first real test**, passed without yelling or blood.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 4:43 P.M. – STILL AROUND THE TABLE**

The last vote is in. Bill’s motion is dead. The band is settling, everyone a little more confident in the system they’ve built.  Then Jim shifts in his chair.

**JIM**
I’m gonna shit a brick here.

(The room goes still. All eyes on him.)

**JIM (CONT’D)**
I know no one’s gonna appreciate this right now.  But this? *This* is crucial to our long-term survival.

**KATHY**
Okay…?

**JEFF**
Jim, what are you—

**JIM**
Resolved—

(He says it clearly. Formally. No smile.)

**JIM (CONT’D)**
—We don’t have sex with each other in the band.

**SILENCE.**

Not awkward silence.  *Existential.*  Like **God muted the garage**.  Kathy blinks. Jeremy Evans freezes with a pen halfway to his mouth. Gilley actually sets his water down. Jeff’s expression is pure firmware error.

**GILLEY**
Wait, like… ever?

**JIM**
Yes.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
No one? Not even, like… distant cousins of members?

**JIM**
No band hookups. No backstage “accidents.” No emotional entanglements that explode into scheduling conflicts and lyric edits and passive-aggressive cymbal setups.

**KATHY**
That’s… bold.

**JEFF**
It’s also probably unnecessary.

**JIM**
We’re barely holding this together as-is. We throw sex into this equation? It’s a time bomb.

(Beat.)

**JIM (CONT’D)**
So yeah.  Call the vote.

**GILLEY**
You’re seriously motioning this?

**JIM**
I am absolutely, unequivocally putting this forward as a resolution.

**BILL**
Seconded.

*FADE OUT on everyone looking at each other, realizing this might be the **hardest vote of the day**—and the one with the longest shadow.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 4:44 P.M. – MOMENTS AFTER JIM’S MOTION**

The room is still frozen in the wake of **Jim’s resolution**: *no sex within the band.* Everyone’s holding their breath, waiting for Kathy to go nuclear, or Gilley to crack a joke. But it’s **Jeff** who breaks first.

**JEFF** (quietly)
I’ll quit if that’s adopted.

(Beat. You could hear a pick drop.)

Everyone turns to stare.

**JIM**
…What?

**JEFF**
Dead serious.

**KATHY**
You?

**GILLEY**
You?!

**JEFF**
Not because I’m planning to sleep with anyone here—Jesus, no. But because I’m not putting my name under a band charter that **polices what we do with our bodies.**

**BILL**
It’s not about morality. It’s about risk management.

**JEFF**
No, Bill. It’s about *control.*  You don’t prevent dysfunction with rules like that. You prevent it by **growing up**.

(He points to the charter.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
We just agreed to shared authorship. Shared power.  And now what—*surveillance clauses*?

(Beat.)

**JIM**
It’s not surveillance. It’s survival.

**JEFF**
It’s bullshit.  And if we adopt it—I’m out.

(Dead silence.)

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
I thought Gilley would rage quit first.

**GILLEY**
Same.

**KATHY**
I *genuinely* had money on me.

**JEFF**
If we’re gonna be a democracy, then we don’t legislate hypothetical sin.  We deal with shit *when* it happens. Not before.

**BILL**
So you’re voting no?

**JEFF**
I’m voting *hell no*.

(Beat.)

The band looks around.  The vote hasn't even been called.  But now it's no longer just about Jim’s rule.  It’s about *Jeff’s line in the sand.*

*FADE OUT on the band caught between two convictions, realizing that real democracy means sometimes the calmest one sets off the loudest explosion.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 4:45 P.M. – STUNNED SILENCE**

Jeff’s declaration still hangs in the air: *I’ll quit if that’s adopted.* No one knows what to say.  Then Jeff leans forward, voice low but clear—**cutting the air like a scalpel.**

**JEFF**
Let’s get real. This isn’t about controlling the band. This is about **controlling the pussy.**

(Dead silence.)

**JIM**
Whoa.

**JEFF**
Don’t “whoa” me.  You can wrap it in words like “professionalism” and “stability” and “long-term survival,” but what you really mean is: *you don’t want Kathy fucking Gilley again.*

(Beat. No one denies it.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
You’re not wrong to be mad about what that’s done to the band.  But you don’t solve that by outlawing desire. You solve it by facing your damn emotions.

**KATHY** (still stunned)
…Thank you?

**JIM**
It’s not like that.

**JEFF**
Yeah, it is. You weren’t trying to protect the music.  You were trying to erase the threat of emotional chaos—**by shutting down the woman in the room.**

(Beat.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
That’s not democracy. That’s patriarchal bullshit with a group charter taped to the front.

(He sits back. Calm.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
Vote if you want.  But let’s not lie to ourselves about what this really is.

(Dead silence. Still.)

Even Bill doesn’t speak.

*FADE OUT on the table, the Sharpie, the pizza box, and six people realizing that rules are easy—**but truth is harder.***

---

# **CHAPTER FOUR: AND THOUGH WE WERE HURT SO BAD**

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 4:47 P.M. – STILL STUNNED SILENCE**

Jeff’s words still echo: *This isn’t about controlling the band. This is about controlling the pussy.*  No one speaks.  And then—**Kathy sits up straighter**, eyes clear, voice sharp but steady.

**KATHY**
Okay. Let’s just call this what it is. **This is about controlling me.**

(Beat.)
Let’s not pretend otherwise.  Let’s not pretend it’s about sound quality or setlist stability or the sacred chemistry of rehearsal vibes.  It’s about me.  And it’s about *who I sleep with.* And it’s about how that makes you feel.

(She looks directly at Jim.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
And I don’t appreciate it.

(Beat. Her hands are steady on the table. Her breath even.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
But—

(She exhales once, long and slow.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
I’m choosing—*actively choosing*—not to rage quit.  Not to throw this chair.  Not to grab my Bowie knife out of my gig bag and decapitate somebody in the garage we just cleaned together.

**GILLEY**
Which, for the record, we all deeply appreciate.

**JIM**
I didn’t mean it like that.

**KATHY**
Doesn’t matter. That’s what it *was.*

(Beat.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
So here I am. Still at the table. Still showing up. Because that’s who I am. You don’t have to like it.  You don’t have to trust me.  But you will **not** legislate my body.

(Dead silence.)

She nods once. Then looks directly at Bill.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Let’s call the vote. Or withdraw the motion. But I’m not going anywhere.

*FADE OUT on Kathy’s hand resting calmly over her notebook—steady, unarmed, and absolutely unflinching.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 4:49 P.M. – CONTINUOUS**

Kathy’s just said her piece. She’s calm. Clear. Still at the table. But **Jim doesn’t let it go**.  He doesn’t raise his voice. He’s not shouting.  He just leans forward, jaw clenched, heart thudding hard behind the words.

**JIM**
This behavior is counterproductive.

(Beat. He shakes his head.)

**JIM (CONT’D)**
No. It’s worse than that. It’s *toxic*. It’s *destructive*.

**JEFF**
Careful, man.

**JIM**
No. I’m being careful. I’ve been careful. And now I’m being honest.

(He turns to Kathy.)

**JIM (CONT’D)**
You say we shouldn’t control each other’s bodies. Fine. But when someone in this band provides sexual favors to another member? That’s not private anymore. That’s not off the books. That’s not just between you and Gilley. That shows **favoritism**.  That changes the *entire room.*

**BILL**
Jim—

**JIM**
Don’t tell me I’m wrong. You all know I’m not.  You *feel it.*  We all feel it when they’re good and we all *definitely* feel it when they’re not.

(Beat. He’s not lashing out—he’s trying to warn.)

**JIM (CONT’D)**
You want jealousy? You want grudges? You want someone quietly sabotaging takes or skipping rehearsals because they’re pissed off and they don’t even *know* why? Then keep mixing business with sex!

**KATHY**
So we’re just animals now?

**JIM**
We’re *human beings*.  And people get hurt.  And when you dump someone—because it will happen—what then? What happens when one of you breaks the other’s heart?  Do we lose a member?  Do we lose the *band*?

(Beat.)

**JIM (CONT’D)**
I’m not trying to police you.  I’m trying to *protect* this. All of it.

(He gestures to the table, the amps, the gear, the charter.)

**JIM (CONT’D)**
Because I don’t care who’s sleeping with who— but I’ll be damned if I’m gonna let that *wreck* what we’re building here.

*Silence again. Not because he shouted—but because he meant every word.*

*FADE OUT on Jim sitting back in his chair, not smug, not vindicated—just tired and terrified of what he sees coming if no one else will stop it.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 4:52 P.M. – AFTERMATH OF JIM’S WARNING**

Jim’s words are still ringing. The table’s heavy with silence. Kathy’s eyes are locked straight ahead.  Jeff is staring at the charter like it personally betrayed him.  Bill is motionless.  Jeremy Evans is chewing a pen cap like it’s laced with tension.

Then **Gilley speaks**.

**GILLEY**
Fine.

(Everyone turns.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
I’ll quit fucking Kathy.

**RECORD-SCRATCH SILENCE.**

**KATHY** (double-take)
*Excuse me?!*

**GILLEY**
Look, I don’t want to torpedo the band. I don’t want people whispering during soundcheck or making weird faces at practice.

(He shrugs.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
So that’s it. I’ll stop. We’re done.

**KATHY** (staring, stunned)
Are you… *breaking up with me* in front of the band?

**GILLEY**
I’m making a tactical decision.  It's not personal. It's procedural.

**JEFF**
Jesus Christ, you’re doing a *breakup as a motion?*

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
Do we have to vote on this?

**BILL**
God, no.

**KATHY** (still blinking)
I cannot believe this is happening.

**GILLEY**
Don’t take it the wrong way. I still like you. You’re hot. You’re terrifying. You’re brilliant.
But democracy.

**KATHY**
Unbelievable.

**GILLEY**
Also, I can’t compete with your songwriting rage.  That’s a lot of energy to sleep next to.

(Beat.)

**KATHY**
So this is a creative decision?

**GILLEY**
It’s a *constitutional* decision.

**JEFF**
Do we need to get you a ceremonial robe?

**JIM** (still tense)
That… wasn’t what I expected. But I’ll take it.

**KATHY** (half-laugh, half-glare)
You think you’re a hero right now, don’t you?

**GILLEY**
Not a hero. Just a guy avoiding a veto.

*FADE OUT on Kathy shaking her head, Gilley leaning back smugly, and the rest of the band trying to decide if this is the most mature moment they’ve ever had—or the dumbest.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 4:54 P.M. – CONTINUOUS**

The breakup-because-democracy conversation is still settling. Kathy hasn’t said much—her eyes flicking between rage and shock. Then **Gilley**, ever the oblivious diplomat, decides to *clarify*.

**GILLEY**
I mean… I didn’t think we were, like, *dating* dating.

(He shrugs, casual as a breeze.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
I thought we were just, you know, *having sex*. Casual.  Fun, convenient. No drama.

**JEFF**
Oh *no*.

**JIM**
God help us.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
You absolute *dumbass*.

**BILL**
**Abort**. Backpedal. Reverse thrust.

But it’s too late. **Kathy doesn’t react outwardly.**  She doesn’t blink. Doesn’t flinch. She just gives him **a 10,000-foot stare**.  The kind of stare you give someone from orbit.  Not because you’re above them— but because you’re **done being on the same planet.**

Her jaw tightens. Her fingers flex once on the edge of the table.  And inside? She **seethes.** **Not a fire. A furnace.**  Roaring. Quiet. Pressurized. She looks at the Sharpie. Then back at Gilley. Then down at her notebook.

**KATHY (flat, calm)**
Noted.

(Beat.)

**GILLEY**
That’s… okay, right?

No one speaks.

**KATHY** (still calm)
I’m going to go stand outside.  For exactly two minutes.  And when I come back in, we are never speaking of this again.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Ever.

She stands. Smooth. Controlled. Walks out the garage door without a glance back.

**JEFF** (to Gilley)
You just nuked a volcano, man.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
It’s honestly impressive how well that went.

**GILLEY**
What? I was being honest.

**BILL**
Buddy, honesty’s not the problem.  *Timing* is.

*FADE OUT on Gilley sitting alone in the beanbag, suddenly realizing that the temperature in the garage just dropped ten degrees—and none of it is from the fan.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 4:56 P.M. – JUST AFTER KATHY WALKS OUT**

The room is dense with awkward. Nobody moves. Gilley shifts in the beanbag like he’s trying to pretend nothing happened.

Jeff finally breaks the silence.

**JEFF** (slow, pointed)
So what are you gonna do now, man?

**GILLEY** (grins, casual)
Same thing I always do.

(He stands up, stretches like a cat.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
Walk around in circles.  Talk in metaphors.  Hunt women.

(Beat. Absolute dead air.)

**JEFF**
…You wanna say that again?

**JIM**
Dude.

**BILL**
Sit down before you rupture the Geneva Conventions.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
You're gonna *die in this garage*.

**GILLEY**
What? It’s who I am.

**JEFF**
It’s not endearing.  It’s not philosophical.  It’s *self-immolation with a soundtrack*.

**GILLEY** (grinning)
But the soundtrack is *so good.*

He shrugs, unbothered, and casually paces a slow circle like nothing just imploded outside.

**JEFF**
You do realize she’s coming back in with that Bowie knife, right?

**GILLEY**
I’m counting on it. Keeps things interesting.

(Beat.)

**BILL**
God help us if she writes about you.

**JEFF**
Oh, she’s *absolutely* writing about him.

**JIM**
We should name the song "Track 3 (He's a Jackass)."

*FADE OUT on Gilley humming to himself as he walks the same loop around the garage, oblivious to the fact that his name may soon become an entire bridge section.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 4:58 P.M. – EXACTLY TWO MINUTES LATER**

The room hasn’t moved. Gilley’s still pacing like it’s all chill and metaphysical.  Jeremy’s scribbling in a notebook, mostly drawing flames.  Jeff is sitting with his head in his hand, the very image of regret. Then—**the side door opens.**

**KATHY** walks in.  Straight-backed. Dry-eyed. Not trembling.  Just… **compressed.**  Like someone who spent exactly 120 seconds counting her breath and **reloading composure round by round**. She stops at the edge of the table.

**KATHY**
Okay. Are we finished?

(Beat.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Are we finished **humiliating me**?

No one answers. Even Gilley, for once, **shuts his mouth**.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Is the spectacle over?  Or is someone else lining up to explain my emotional dysfunction to me like it’s a group project?

(Silence.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
I’m giving you this one chance. If there’s anything else to say, say it now.

(Beat. Nothing. Not even from Jim.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
No? Good. Let’s write.

(And with that, she sits. Calm. Composed. The lid sealed tight.)

*FADE OUT on everyone glancing around, then at their pages, knowing full well that **whatever song gets written next is going to have blood in it.***

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 4:59 P.M. – IMMEDIATELY AFTER**

Kathy has just sat back down, calm but seething, staring daggers into the table.

**KATHY**
Let’s write.

She opens her notebook. Pen uncapped. Then Jeff speaks.  Quiet. Level. No edge. But firm.

**JEFF**
It doesn’t work like that.

(She stops mid-stroke.)

**KATHY**
Why not?

(Jeff looks at her. Steady.)

**JEFF**
Because we’re gonna *vote*.

(Silence. **Kathy freezes.**)

**KATHY**
…Vote on what?

**JEFF**
On whether we’re actually moving on.  On whether we’re ready to write.

**KATHY**
You’re serious?

**JEFF**
This isn’t a dictatorship.  Not even a dramatic one.

(Beat. She’s not yelling. But she’s **horrified.**)

**KATHY**
You want to put me on trial?

**JEFF**
No. I want to put the *moment* to a vote.  Not you.  The moment.

(She leans back in her chair, stunned.)

**KATHY**
You’re going to make everyone *declare* whether they’re still mad at me?

**JEFF**
I’m going to make everyone declare if we’re ready to do the work.  Together.

(Beat.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
You said “Let’s write.”  I say—*let’s vote.*

The room holds its breath. **Kathy**—the fireball, the hurricane, the architect—**is suddenly not in control.** And that may be the most vulnerable thing that’s happened all day.

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 5:01 P.M. – SILENCE HANGING**

Jeff has just said, *Let’s vote.* Kathy looks stunned.  Nobody breathes. Then **Bill** clears his throat—**not emotional, not hesitant.** Just Bill.

**BILL**
I move that the matter be put to a vote.

(Beat. He glances around, giving anyone a chance to object. No one does.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
I vote in favor of prohibiting sexual relationships within the band structure. I believe this is a good idea.

(He nods. Notes it for himself.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
My voice has been heard.

**1–0.**

He leans back in his chair. And the room holds that number like a **match suspended over a powder keg.**

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 5:02 P.M. – IMMEDIATELY AFTER BILL’S VOTE**

The room is dead still. Bill’s voice has just landed. His vote: recorded. Calm. Clinical.

**BILL**
My voice has been heard. One–zero.

That’s when **Kathy snaps her pen shut**.  Looks directly at him. No flinch. No softness.

**KATHY**
Fuck off and die, bro.

(Silence. Sharp intake of breath from someone.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
That’s *one-to-one.*

(She leans back in her chair, arms folded, like a general who just shot back across a border.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
My voice. Heard. Count it.

**JEFF** (quietly, acknowledging)
One-to-one.

**GILLEY**
Oh, we are *deep* in the fire now.

**JIM**
No one move. No one breathe.

*FADE OUT on the table, the charter box, the numbers taking shape, and the band realizing that this isn’t just a vote—it’s **a referendum on trust, freedom, and whether they can survive the truth about each other.***

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 5:03 P.M. – THE VOTE CONTINUES**

Kathy’s “fuck off and die” is still vibrating in the air.  Bill has said yes. Kathy, no. All eyes shift to **Jeff**. He’s calm. Hands folded. Voice measured.

**JEFF**
You can’t control me.

(Beat.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
I understand the sentiment.  I understand the fear.  But I reject the exclusive nature of the motion.

(He looks at Jim. Then Bill. Then Kathy.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
I vote no.

(Beat.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
One of two. Against.

(Silence again.)

**BILL**
Vote recorded.

**JIM**
Okay then.

*FADE OUT on the room locked at 2–1 against. Tension rising. No one's moving a muscle. Not yet.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 5:04 P.M. – TENSION TIGHT**

Jeff has just voted no. Calm. Clean. Categorical.  Everyone looks to **Jim**. And Jim lets out a quiet, sardonic breath.  **Not angry. Just stunned.**

**JIM**
Control–you, Jeff?

(Beat.)

**JIM (CONT’D)**
Really? This sounds about ridiculous.  No—this *is* ridiculous.

**JEFF**
I’m not asking for anarchy. I’m saying we don’t preemptively legislate behavior out of fear.

**JIM**
No. What you’re saying is that **boundaries**—basic ones, rational ones—are somehow oppression.

(He shakes his head, frustrated.)

**JIM (CONT’D)**
We built a system to keep us together. This—this clause, this motion—it’s about *holding the band together*.  It’s not about purity tests. It’s about *not self-destructing because two people decided to hook up and then detonate on the rest of us like it's an encore.*

(Beat.)

**JIM (CONT’D)**
This isn't about your freedom, Jeff.  It's about *our stability.*

**JEFF**
You can’t protect the band by making rules that insult the people in it.

**JIM**
And you can’t pretend that sleeping together doesn’t come with consequences!

*FADE OUT on the standoff intensifying—Jeff calm, Jim coiled, and the vote still hanging in the balance.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 5:06 P.M. – CONTINUING THE VOTE**

Jeff and Jim have just clashed over freedom vs. stability. The room is vibrating with heat and judgment. Then—**Gilley stands**. Smooth. Grinning like a man delivering a eulogy with punchlines.

**GILLEY**
Gentlemen. Lady. Democracy.

(Silence.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
Let the record show: I am a man of many needs and limited self-restraint.

(Beat. He claps his hands once.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
So, with full acknowledgment of my past, present, and probable future behavior—I hereby commit to taking my sexual conduct… *into someone else's bed.*

(He does a tiny, mock bow.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
I vote yes.

(Beat.)

**BILL**
Vote recorded.  Two in favor.  Two opposed.

**KATHY**
You absolute *coward*.

**GILLEY**
Hey, I'm protecting the charter.  And my *testicles.*

*FADE OUT on Gilley sitting back down, smug, and the vote now locked at 2–2—with two left to cast, and everything on the line.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 5:07 P.M. – ALL EYES ON JEREMY**

The tally:  **2 in favor. 2 opposed. 2 left.**

**Jeremy Evans** slouches forward, rubbing his temples like he’s just been asked to mediate a nuclear standoff with a sock puppet.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
Alright. This is, without a doubt, the *last fucking thing* I thought I’d have to weigh in on today.

(He gestures around.)

**JEREMY (EVANS) (CONT’D)**
I came here to maybe work on a bridge section. Instead, I’m now voting on whether I can—or cannot—*hypothetically* have sex with our lead singer, while trying to not offend half the band or start a constitutional crisis.

(Beat. He exhales.)

**JEREMY (EVANS) (CONT’D)**
So. Here’s what I think: This rule?  It’s a bad idea. Not because it’s immoral.  Not because people aren’t messy.  But because it **preemptively** punishes the idea of trust.

(He points at the charter pizza box.)

**JEREMY (EVANS) (CONT’D)**
We just wrote down that this thing runs on trust and vote and freedom. And now we’re trying to throttle that freedom *because one of us doesn’t like where someone else put their lapida.*

(Silence. Kathy blinks.)

**JEFF**
Did you just use lapida in a sentence?

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
Yes, and I’m not proud of it.

(He squares his shoulders.)

**JEREMY (EVANS) (CONT’D)**
Here’s the truth: if any of us wants to have sex with Kathy, and she wants to have sex with us, and it’s consensual and honest and not screwing over the band—that’s called *free will.*

(Beat.)

**JEREMY (EVANS) (CONT’D)**
You don’t vote away consent.

(He leans forward.)

**JEREMY (EVANS) (CONT’D)**
I’m casting the decisive vote.

(He looks at Jim. Then Bill. Then Kathy.)

**JEREMY (EVANS) (CONT’D)**
And this is gonna go down in flames.

(Beat.)

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
No.

**BILL**
Vote recorded.

**JEFF**
Three to two.

**BILL**
The motion fails.

**JIM**
Goddammit.

**KATHY** (quiet, razor-edged)
Good boy.

*FADE OUT on the charter, the circle of faces, and the heavy knowledge that the band just survived its first civil war—but only just.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 5:08 P.M. – POST-VOTE AFTERSHOCK**

The motion has just failed. Three against, two in favor.  The room is still buzzing with the heat of it.

**Jeremy (Evans)** is sitting there, a little proud, a little shaky, still recovering from making *the* deciding vote.

And then—

**KATHY** (flat)
Jer, did you mean *libido*?

(Beat.)

Jeremy blinks.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
As in your **sexual desire**?  **Libido**?

(Silence. Gilley starts chuckling.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Aren’t you taking the **ACT** next month?

**JEREMY (EVANS)** (sinking into his chair)
God *damn* it.

**JEFF**
You said “Lapida,” bro.

**JIM**
Which I’m pretty sure is either a Star Wars character or a species of fish.

**BILL**
In Spanish it means “gravestone.”

**GILLEY**
So… poetic in a way?

**KATHY**
Honestly, kind of accurate.

(Beat. She stares at Jeremy.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
You tried to make a high-minded defense of sexual liberty and accidentally told me you wanted to bang me *from the grave.*

(Everyone breaks. Laughter—tense, tired, but real.)

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
Forget it. I resign. I’m going to vocational school.

*FADE OUT on the first laugh of the day, the vote behind them, and six exhausted humans remembering that democracy might be brutal—but it’s never boring.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 5:09 P.M. – POST-LAUGHTER PAUSE**

Laughter is dying down. Jeremy’s slouched in his chair, Gilley’s still smiling, Bill’s back to neutral. Kathy’s eyes narrow.  She’s scanning the room.  She’s counting.  Then she speaks—low, sharp, and direct.

**KATHY**
Wait a second.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
There are **six** of us in this band.  We got five votes.

(Dead silence.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Somebody’s **dodging**.

(Beat. She looks around the room, one by one. Her tone hardens.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
That smells like **cowardice**.

**JEFF** (quiet)
She’s right.

**BILL**
Roll call.

**KATHY** (louder, not yelling—*commanding*)
Who hasn’t voted?

(Jeremy raises his hand.)

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
I voted.

**JEFF**
I did.

**KATHY**
Me.

**GILLEY**
Yup.

**BILL**
Obviously.

All eyes turn to **Jim**.

**JIM** (flat)
I motioned the vote. I didn’t cast one.

**KATHY**
That’s not how this works.  This is a democracy, remember?

**GILLEY**
Come on, man. Step up. Don’t be the one guy who throws the grenade and ducks out of the blast radius.

**JEFF**
You started this. Finish it.

**KATHY**
Yeah.  Let’s hear it.

*FADE OUT as Jim stares at the table, the pizza box charter, and the faces around him—waiting. Watching. Demanding that he finally **own what he started.***

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 5:10 P.M. – STILL WAITING ON JIM**

All eyes are on him. The vote's been cast. The room’s scorched. Kathy just called out the missing ballot.

**JEFF**
You started this, man. Finish it.

**KATHY**
Let’s hear it.

Jim leans forward, resting his arms on the table, and **delivers a line he clearly thinks is Socratic wisdom**.

**JIM**
On a scale from one to epically, completely, stupidly bad…

(Beat.)

**JIM (CONT’D)**
…having sex on the same golf course as the people who own the means of production is…suboptimal.

(Dead silence.)

**KATHY (flatly)**
What?

**GILLEY**
Hold up.

**JEFF**
Golf course?

**BILL**
You lost me at “epically.”

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
Are *we* the means of production? Or is Kathy the golf course?

**KATHY**
I—

(stops, blinks)
I can’t even—Like, I was ready to be mad, but that was so incoherent I’m *stuck.*

(Beat. She squints at Jim.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
That metaphor doesn’t make any sense *whatsoever*.

(She points at him.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
I’m not angry. I’m just… **struggling**.

**GILLEY**
What does that even mean? Are we putting on cleats and ruining the greens?

**JEFF**
Is Gilley the caddy? Or the cart?

**KATHY**
I think I’m the sand trap. I *feel* like the sand trap.

**JIM**
You’re all being deliberately obtuse.

**KATHY**
No. You’re being **deliriously abstract.**

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
We need a glossary for your votes.

**KATHY**
Give us a straight answer, Jim. Not a Kafkaesque *par three*.

*FADE OUT on Jim looking cornered, Kathy staring like she’s trying to decipher a burnt-out circuit board, and the whole band spiraling into absurdism until he says one word: “yes” or “no.”*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 5:12 P.M. – THE TABLE WAITS**

Kathy still hasn’t blinked since Jim mentioned golf courses. Everyone else is locked in an awkward blend of confusion and anticipation. Then—Jim exhales.

**JIM**
Alright. Let’s say—

(Beat. He squares his shoulders.)

**JIM (CONT’D)**
I’m firmly in favor of no intraband sex.

(Silence.)

**BILL**
That’s a yes vote.

**JEFF**
Three in favor, three against.

**KATHY**
Deadlock.

**GILLEY**
The charter didn’t account for ties.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
Then we’re officially in a constitutional crisis. Fantastic.

**KATHY**
No.  We’re not!

(Everyone turns to her.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
A tie means it **doesn’t pass**.  That’s how supermajority works.  We said four out of six.

**BILL**
Yeah.

**JEFF**
The motion fails.

(Beat. Kathy rises—slow, precise. She doesn’t gloat. She doesn’t explode. She just **smiles. Once. Sharp as a blade.**)

**KATHY**
And now…*Now*, we write.

*FADE OUT on the pizza box charter in the middle of the table, still intact, still smudged, and now marked with its first true failure to pass. The system held. Barely.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 7:14 P.M. – TWILIGHT BLEEDING THROUGH THE RAFTERS**

The table is littered with scribbles, crumpled drafts, one half-eaten bag of pretzels, and the still-visible **grease-glossed charter box**. The war is over, and in its place is something quieter.

**KATHY** (staring at a blank page, almost a whisper)
I’m kind of happy right now.

(Heads turn. Eyebrows rise. No one speaks.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Like, not in a fairytale way.  But this—*this* feels like we survived something.  Like we’re actually doing it.

Maybe we should write about that.

(Beat.)

**JEFF** (same tone, but deadpan)
No one’s ever going to be happy.

**JIM**
There it is.

**JEFF**
Happiness is a lie.  It’s manufactured by greeting cards and pharmaceutical company marketing teams.

(He scratches something down.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
But *authenticity*—That’s what we got to go for.  Even if it’s ugly.

**KATHY** (grinning, dry)
Of course. Silly me.  I forgot we’re legally required to suffer for our art.

**GILLEY** (quietly, pacing)
We’re not suffering. We’re fermenting.

(Beat.)

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
Can we put that on a shirt?

**BILL**
*“We’re not suffering. We’re fermenting.”*  First merch drop. Write it down.

**JEFF**
Only if the font is moldy and the shirt smells like rehearsal socks.

**KATHY**
Stop.  I’m writing.

*She puts pen to page. The others fall into a quiet shuffle. There’s still tension—but there’s laughter under it now. There’s momentum. And maybe, just maybe, the bones of a song.*

*FADE OUT on the click of Kathy’s pen and the first scribbled lyric that might just save them from themselves.*

---

# **CHAPTER FIVE: EVERY LINE IN YOUR PALM**

---
## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 7:46 P.M. – HALF AN HOUR INTO WRITING**

The table’s quieter now. Less tension. More pencil scratches. Kathy’s in her notebook. Bill is hunched over a synth chart. Jeremy (Evans) is drawing a rough chord diagram. Gilley’s circling the perimeter like a coyote on Adderall. And then—

**Jeff speaks. Not loudly. Not performatively.**  He just says it like it’s already printed on the inside of his skull.

**JEFF**
*Underneath the neon lights,*
*we find our secret place.*
*Heart beats racing faster—*
*I pull you closer… adjust the taste.*

(Everything stops.)

**KATHY** (slowly looking up)
Say that again?

**JEFF**
*Underneath the neon lights,*
*we find our secret place.*
*Heart beats racing faster—*
*I pull you closer, adjust the taste.*

(Beat. Gilley actually stops pacing.)

**BILL**
That's… better than anything on this table.

**JIM**
I was not ready to be impressed.  Now I’m angry.

**KATHY**
Adjust the taste?

**JEFF**
Yeah. Could be anything. Could be a drink. Could be… us.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
Could be both.  Tastes like danger and poor decisions.

**GILLEY**
Tastes like what we weren’t supposed to survive.  But somehow did.

**KATHY** (write-scribbling fast)
Don’t move. Don’t breathe.  Nobody screw this up.

**JEFF**
Too late. It’s on paper.

(Beat.)

*And just like that—**the first real lyric**. Not born from rage. Not forced.*  *Just pulled from the moment.*  *Clean. Lived. Sharp.*

*FADE OUT on Jeff holding the pen now. Not just contributing. Leading.*  *And nobody questions it yet.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 7:48 P.M. – THE LYRIC ON THE TABLE**

The band is still processing what Jeff just dropped. Kathy’s scribbling. Jeremy’s humming a half-melody. Bill’s watching the words with clinical fascination. And **Gilley**, mid-pace, suddenly stops.

**GILLEY**
You don’t adjust the taste of a pussy.

(The entire garage freezes again.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
You just accept it.

(Beat.)

**KATHY**
Jesus, Gilley.

**JEFF**
Are you—*what* are you doing?

**GILLEY**
Listen—seriously.  You wrote: *I pull you closer, adjust the taste.*  But that feels…calculated. Like the protagonist’s being sneaky.  Like he’s trying to fine-tune a *moment*.

(He steps closer, voice quieter now. No grin. All focus.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
But if you change it to *just accept the taste*— Now he’s honest.  Raw. Vulnerable. **Me.**

**JEFF** (quietly, absorbing it)
*"I pull you closer, just accept the taste."*

**BILL**
Damn.

**KATHY**
Intriguing.

**JIM**
Hate that he is. But yeah.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
Okay but also, like… wow.

**GILLEY**
I'm not always helpful. But when I am? I *cut through bullshit.*

**KATHY** (staring at the page)
Yeah.  Yeah, that’s better.

*FADE OUT on the updated lyric, heavier now, sharper—because Gilley saw the mask in the line and ripped it off. And for once, nobody’s mad about it.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 7:49 P.M. – THE LINE IN QUESTION**

Gilley’s just dropped his interpretation—suggesting “*just accept the taste*.” The room absorbed it like a slap of cold water. But **Jeff holds his ground**. Calm. Unshaken. Clear.

**JEFF**
Nope.

(He taps the page once. Not angry. Just certain.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
That’s not gonna work.

(Beat.)

**GILLEY**
Why not? It’s honest.

**JEFF**
No—it’s *yours*. And that’s not what I meant.

(He leans forward slightly, pen in hand.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
If that’s what we’re talking about, then the line isn’t *adjust the taste.*  It’s—

(He rewrites it aloud.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
*I pull you closer. Just a taste.*

(Beat.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
It’s physical. Intentional.  Like you're grabbing someone by her ass. Bringing them in.  *Preparing.*

(Silence. The room gets still.)

**KATHY**
That hits harder.  Sharper rhythm. More agency.

**JIM**
It also makes the line breathe better.

**GILLEY**
So you’re keeping the control in the hands of the protagonist?

**JEFF**
No.  I’m keeping the honesty in the moment.  Not every line’s a metaphor.  Some lines are just *what happened.*

(Beat.)

**GILLEY**
Respect.

(He nods once, genuinely.)

*FADE OUT on the revision inked into the notebook:*  *“I pull you closer. Just a taste.”*  *The lyric lives now—balanced between Jeff’s precision and Gilley’s instinct, **crafted in tension, not compromise.***

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 7:52 P.M. – WRITING MOMENTUM**

Jeff’s eyes are on the page, but he’s not reading. He’s *speaking*. Low. Fluid. Like the lines have already been rehearsed in his bloodstream.

**JEFF**
*You’re the fire in my veins,*
*igniting every spark.*
*With every whispered promise—*
*you are the song that I want to spark.*

(Beat. Pen glides across the paper as he says it.)

**KATHY** (murmured)
Holy shit.

**JIM**
That’s… almost too good.

**GILLEY**
No such thing. Keep going.

**BILL**
We’ve got pulse. We’ve got a build.  Now we just need the fracture.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
You just wrote a heartbeat with a knife in it.

**JEFF** (quiet)
Yeah.

(He lifts his pen. Lets it hover.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
That’s the problem.  I don’t know what comes next.  Not yet.

**KATHY**
You just opened the door.  We’ll walk through it.

*FADE OUT on the line inked into the middle of the notebook like it’s glowing:*  **“You are the song that I want to spark.”**

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 7:53 P.M. – RIGHT AFTER JEFF’S LINE**

The room is still glowing with what Jeff just laid down. “You are the song that I want to spark.” He sets the pen down like it might burn through the table. And then—**Gilley snaps his fingers twice**. Focused.

**GILLEY**
Nope.

(Jeff blinks.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
I can’t sing that.

**JEFF**
What?

**GILLEY**
*“Want to spark”?*  It’s too stiff. It’s beautiful, yeah. But it’s *precious.*  You want this to be a feeling, not a fable.

**JEFF**
It’s supposed to be tight.

**GILLEY**
It’s supposed to be *felt.*

(Beat.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
*“You’re the song that I wanna spark.”*

**JEFF**
Wanna?

**GILLEY**
Yeah. *Wanna.*  You’re not writing a perfect story.  You’re selling an **emotion**.  Real people don’t *“want to”* in a moment like that.  They *wanna.*

(Silence. She lets it sit.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
This isn't a novel. It's a lyric.  It has to roar.

**BILL**
He’s right.  "*Wanna*" hits like a punch in the teeth.  "*Want to*" is… *adjacent to a nap.*

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
You guys are monsters. I’m never writing a lyric again.

**JEFF** (smiling despite himself)
“*Wanna*,” huh?

**KATHY**
Write it. Then sing it. You’ll feel the difference.

(Beat.)

Jeff crosses it out, rewrites: **“You are the song that I wanna spark.”**

**JEFF**
Fine. But if this turns into a pop single, it’s your fault.

**KATHY**
You’re welcome.

*FADE OUT on Jeff’s clean line now marked with her correction—stronger, less refined, but real. Like everything they’re finally learning to become.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 7:56 P.M. – POST-EDIT GLOW**

Kathy’s correction has landed.  Jeff’s lyric is sharper now.  The page breathes. Then **Bill looks up from his corner**, calmly pulling the lid off his synth case.

**BILL**
I do wanna turn this into a pop single.

(Everyone turns. Blank stares.)

**KATHY**
…what?

**BILL**
Dead serious. What’s more *punk* than taking something *pop*…and making it *punk*?

(Beat.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
Or taking something *punk* and turning it *pop*?

(He folds his arms. Completely unfazed.)

**JEFF**
Bill, are you—are you *on peyote*?

**JIM**
You’re talking like you just got back from a vision quest in Joshua Tree.

**JEREMY**
Or listening to *Joshua Tree* backwards.
*"You wait for I*
*Side your twisted thorn in the sea*
*Your eyes set in stone, the sea…"

**GILLEY**
Are we about to start selling perfume and playing Super Bowl halftime?

**BILL**
It’s inversion. It’s theft.  It’s transformation.  That’s the *most* punk thing we could possibly do.

(He shrugs.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
Weaponize polish.

**KATHY**
…Shit.

**JEFF**
Okay. He might be right.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
I think I need to sit down.

**GILLEY**
You are sitting.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
Then I need to *sit lower.*

*FADE OUT on Bill plugging in his synth with monk-like stillness, while the others stare like he just explained time travel using a soda can. Because maybe—maybe—he did.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 7:57 P.M. – MOMENTS AFTER BILL’S COMMENT**

Everyone is still reeling from Bill’s line. *“Weaponize polish.”* They’re stunned. Trying to process it. But **Kathy’s not stunned. She’s smitten.** She leans back in her chair, exhales like she just tasted something perfect, and smiles.

**KATHY**
I am absolutely *enamored* with that phrase.

**JEFF**
Weaponize polish?

**KATHY**
Yeah.

(She nods, slow, thoughtful—then delivers it like a deathblow.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
If I ever got a tattoo—*ever*—that’s what it’d be.  Right beneath one of my tits.

(Everyone reacts in staggered silence.)

**JIM**
…What?

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
Like, weaponized *underboob*?

**GILLEY**
That’s a merch design. That’s *album art*.

**BILL**
I accept this honor with grace and mild horror.

**KATHY**
No, but seriously.

(She points at Bill.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
That phrase? That’s the thesis statement for what we’re doing.  Make it clean. Make it sharp.  Then *slice someone open with it.*

**JEFF**
Jesus.

**KATHY**
*Weaponize polish.*  That's the mission. That’s *everything.*

*FADE OUT on Kathy grinning at the lyric sheet, one hand scribbling again, the other resting casually against her ribs—where the phrase might one day live in ink, just beneath her skin.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 8:04 P.M. – THE AIR IS STILL ELECTRIC**

The lyric sheet is half full. Everyone’s working—burned, bonded, bruised. A fragile kind of synergy is holding them together. **Jeff** looks up from his notebook, eyes settling on **Kathy** across the table. His voice is soft, but direct.

**JEFF**
How cutting do you want me to be?

(Beat.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
For the rest of my life?

(Everyone stops—subtly. No one interrupts.)

Kathy doesn’t answer right away. She sits back. Thinks. The pen taps her thigh in rhythm. Then she leans in, voice low but absolutely clear.

**KATHY**
