I prefer a stiletto.

(She lets it hang.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Stab someone in the front.  Right in the gut.  No surprises. Just precision.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
But—

(She nods at him.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
If you want to use a battle-axe? Be my guest. Chop someone to pieces.  Chop *me* to pieces.  Chop your own dick off if it makes the point land.  Just… **wield it.**

(Dead silence.)

**GILLEY**
We are so writing that into the bridge.

**JIM**
I don’t even know what genre this is anymore. But I’m afraid to stop it.

**BILL**
It’s surgical violence with melody.  Keep going.

**JEFF** (writing as he speaks)
Battleaxe lyrics. No backing down.

**KATHY**
Just don’t miss.

*FADE OUT on the table, now a war room—no illusions left, no pretenses. Just six people forging blades out of lyrics, and learning exactly how sharp they’re willing to be.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 8:07 P.M. – AFTER KATHY’S BATTLEAXE DECLARATION**

Pens are moving. The room is throbbing with creative heat.  Then **Gilley stops pacing**. Stands dead center. One hand in the air like he’s asking for silence in a cathedral.

**GILLEY**
Okay. Okay. Just—hear me out.

(They all look up. He’s not smiling. He’s lit up.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
If we’re gonna write about sex…love…affection…

(He gestures broadly, circling the table.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
Then we have to **dare** to be vile.  We have to be strident. Graphic. Obscene. Raw.  We don’t flirt with discomfort—we *barrel through it.*

(Beat. He’s locked in.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
It’s 1990.  Not 1976.  We don’t need permission anymore.  We need to **dare to be—**

(He stops. The words snag in his throat.)

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
What, Gilley?

(Beat.)

**GILLEY**
Truth tellers.

(Silence.)

**JEFF**
Yeah.

**KATHY**
Fucking right we do.

**JIM**
God help the truth when we’re done with it.

**BILL**
Truth isn’t the goal. It’s the *material.*

**GILLEY**
Exactly.

*FADE OUT on Gilley stepping back into his orbit, pacing again—but now the whole room is aligned with him. The lyric isn't just a song anymore. It’s a dare.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 8:09 P.M. – THE TRUTH DARE HAS JUST BEEN SPOKEN**

Gilley’s truth-teller manifesto still hangs in the air.

Everyone’s quiet. Focused. And then **Jeff looks up**—calm, certain, notebook still in his lap.

**JEFF**
You want to know what tone we’re chasing?

(They all look.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
*Love and Affection.*  Off the new Def Leppard album.

(Beat. Someone snorts.)

**KATHY**
Seriously?

**JEFF**
Dead serious.

(He sits forward.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
Listen to it. Really listen.  Yeah, it’s got that shimmer. That ‘80s arena gloss.  But *underneath*?  It’s cold.  It’s surgical.  It’s like someone smiling while they tell you they’ll never need you again.

**BILL**
Yeah!  He's right.

**JEFF**
It’s a break-up song dressed as a seduction.  It cuts *through* affection to get to the power dynamic underneath.

**GILLEY**
And that’s the line we ride.

**JEFF**
Exactly.  Not the sound. The **message**.

**KATHY**
Polish it. Weaponize it.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
Put a dagger in the harmony.

**JIM**
Use the bridge as an execution chamber.

**JEFF**
Yes.  That’s the tone.  That’s where we live.

*FADE OUT on heads nodding, pens scribbling, and the unspoken agreement that if a band like Def Leppard can slip a scalpel into a chorus, **then so can they.***

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 8:12 P.M. – THE WRITING TABLE**

Kathy is flipping back through the latest draft, marking changes. Jeff’s eyes flick toward her. He watches her read, just long enough to know *she’s waiting for him to say something.*

Then, without lifting his voice, he leans forward and speaks.

**JEFF**
*With every whispered promise…*

(She glances up.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
*You're the song I wanna start.*

(Beat.)

He holds eye contact. Doesn’t blink.

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
Pay attention, Kathy.  I said *wanna*, not *want.*  *Wanna.*

(He tilts his head, deadpan.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
Happy now?

(Beat.)

**KATHY** (smiling slowly, not looking away)
Almost.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Try it again. Louder.

*FADE OUT on Jeff grinning despite himself, the rest of the band watching like they’re watching a knife fight that might also be a duet—and maybe, somehow, a love story too.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 8:14 P.M. – MOMENT OF CALM**

The band’s working. The energy has shifted from volatile to charged. Lyrics are building. The first chorus is close.  Jeff is leaning back in his chair, relaxed, pen in hand, notebook open—but he hasn’t written anything down in five minutes.  He’s just… *sitting there*. Looking slightly bored. Maybe a little smug.

**JIM** (eyebrows knitting)
Okay, what the hell, man.

**JEFF**
Hm?

**JIM**
How are you *doing* this?  You’re just sitting there, looking sly, looking bored.  And then you drop a perfect fucking lyric out of nowhere like you *overheard it*.

(Beat.)

**JEFF** (quietly, not looking up)
I kind of do.

**JIM**
Come again?

Jeff leans forward, taps the side of his head.

**JEFF**
The words… they just—I see them.  Like they’re on a chalkboard.  Big, block letters. Real clean. Like someone already wrote them.

(Silence.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
I just read them back.

(Beat.)

**KATHY**
God, I hate you.

**GILLEY**
No—*worship* him. He’s the sacred projector.

**BILL**
That’s a neurological event. Not a talent.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
I once thought I had that, but it turned out to be a Pop-Tart commercial.

**JEFF** (chuckling)
Look, I don’t know how it works.  But when it’s quiet enough in here—*points to his temple*—it’s like the words are already waiting.

**JIM**
Well.  Fuck your chalkboard.

(He goes back to tuning his snare.)

*FADE OUT on Jeff blinking, glancing at the page, and reading something only he can see—until the rest of the band catches up and turns it into a song.*

---

##  **INT.JIM’S HEAD – INTERNAL MONOLOGUE – BLARING**

*Jeff leans back. Says a line like he’s ordering coffee.*  *Everyone stares like he just parted the sea.*  *Kathy scribbles it. Bill nods. Jeremy laughs. Gilley paces and echoes it like it’s scripture.*

**JIM (INTERNAL)**
Oh my god. He’s doing it again.  He just *did it again.* That wasn’t a lyric. That was an airstrike.  How the hell is he sitting there, looking like he’s half asleep, and then suddenly

**BOOM.**

It’s not even flair. It’s not loud.  It’s like a countdown in his head.

***5…***
He taps the table.

***4…***
He fidgets with his pen.

***3…***
He breathes through his nose like he’s annoyed.

***2…***
He tilts his head to the side. Looks bored.

***1…***
And then it comes out like the voice of God after a smoke break.

*Detonation.*

***“You are the song that I wanna start.”***

And the rest of us?  We’re playing in the wreckage, acting like we helped build the bomb. I hate this.  I hate that I *can’t* hate him.  Because it’s beautiful.  It’s *fucking beautiful*.  And I’m sitting here with calluses and caffeine and a heart full of rhythm—but nothing to say.  And that terrifies me.  Because what if that’s all I am?  A metronome. A mechanic.  Not a creator.

What if I don’t belong in this band?  What if they figure it out?  What if I’m the only one who already has?

**(FADE BACK TO THE GARAGE)**

Jeff is staring at the page.  Kathy is nodding slowly.  Gilley is pacing again, smiling.  And **Jim**?  He’s looking at his sticks like they might never be enough.

---

##  **INT.GILLEY’S GARAGE – 8:17 P.M. – SONG IN MOTION**

Jeff’s staring into space again—*that chalkboard look*. Then, suddenly, he jolts forward and starts speaking, like he’s narrating the machinery in his head.

**JEFF**
I’m thinking real rapid.  *Staccato* drum intro.  Fast. Tight. Clipped. Like— **rat-tat-tat.**

(He drums on the tabletop, fast but featherlight.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
And gated. Like Collins gated. *Soft* but explosive. Real gated.

**(He looks straight at Jim.)**

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
Real rapid. Real soft. Real gated.

**(beat)**
I think you can pull that off.

**JIM**  (quiet, flat)
I’m using it on my kit. Not a machine.

**BILL**
That’s a whole lot of drum noise.

**JIM**
Yeah.

(He looks up—eyes sharp, voice rising with conviction.)

**JIM (CONT’D)**
That’s the *entire point*.

(He taps his sticks against his palm like he’s winding up for war.)

**JIM (CONT’D)**
We’re talking about a guy who’s *considering* going down on a woman.  And in *his* mind, if that ever happens, that moment?  It’s gonna be **spectacular**.  So we don’t tiptoe into the verse.  **We announce it.**  We **announce** the *whole damn song* with authority.

**JEFF**
Exactly.

**KATHY** (chuckling under her breath)
I’m so glad this band is 50% poetry, 50% sexual panic.

**GILLEY**
That's why it works.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
Okay, but do I *write that line* or just let the drums say it?

**JEFF**
You let the drums scream it.

*FADE OUT on Jim tapping a rapid-fire fill into the air, finally *seeing* what the others see—that he might just be more than a timekeeper. He might be the *detonator.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 8:19 P.M. – BUILDING THE FRAME**

Jim is still tapping that rapid fill in midair. Kathy’s pacing now, notebook open, muttering phrases under her breath like she’s loading rounds.  Bill’s got a synth powered up, fingers hovering.  Jeff raises a hand—not to stop them, but to **focus them**.

**JEFF**
There’s no guitar riff here.

(Everyone looks over.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
Not quite yet.  This? This is all **synths and drums**.  Hard staccato.  Cold atmosphere.  And Kathy’s **spitting out words** like they’re **bullets.**

**GILLEY**
Like she’s got something to prove?

**KATHY**
Like I’ve already proved it, and now I’m cleaning up.

**JIM**
So we’re launching this with rhythm and venom.

**JEFF**
Exactly.  The guitar part’s coming.  That’s **later**—when we’ve earned it.  When the room’s *begging* for it.

(Beat.)
Right now?  Let the drums and synths talk.  Let Kathy hit first.

**BILL**
We’ll use guitar as a weapon. Not a foundation.

**JEFF**
Correct.

**KATHY**
Then stand back.

(Beat. She rolls her shoulders.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
'Cause I’m about to open fire.

*FADE OUT as synth tones start to swell, Jim’s snare clicks into that staccato countdown, and Kathy breathes once—then dives into the first line like a gunshot.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 8:22 P.M. – LYRIC FUSE BURNING**

The drums are mapped. The synth is humming. Kathy is pacing, prepping her opening salvo. And Jeff—still sitting there, calm as ever—leans forward and speaks **like he’s narrating something already burned into memory.**

**JEFF**
*I huffed, still trying to catch my breath.*
*But in your wild embrace—*

I forget the rest.

(Beat. A glint in his eye.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
*Get ready, babe.*

(He smiles.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
*I’ll get you back for that.*

(Dead silence. Then—**Kathy explodes.**)

**KATHY**
Jesus *fucking* Christ—

(Hands in the air, half-laughing, half-furious.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
You’re doing this in *real time* now, Jeff?!?

**JEFF** (chill as hell)
Seems like it.

**GILLEY**
We’ve officially crossed into divine possession.

**JIM**
He’s not writing lyrics. He’s testifying.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
I’m just here for the fireworks and the emotional scarring.

**BILL**
Please tell me someone is recording.

**KATHY**
That’s not fair. That’s *not fucking fair.*

(Beat. She grins, furious and awed.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Keep going!

*FADE OUT on Jeff flipping to a new page, pen already moving, as Kathy stares at him like he just raised the dead—and maybe, just maybe, wrote her into immortality.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 8:26 P.M. – THE LINE JUST LANDED**

Jeff, still channeling, lets the next lyric fall out like breath.

**JEFF**
*You laugh like thunder.*
*It’s a playful chat.*

(Beat.)

**GILLEY**
So it’s like… two lovers having fun? Not two lovers hating each other and, y'know… *fucking?*

**JEFF**
Yeah. That’s it.  **Fun.**

**KATHY**  (stops cold)
*Fun*?

(Beat.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Fun… *question mark*?

**JEFF** (grinning now)
Yeah. *Fun.*  They’re **delighted**.  He **can’t wait** to lick her cunt.

(Beat. No one moves.)

**GILLEY** (laughs under his breath)
So it’s a devotional anthem.  Just… wet.

**JIM**
You people are insane.

**BILL**
And yet we’re tracking this.

**JEFF**
You don’t write a track like this with guilt.  You write it with **grin and fire**.

**KATHY** (nods, dead serious)
Then make sure the chorus sounds like *heaven’s doors opening and someone’s about to moan.*

**JEFF**
On it.

*FADE OUT on the room tilting toward the chorus—fully committed, filthy with clarity, and finally telling the truth like it’s the only thing they’ve ever had to sell.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 8:29 P.M. – LIGHTS LOW, TENSION HIGH**

They’ve been building to this. The synths are pulsing. Jim’s kit is armed. Kathy’s mouth is half open like she’s about to sing—but then **Jeff starts talking again.**  Not loud.  Not confident.  Just… **inevitable**.

**JEFF**
*Lust is a game we play.*
*With every touch, you lead the way.*

*Sara, you're my sweetest thrill.*
*In your arms, time stands still.*

*I’ll lose control.*
*I won’t look back.*

*With every moment—*
*we're on the attack!!*

(Beat.)

**And then silence.**  Everyone stares.  Even the fans seem to slow.

**JIM** (quiet)
You just did that in one take.

**GILLEY**
That wasn’t a lyric. That was a séance.

**KATHY**
You *whispered with God.*

**BILL**
He spoke back.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
This is why you terrify me, big bro.

**JEFF** (shrugging)
It’s just what was there.

**KATHY**
You wrote a chorus for people to *fuck to* and *cry to* at the same time.

**JEFF**
Then we’re doing it right.

(Beat.)

**KATHY**
Say it again.  Exactly as it came.

*FADE OUT on the page being inked, the air crackling like divine static, and the band silently realizing: this song’s not about power or rebellion anymore.*

**It’s about desire.**  **And they just nailed it.**

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 8:32 P.M. – POST-CHORUS AFTERGLOW**

The air is still reverberating from Jeff’s line.  Kathy has the pen poised.  Everyone’s staring at Jeff like he just caught lightning in his bare hands.  And then—

**JEFF**
Yeah. It’s about two gay women.

(Everyone freezes.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
Oh, and Sara? No H.

(Beat.)

**JIM**
Wait.

**KATHY**
*What?*

**BILL**
Why… why no H?

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
I don’t—what just happened?

**GILLEY**
Hold up.  *What happened to the dick in the song?!*

**JEFF**
There was never a dick. That was your projection.

(Chaos erupts.)

**JIM**
The line about licking her—*you wrote that.*

**JEFF**
Still applies.

**KATHY** (to Gilley)
Wait, did you *need* there to be a dick?

**GILLEY**
I didn’t *need* it! I just assumed there’d be one! I thought Jeff was the narrator!

**JEFF**
I’m the voice. Doesn’t mean it’s me.

**BILL**
So this is a female narrator?

**JEFF**
Yeah. She’s in love with Sara. No H. She’s confident. She’s obsessed. She’s real.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
We’ve been building a lesbian sex anthem and you’re *just now* telling us?

**JEFF**
What difference does it make?

**KATHY** (sharp, impressed)
*All* the difference.

(She grins.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
That changes *everything.*

**JIM**
Honestly, I feel kind of stupid now.

**GILLEY**
I feel *betrayed.*

**JEFF**
You should feel *enlightened.*

**KATHY**
Write her name again. Bigger. Top of the page.

**JEFF** (quietly, writing)
*Sara. No H.*

*FADE OUT on the band all talking at once—some still catching up, some already reimagining the structure, and Jeff, serene in the middle of it all, reshaping truth into sound while they scramble to understand it.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 8:34 P.M. – POST-SARA REVEAL, CONFUSION IN FULL BLOOM**

Jeff’s just written *Sara (no H)* across the top of the page.  The band is still talking over each other, but **Gilley raises a hand** like a kid in a civics class with a very complicated question.

**GILLEY**
Okay. Wait. Hold up.

Everyone quiets.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
What kind of lesbians are we talking about here?

(Blank stares.)

**JIM**
*Jesus.*

**GILLEY**
No, seriously. Like—are we talking about the chicks you see on *Skinemax*?  Or are we talking about *real* chicks?  Because that makes a difference.

**KATHY**
To *whom?*

**GILLEY**
To *me*! To the listener! There’s a vibe shift!

**JEFF**
Please elaborate. We are all *morbidly* curious.

**GILLEY**
Okay so…look.  One of them you lust after because they’re like…oiled up and fake and moving in slow motion with softcore jazz in the background.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
Skinned knees. Vaseline on the lens.

**GILLEY**
Exactly.  The *other* kind?  They’re real. Like, they *look* at each other like the world ends when the other one blinks.  And you still lust after them, but it’s a different kind of lust.

(Beat. He gestures vaguely.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
It’s… *existential*. You want to be inside their story, not just in the room.  It’s like watching religion on fire.

(Everyone stares.)

**KATHY**
…Did you just become a poet?

**BILL**
He stumbled face-first into gender studies and came out with a thesis.

**JEFF**
And he’s not wrong.

**KATHY**
He’s annoying. But he’s not wrong.

**GILLEY**
So which is it?

**JEFF**
They’re the second kind.

(Beat.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
It’s real.  It’s messy.  It’s *devotion* at a thousand volts.

**KATHY**
Then give me the mic.

(Everyone freezes.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Because I know exactly how that sounds.

*FADE OUT on the band falling silent as Kathy stands—no smile, no theatrics—just **ready**. Because this song just found its soul. And its voice.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 8:37 P.M. – THE AIR STILL CHARGED**

Kathy’s last line lands hard:

**KATHY**
I’m the one with the mic.

(Beat. Gilley blinks. And then, with a weird, boyish reverence—)

**GILLEY**
That’s the most precious thing I’ve ever heard.

(Beat.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
That’s real big dick energy.  No lie. I absolutely respect it.

(He holds up his hands, surrendering.)

**KATHY** (smiling slowly, tight)
Well…I don’t exactly have a big dick.  But I appreciate your sentiment.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
I understand where your *dinosaur-sized brain* is going with it.

(Everyone tries not to laugh. Gilley looks genuinely flattered.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
But…

(She sighs, head tilting, voice dipping into something almost tender.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
You’re perpetually going to be Peter Pan, aren’t you?

**GILLEY**
If I get to fly and never grow old, hell yes.

**KATHY** (half-smiling)
And occasionally get verbally stabbed by Tinker Bell?  Also yes.

**JEFF**
You two need your own sitcom.

**JIM**
No, they *are* the sitcom. We’re just the laugh track.

**BILL**
Can we please record this before the goodwill dies?

**KATHY**
On it.

(She steps to the mic. Calm. Ready.)

*FADE OUT on Gilley watching her with real admiration now—not lust, not confusion—just awe. And Kathy, owning the room, because yeah—she’s the one with the mic.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 8:40 P.M. – MOMENTS BEFORE KATHY STEPS TO THE MIC**

Kathy’s at the stand, fingers wrapped around it like she’s about to light a fuse.  But Jeff’s off to the side, **brow furrowed**, scribbling furiously, scratching out lines, muttering.

**JEFF**
Shit… hang on… hang on.

(He squints at the page. Then at the air. Then closes his eyes like he’s trying to see through his own skull.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
I’m working on the next lyric. It’s there, it’s—

(frustrated)
It just doesn’t work like that sometimes.

(Beat.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
Sometimes I’ve got a squint.  Sometimes I’ve got nothing.

(He shrugs.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
Maybe I might need help.

**KATHY**  (whipping around)
*Help*?

**GILLEY**
Oh my god, the muse stuttered.

**JIM**
So it’s not like you’re *mainlining genius*, is it, Jeff?

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
Should we call the Vatican? Cancel the canonization?

**BILL**
Alert the press: Jeff Evans is—wait for it—*human.*

(Jeff holds up his notebook like a shield.)

**JEFF**
Okay, okay. One minute I’m Moses, next minute I’m a crossword puzzle with coffee stains.

**KATHY**
It’s adorable watching you sweat.

**JEFF**
It’s panic. But make it fashion.

(He exhales. Smiles.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
Alright, hit the verse. I’ll catch up.  Eventually.

*FADE OUT on Jeff looking at the page like it just betrayed him, the rest of the band relishing the moment, and Kathy stepping up to deliver what he started—with or without his genius on call.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 8:45 P.M. – CHAOS MOMENT**

Kathy’s about to drop her line. Jeff’s been sweating—squinting, scribbling, muttering like the magic’s gone.  Then suddenly—

**JEFF** (reading, almost like in a trance)
*You’re moving further down, tracing the line.*
*A trail of heat ignites. Oh, this moment feels divine.*
*Gasping softly, my body arches high—*
*As your kisses flutter, I know I can’t deny.*

**Silence.**

Not reverent silence.

**Shock.**

**KATHY**
*What the fuck.*

**JIM**
No. Nope. *Nope.*

**GILLEY**
You *have* to be time traveling.

**BILL**
Are you reading your own book from 1992?

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
This isn’t songwriting. This is **chronomancy**.

**KATHY**
You sat there like a dying houseplant for ten minutes and then *moaned out* a second verse that makes me want to either blush or write fanfiction.

**JEFF**
I—I just—

**GILLEY**
Just what? Slipped into a trance and transcribed *divine lesbian erotica* from the future?

**JEFF** (still blinking)
I thought it was good…

**JIM**
It’s **terrifying**.

**KATHY**
It’s *perfect*. I hate you.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Say it again. But slower. I want to taste it.

(Everyone groans. Kathy doesn’t care.)

**JEFF** (reading, slower, almost sheepish now)
*You’re moving further down, tracing the line…*

*FADE OUT on a garage full of people howling, cursing, throwing paper in the air, while Jeff, stunned, just keeps reading like he can’t help himself. Like the lyric is already written—he’s just the one lucky enough to catch it.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 8:47 P.M. – RIGHT AFTER THE VERSE HITS LIKE A BOMB**

Jeff’s verse has destroyed the room. Kathy’s got her hands over her mouth, *not* to scream—just to hold the lyric in. Gilley is on the floor, not metaphorically. **Literally.** Flat on his back, staring at the ceiling like the Spirit of Rock just touched his forehead.

And then **Jeremy** stands. Hands gesturing like he’s sculpting thunder out of air.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
Jeff.

(Jeff looks over, still dazed.)

**JEREMY (EVANS) (CONT’D)**
Can you *hear* it?  Can you hear the **big-time power ruff**?

(Beat.)

**JEREMY (EVANS) (CONT’D)**
That’s what we need.  That’s what this *deserves*. Big ruff in the chorus. Huge. *Stupid huge.*

(He’s pacing now, drumming his fists against the air.)

**JEREMY (EVANS) (CONT’D)**
This is where we need to **move air**.  This is where we **punch**.  This is where we bring our noise—And *stop being precious* and *start whipping everyone’s ass.*

**KATHY** (grinning, lit up)
Hell yes.

**JIM**
I got it.

**GILLEY** (half-sitting up)
You mean like that driving octave pedal riff with wide bends and no reverb?

**BILL**
Make it ugly. Make it mean.

**JEFF**
Layer the synth under it. Big attack.  I want speakers to *buckle*.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
Yes. YES.  This is the **impact moment.**  We’re not asking for attention.  We’re **beating the door off the hinges**.

*FADE OUT on Jeremy throwing his arm like he’s conducting an explosion, Jeff flipping to a clean page, and Jim cracking his knuckles—because now it’s time to **stop whispering and *hit.***

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 8:49 P.M. – THE CHORUS IGNITES**

Jeremy’s in the zone—**pure instinct**, fingers flying.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
Wait—wait—I think I got it.

He shreds five different riffs in under a minute—grinding, bending, snapping at the edges.  On the fifth one?  **Lightning.**  He cleans it, compresses it.  **Hooks it.**

**JEREMY (EVANS) (CONT’D)**
Forty-five seconds. This one *breathes*.

**GILLEY**
I’ll double it. Give me a sec.

(He picks it up, tries to follow—slips a bit.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
Damn. Almost. I’m close.

(He adjusts, tries again, still just shy.)

And then—

**KATHY** (sharp, calm)
Let me try, boys.

(They turn. She’s already plugging in her guitar.)

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
You brought yours?

**KATHY**
I *always* bring mine.

(She steps forward, **no hesitation**—shoulders squared, fingers already on the neck.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
I’ve been playing it in my head for the last ten minutes.  Now I’m gonna *make it bleed.*

She sets her stance, grips the pick—**and hits the riff.**  **Dead on.**  Clean. Aggressive.  Better than either of them.

**JEFF**
That’s it.  That’s the line. That’s the *attitude.*

**JIM**
That’s the chorus walking into traffic with no fear.

**BILL**
The girl just landed the plane.

**GILLEY**
Okay. Fine.  She wins.

**KATHY**
It’s not about winning.

(Beat. She smiles.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
It’s about *impact.*

*FADE OUT on her guitar still ringing, the riff fully formed, and the band suddenly realizing—Kathy didn’t join the song. She just owned it. And now they have to keep up.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 8:51 P.M. – CHORUS COMPLETE, STRINGS STILL RINGING**

Kathy’s just nailed the riff—**harder, cleaner, dirtier** than anyone else in the room.  The feedback hums like a live wire across concrete.  Everyone’s staring at her.  She doesn’t bask. She just steps forward.  Shoulders squared. Voice **low and lethal.**

**KATHY**
It bleeds like me.

(Silence.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
And don’t any of you boys ever forget that.

(Beat. The kind of pause you measure in heartbeats.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Have you learned your lesson yet?

**JEFF** (laughing, shaking his head)
Absolutely. Repeatedly.

**JIM**
Consider me educated and terrified.

**GILLEY**
Can I get it tattooed on my soul?

**BILL**
Not sure it’d fit.  Might need to stretch the canvas.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
Should we vote to make that the name of the song?

**KATHY**
No.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
The song doesn’t need a name.  It’ll speak for itself.

*FADE OUT on Kathy turning back to her mic, sweat in her hair, guitar still hot, and five guys realizing—*she didn’t just bring her guitar.*

**She brought judgment.**

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 8:53 P.M. – RIGHT AFTER KATHY'S DOMINANCE MOMENT**

The room is still buzzing. Kathy just finished dropping the hammer, guitar still buzzing under her fingertips.

But **Jeff**, sitting cross-legged on the floor, shakes his head—calm, almost quiet.

**JEFF**
No.  Wrong.

(Everyone turns.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
That’s really wrong.

(Beat.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
It’s not rage. It’s not judgment. It’s not vindication.  This isn’t an explosion.

(He stands slowly, looking at the lyric sheet. His tone goes flat. Focused.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
It’s a **dissection of sentiment**.

(Beat.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
It’s a *dissection*.  It’s a dissection.  We’re **tearing something apart**.  Not wildly. Not emotionally. With **precision**.

**JIM**
You’re talking about a breakup?

**JEFF**
I’m talking about *everything*.  About desire. About power. About what it means to let someone inside you and then ask—*what is this, really?*

(He walks to the table, taps his finger against the lyric sheet.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
It’s not a controlled demolition.  It’s not “burn it down and walk away.”  It’s **slicing.**   It’s **questioning**.  With cold hands.

**BILL**
Intention-free?

**JEFF**
Exactly.  *Not* manipulative.  *Not* strategic.  It’s interrogation for the sake of truth.

**KATHY**
So you’re not bleeding. You’re cutting.

**JEFF**
I’m cutting to *see*.

*FADE OUT on the band standing around the table, looking at the page with fresh eyes—not as a confession, not as a war cry, but as **an open body** on the table. And Jeff holding the scalpel.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 8:55 P.M. – AFTER JEFF’S “DISSECTION” MONOLOGUE**

The room is still tense, quiet, analytical. Jeff’s words hang in the air like frost.  Everyone’s circling the idea—no one touching it yet.  And then—

**GILLEY**
Oh.

(They all look at him.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
So this is just like chemistry class.

(Blank stares.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
You’re applying the scientific method.  You’ve got your subject, your variables, your tools, your step-by-step peeling back of the *why*.

(He spins a pick between his fingers.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
That’s what you’re doing.

(Beat.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
This is “*Scientific Method*.”

(He looks around.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
You can thank me in the morning.

**KATHY** (half-laugh, half-choke)
Jesus Christ, he’s right.

**JIM**
That’s…actually perfect.

**JEFF**
It works to a degree.

**BILL**
And it makes it colder.  Clinical.  Detached.  Exactly what we’re building.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
Sounds like something you’d read in a psych ward and then hear on the radio six weeks later.

**KATHY**
*Scientific Method.*

(Beat.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Fuck me, that’s the name.

**GILLEY**
That’s what I do, people. Every now and then I *name a masterpiece.*

*FADE OUT on Gilley smugly grinning, the band nodding slowly, and the lyric sheet now bearing a title:*

***“Scientific Method.”***

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 8:57 P.M. – THE FINAL VERSE HITS**

Jeff is back in the trance. Pen in one hand, other hand just hovering, guiding the line into place.

**JEFF**
*Quite responsive, you tease with a grin.*
*But in this dance of passion, it’s a thrilling spin.*
*Only when it’s worth it, I say with a sigh.*
*In this wild connection, we’re both flying high.*

**KATHY**  (under her breath)
Oh shit.

**GILLEY**
*BOOM.*

**BILL**
We’re in.

**JIM**
That’s the moment. That’s the *cut line*.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
*Drop it. DROP IT.*

Jeff doesn’t even look up. He just says it:

**JEFF**
And then—*boom*—we’re into the chorus.

**KATHY** (stepping forward, fire in her throat)
Let’s fly.

Jim counts in—**two quick taps**—and the **garage explodes**. Guitars shred into the chorus.  Bill floods the room with synth.  Kathy grabs the mic and *screams with melody.*  They’re not building a song anymore.  **They’re in it.**  This is ***Scientific Method**.*  Cold. Erotic. Wild. Surgical. Divine.  They’ve been chasing this feeling for months. Now it’s here: their own song. Raw, jagged, and bleeding at the edges. But it’s *theirs*. Not a cover. Not a mimic. Not a borrowed sound. They built it from scratch. They *earned* it.

Kathy leans against her amp, eyes closed, still hearing the riff echo in her skull. Jeff’s notebook is a mess of ink and torn corners. Jeremy’s hands are shaking from the last chorus. Jim’s still tapping out fills on his thighs. Bill’s synth is humming, faintly, like it doesn’t want to stop.

Gilley claps once. Loud. Final.

**GILLEY**
That’s it. Go home. Dream about it. Come back tomorrow and make it real.

They pack up in silence, but it’s not awkward. It’s reverent. They’re carrying something fragile now. Something that didn’t exist before tonight.  Outside, the night air hits them like a wave. Cool. Sharp. Cleansing.

**KATHY** (softly)
We did it.

**JEFF** (grinning)
Yeah. We fucking did.

They part ways, each carrying a piece of the song with them. It’s not finished. It’s not perfect. But it’s alive.

And tomorrow, they’ll bring it back to life again.

---
## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – 11:00 P.M. – END OF PRACTICE**

The garage is dimly lit, the air thick with the scent of sweat, dust, and the lingering vibrations of amplifiers. The band members are scattered around, instruments in hand, faces flushed with the exhilaration of creation.  A moment of silence settles, each member lost in their thoughts, basking in the afterglow of their breakthrough.

**JIM** (checking his watch)
It's eleven.

The room stills. No one moves. They all know the rule. Mr. Gilley doesn't need to be present to enforce it. The unspoken agreement is clear: practice ends at eleven.

**BILL** (starting to unplug his synth)
Alright, let's wrap it up.

**GILLEY** (nodding, already packing his guitar)
We finally have our own material.

**JEREMY** (smiling)
It's raw, but it's ours.

They begin to pack up, the room filled with the soft clatter of equipment being stowed away. The energy is still high, the adrenaline coursing through their veins. They exchange glances, smiles, and nods, the unspoken bond between them stronger than ever.

**KATHY** (slinging her guitar over her shoulder)
Can't wait to see where this takes us.

They exit the garage one by one, stepping into the cool night air, each carrying the weight of their creation with them. The garage door closes behind them, the sound echoing in the quiet street.

*FADE OUT.*

---

## **EXT. GILLEY’S DRIVEWAY – 11:03 P.M. – THE BAND DISPERSING**

Guitar cases click shut. Amp cords are coiled and slung over shoulders. The garage door rolls closed behind them with a mechanical groan and a final *clunk*—practice is over.  The night is cool. The cicadas are loud.  The band is glowing, still high on adrenaline, the echo of their new song thudding through their ribs.  Kathy slings her bag over her shoulder. Her face is calm. Poised.

But her words cut through the moment like wire.

**KATHY**
I know exactly where this is taking me.

(They all turn.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
I’m going home.  I’m going to crawl into my own bed.  Alone.

(She turns her head—**locks eyes with Gilley.**)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Alone.

**GILLEY** (small voice)
…Copy that.

**JEFF**
Holy shit.

**JIM**
That wasn’t a lyric, but I still felt it.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
I'm gonna need therapy.

**BILL**
You won’t be alone, Kathy.

(Beat. He points to his head.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
We’re all going with you. Right up here.  Like a trauma flashback with a soundtrack.

Kathy smiles faintly, turns, and walks off into the darkness, guitar swinging low.

*FADE OUT on Gilley still staring at the spot she stood, not sure whether he just lost something—or narrowly avoided being set on fire.*

---

## **EXT. GILLEY’S DRIVEWAY – MOMENTS AFTER KATHY WALKS OFF**

The band is still frozen in the wake of Kathy’s declaration.

**GILLEY** (muttering, to no one in particular)
Whatever. I’m going out tonight anyway.

(He grabs his jacket off the porch rail, brushes dust off his sleeves.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
I was already planning it.

**JIM**
Planning what?

**GILLEY**
1470.

(They all look at him.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
The dance club.

(Beat.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
I’m gonna pick someone up. That was the plan. That’s *still* the plan.

**JEFF**
Oh boy.

**GILLEY**  (staring toward the street where Kathy disappeared)
Let me iterate something—real clear.

(Beat.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
I was serious earlier.  I’m never fucking you again, Kathy.

(He says it to the night, not shouting. Just *declaring*.)

**BILL**
You know she’s not here to hear that, right?

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
But we are. Unfortunately.

**JIM**
And now we have to live with it.

**GILLEY**
Good.  Let the record show.

(He steps off the porch, chin up, **like he didn’t just lose a war he started by accident.**)

*FADE OUT on Gilley walking alone toward his car, trying to turn heartbreak into swagger—and not quite making it stick.*

---

## **EXT. GILLEY’S DRIVEWAY – 11:06 P.M. – NIGHT AIR THICK**

The streetlamp throws long shadows across cracked pavement.  The band stands scattered near the curb—five of them now.  No one says a word as **Gilley slides into his car**. That tiny, sun-faded **Ford Escort**.  The driver’s door creaks. The seat squeaks.  He shuts the door a little too hard. Just once.  The engine kicks over on the second try.  He doesn’t look back.

The taillights glow red as he backs out with **surprising smoothness**, as if that tiny car is the last thing he still has full control over.

**JIM** (softly, to no one)
There he goes.

**JEFF**
Heading toward Dayton.

**BILL**
Of course he is.

The Escort turns the corner.  Gone.

The five remaining members just stand there in the quiet buzz of crickets and amplifier ghosts.  Nobody says it out loud, but they’re all thinking it: **Gilley left.**  But **Kathy stayed**.  And that means everything.

*FADE OUT on five silhouettes in the night, guitars slung, notebooks in hand, and a song humming low inside each of them—unfinished, but undeniably alive.*

---

## **EXT. GILLEY’S DRIVEWAY – 11:08 P.M. – ESCORT GONE**

The Escort’s red taillights have vanished around the corner.  Kathy’s standing with her arms folded, face unreadable.  The rest of the band lingers in the driveway, still half-lit by the porch.

**JEREMY (EVANS)** (quietly, to Kathy)
Do you think… I mean, do you think you might’ve hurt him?

(Beat. Kathy doesn’t look up.)

**JIM** (snorts)
That’s ridiculous.

**JEFF** (sharp, dry)
Gilley doesn’t have a soul.

**JEFF** (beat, then calmly)
Maybe not.  But he *does* have a conscience.

(Everyone’s quiet for a moment.)

**BILL**
A twisted one, maybe. But yeah. He *feels* it. He just doesn’t know where to file it.

**KATHY** (still not looking at anyone)
I wasn’t trying to hurt him.

**JEFF**
That’s not what this was.

**JIM**
No.  This was her choosing *herself.*

(Beat. Kathy finally lifts her chin.)

**KATHY**
And if that hurts him?

(Beat.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Then maybe it should.

*FADE OUT on that line hanging in the air—sharp, earned, and still echoing as the band starts walking back to their cars, knowing damn well that the night might be over—but the song is just beginning.*

---
# **CHAPTER SIX: WE'RE FOOLS TO MAKE WAR**

---
## **INT. 1470 DANCE CLUB – 1:04 A.M. – DAYTON, OHIO**

Lights strobe. Bass thumps. Sweat beads on mirrors and skin.  **Gilley is in his element.** Black button-up open just enough. Cheap cologne. A smile that’s too easy and always dangerous.  **He’s already got three phone numbers.**  One written in eyeliner on a napkin.  One in blue ink up the inside of his wrist.  One scrawled on a drink receipt, circled twice with a heart.

**KATHY?** Forgotten ten seconds after he walked through the front door.  That’s not bitterness.  That’s **Gilley’s coping mechanism**—obliteration by distraction.  He’s not thinking about bands or democracy or guitar riffs.  He’s **gliding**, drink in hand, hips in rhythm, tongue silver-coated.  He **laughs too loud**, moves like someone who owns the room by default, and when the DJ plays something synthy and slutty, he raises his arms like he summoned it.

**GILLEY** (to no one, to everyone)
Let’s go. Let’s *fucking go.*

He’s not looking back.  Not tonight.  Not when the neon loves him, and the world is loud enough to drown every leftover feeling.

*FADE OUT on Gilley lit in red and violet, spinning through strangers like a star that refuses to collapse, even if it’s already burning out.*

---

## **INT. 1470 DANCE CLUB – 1:12 A.M. – DAYTON, OHIO**

The floor’s slick. The air is humid with breath and perfume and potential. Then—**it happens**.  The DJ drops the needle on **Nine Inch Nails**.  **Early stuff. Raw. Ugly. Fuck-you-and-beg-for-more industrial.**  The bass kicks in—And **the volume isn’t 10.**

It’s **11**.

The sound system wasn’t built for this.  The building wasn’t either.  **The foundation shakes.**  Barstools vibrate.  Glasses on the shelf *clink* against each other like a warning.  People stop mid-grind.  Look up.  Smile.  **They know.**

**GILLEY**  (arms raised, ecstatic)
*YES.*

The drop hits and **the house rocks**.  It becomes *heat*.  It becomes *pulse*.  It becomes the kind of music that **blasts the thoughts out of your skull** and leaves nothing but instinct.  **Gilley vanishes into the sound.**  Not as an escape.  As a *declaration*.  He’s not thinking about Kathy.  He’s not thinking about the band.  He’s thinking about **this second**, this note, this volume, this *goddamn frequency* that feels like it was tuned specifically to his bloodstream.

*FADE OUT on him in strobe light and distortion, smiling like a man on fire who swears he’s never been more alive.*

---

## **INT. 1470 DANCE CLUB – 1:20 A.M. – STILL SHAKING**

The last of **Nine Inch Nails** rips through the floor like a final warning shot.  People are breathless. Feral.  Then—**a new pulse**.

**Depeche Mode.**

Low. Smooth. Commanding. Not a scream—**a whisper with teeth.**  *“Never Let Me Down Again.”*  Or *“Strangelove.”*  One of the *slow burns*. **The lights go cooler.**  Blue now. Violet.  Smoke curls from the floor like the room itself is exhaling.  And **Gilley?**  He shifts on cue.  The wild grin fades into a smile.  His movement slows.  Becomes deliberate.
More hips. Less chaos.

The phone number on his wrist smudges a little as he lifts his drink.  **He’s not chasing anymore.**  Now?  **He’s being followed.**  Someone brushes past him on the floor. A girl in red.  He lets her go—just long enough to turn, lock eyes, and draw her back in.

**GILLEY** (mouth barely moving)
Told you this place had levels.

*FADE OUT on the bassline pulsing through the crowd, Gilley a silhouette now—half man, half rhythm—moving like he never lost anything in the first place.*

---

## **INT. 1470 DANCE FLOOR – 1:27 A.M. – DEPECHE MODE IN FULL SEDUCTION MODE**

Gilley’s in the zone.  Bodies moving. Bass melting spines.  Everything is soft-focus but *precise.*  He turns—half-step, half-drift—and **there she is.**

**Stacey Dawson.**

Same smile. Same swing in her step.  Dressed to kill with just enough nostalgia to sting.
Gilley doesn’t miss a beat.  Raises his glass, voice low but perfectly audible.

**GILLEY**
Stacey.  **Motherfucking. Dawson.**

(He smiles like a blade.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
How *are* you?

(Beat.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
Where’s your husband?

(Everything stops for a half-second. Her eyes narrow. She doesn’t answer.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**  (leans in slightly)
Don’t worry. That wasn’t an invitation.  Just a… *census check*.

*FADE OUT on the two of them circling each other in the slow dark, history dancing right alongside the rhythm. Because some nights? The past doesn’t knock. It struts straight through the door.*

---

## **INT. 1470 DANCE FLOOR – 1:28 A.M. – THE TEMPERATURE SPIKES**

Gilley’s last line still lingers in the air.  **“Don’t worry. That wasn’t an invitation.”**  Stacey stares at him, slow blink, one eyebrow rising like the curtain on a one-woman show he’s not equipped to handle.  Then—

**STACEY**
No, it wasn’t.

(Beat. Her smile spreads, slow and razor-clean.)

**STACEY (CONT’D)**
But don’t worry, sweetheart.  I’m planning on being *chaste* tonight.

(Leans just enough to make him wonder.)

**STACEY (CONT’D)**
Not planning to sink my fangs into your neck.  Tonight.

(She turns back to the floor—leaving the word *tonight* like a lit cigarette on his collar.)

**GILLEY** (murmuring to himself, adjusting his jaw)
And people say I’m dangerous.

*FADE OUT on them dancing ten feet apart—neither advancing, neither retreating. Just circling. Because sometimes restraint is more loaded than any kiss.*

---

## **INT. 1470 DANCE FLOOR – 1:32 A.M. – DARK LAUGHTER IN THE LIGHT**

Gilley lifts his glass again, nodding toward the crowd.

**GILLEY**
So where is he?

**STACEY** (rolling her eyes with fond exasperation)
Jeremy? My Jeremy?  He went off to get drinks. Supposedly.

(She glances toward the bar.)

**STACEY (CONT’D)**
But clearly, there’s been a *delay in logistics.*

**GILLEY** (chuckling)
It’s almost tragic, isn’t it?  So many Jeffs and Jeremys in this world.

**STACEY**
Deadly accurate.

(Beat.)

**STACEY (CONT’D)**
It’s *exhausting* dealing with you people.  Jeremy Dawson.  Jeremy Gilley.
Jeremy Evans.

**(She steps closer. Drops her voice. Low and syrup-slick.)**

**STACEY (CONT’D)**
Shhh.  Here’s a secret.

(She leans just enough to buzz his sense of gravity.)

**STACEY (CONT’D)**
I’m only going to fuck *one* of them.

(Beat. Straight in his eyes.)

**STACEY (CONT’D)**
And it ain’t you.

(She pauses, lets it hang—then, with a glint:)

**STACEY (CONT’D)**
But…

(That slow, serpentine smile.)

**STACEY (CONT’D)**
I wouldn’t mind.

(She turns on her heel, disappearing into the crush of bodies before he can fire back.)

**GILLEY** (half to himself, half grinning)
Jesus Christ, I’m in love with every dangerous woman in Ohio.

*FADE OUT on Gilley frozen for once—laughing, impressed, a little scorched—and the dance floor swallowing up the moment like it never happened.*

---

## **INT. 1470 DANCE FLOOR – 1:36 A.M. – STILL IN THE PULSE**

Stacey’s just dropped her line.  *“I’m only going to fuck one of them. And it ain’t you. But… I wouldn’t mind.”*

She starts to turn.  It’s a clean exit line.  **Gilley doesn’t let her have it.**  He closes the space—just a step. Just enough.  He says it low. Calm. Right in her face.

**GILLEY**
I don’t need to fuck you, Stacey.

(She stops.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
I’ll show up with a straight edge razor.

(Beat.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
Trim your pussy.

(Shrugs. Smiles. *Flat-out dangerous.*)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
And leave.  That’s all you’d get from me.

(Silence. Between them, the bassline keeps thumping—slow, dirty, deliberate.)

**STACEY**
You’re out of your fucking mind.

**GILLEY**
Then why’s your heart beating faster?

(They lock eyes. No one flinches.)

*FADE OUT on the standoff that isn’t a standoff—it’s a slow ignition. Neither of them won. Neither of them lost. But **both of them are thinking about what happens next.***

---

## **INT. 1470 DANCE FLOOR – 1:38 A.M. – STANDOFF CONCLUDED**

Gilley delivers the line.  *Trim your pussy. And leave.*  And then—**he turns.**  **No follow-up. No glance back.**  He just *walks away.*  Into the neon. Into the crowd.  Already scanning the floor for a redhead he half-remembers, **a number inked in sharpie on the back of his wrist.**  It’s not about the redhead.  It’s about the *exit.*

Stacey stands where he left her.  Still warm. Still vibrating with tension.  **She exhales. Once. Sharply.**

**STACEY** (muttering to herself)
Motherfucker.

(Beat.)

He took her *right to the edge.*  Didn’t flinch. Didn’t beg. Didn’t play for the kiss.  **He *walked*.** That was the move.

**STACEY (CONT’D)**  (under her breath, almost smiling)
Somebody’s getting laid tonight.

(Beat. She takes a sip of her drink.)

**STACEY (CONT’D)**
And my husband is going to take *delight* in my pleasures.

*FADE OUT on Stacey standing alone in the dark velvet of the club, half-smirking, half-scorched, fully turned on—and knowing exactly where she’s going to channel every last spark.*

---

## **INT. KATHY’S BATHROOM – 2:04 A.M. – DIM LIGHT, STEAM COILING**

The apartment is still. The only sound is water—hot, steady, endless.  Kathy stands under the showerhead, eyes closed, arms folded across her chest. **The water scalds. She doesn’t flinch.**

She’s been up forever. Her legs ache.  Her neck is sore.  There’s grime behind her knees and across her shoulders from when she dropped to the garage floor to tune her amp.  She skipped this shower **twelve hours ago**—to be three hours early, to clean the garage, to be first, to lead.

She skipped treating herself like a woman so she could be a soldier.  Now, she’s **neither**.  Now—she’s **just herself.**  Slowly, she soaps her forearms.  She lathers between her toes.  She scrubs the nape of her neck with *deliberate tenderness*, like she’s reintroducing herself to her own skin.  It’s not glamorous.  It’s not performative.  It’s **necessary**.

**KATHY**  (softly, to no one)
There you go.

*FADE OUT on steam thick in the room, her outline blurred but whole again, the water rinsing away nothing but what needed to go.*

---

## **INT. KATHY’S BATHROOM – 2:17 A.M. – POST-SHOWER**

She stands in a towel, one leg propped up on the tub.  Razor in hand.  Looks down at the light fuzz on her shin.  Tilts her head.  Considers.

**KATHY**
Nope.  Not gonna.

(She tosses the razor back into the basket.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
What I *am* gonna do…is get me an ice cream bar.

(Beat. She grins at her reflection.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
And I’m gonna *eat* it.  And then I’m gonna *enjoy* it.  And then I’m gonna *fall asleep.*

(She grabs her pajamas from the hook.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Because life right now?  Is just that simple.

*FADE OUT on Kathy walking barefoot into the quiet apartment, towel still around her neck, humming under her breath. In the fridge: one chocolate-dipped ice cream bar with her name on it. And for once, she’s not fighting anything. She’s just being. And it’s enough.*

---

## **INT. KATHY’S KITCHEN – 2:21 A.M. – THE FRIDGE LIGHT BLOOMS**

Barefoot. Damp hair. Loose pajama shirt.  Kathy opens the freezer and stares at the row of ice cream options like they hold cosmic truth.  She grabs an **ice cream sandwich**. No hesitation.

As she closes the freezer, the image hits her—**Jeff**, lounging on the garage floor,
grinning like he was half-asleep, then casually opening his mouth and **writing a second verse that cracked the room in half.**

**KATHY** (softly, mouth full of ice cream)
Fucking terrifying.

(Beat. She chews. Swallows.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
How do you *do* that on the fly?

(She leans against the counter, ice cream sandwich in hand, half-melted already.)

It scared the hell out of her.  The **effortlessness** of it.  The way the words came out **beautiful and violent and alive**, like Jeff was just **reading the song off the back of her spine**.

She exhales. Shrugs.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
But hey.

(She takes another bite.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Ice cream sandwich.

*FADE OUT on Kathy standing in the kitchen in the early morning stillness, sugar on her tongue, fear in her chest, and a tiny smile on her face—because **tomorrow she’ll fight the talent war again**. But tonight? Tonight is just ice cream.*

---

## **INT. EVANS BROTHERS’ BEDROOM – 2:26 A.M. – DONNELSVILLE**

**Still. Dark. Crickets outside.**  A box fan in the window hums low and steady.  The ceiling fan ticks and spins in lazy rhythm overhead.  Two windows cracked open.  One screen door at the back of the room, letting in a **cool breath of summer air**.

And the **Evans brothers?**  Out cold.  **Snoring.**  **Jeremy** sprawled across his twin bed like he lost a wrestling match with gravity.  **Jeff**, diagonal on his own mattress, **mouth slightly open**, breathing like he hasn’t had a thought in three hours.

They’re both shirtless.  The room smells like **sweat, clean laundry, and guitar picks**.  There are **notebooks on the floor.**  One amp cable slung across a chair.  But no tension. No reflection. **Just sleep.**  They snore in stereo—off-sync, then in rhythm, then apart again.  **Unbothered.** **Unconcerned.** **Completely still in the moment.**

*FADE OUT on the slow arc of the ceiling fan blades overhead, circling like time itself has taken the night off.*

---

## **INT.  JIM’S DAD’S HOUSE – BASEMENT – 2:32 A.M.**

The basement is dim.  Carpet thin.  Wood paneling warped from too many Ohio summers.  The **Atari 2600** sits crooked on a milk crate beside a 13-inch TV with a dial tuner and one loose cable that fuzzes if you breathe near it.

On the screen?  **Yars’ Revenge.**  That glowing little pixelated bug.  That eerie hum.  That relentless laser trap and the satisfaction of getting it just *right*.

**Jim** sits cross-legged on the floor, back straight, eyes locked in.  He’s played this game **three thousand times**—but he’s **leaning forward** like it’s his first night home from college and someone just told him that everything’s gonna be okay as long as he *gets through this next level.*

**He’s not thinking about the song.**  Not Jeff.  Not Kathy.  Not even the band.  He’s thinking in blips and dodges.  In tiny victories.  In **simple, absolute objectives.**  Avoid the destroyer.  Fire at the shield.  Get revenge.

**JIM**  (softly, to himself)
C’mon. Just one clean pass.

The screen flashes. He lands the shot.

**Score: +1.**

*FADE OUT on that faint, staticky glow lighting his face, the hum of digital nostalgia, and a teenage drummer holding the joystick like it’s the only thing in the world he can fully control tonight.*

---

## **INT. REDHEAD’S BEDROOM – 4:08 A.M. – DAYTON APARTMENT**

Dim morning blue filters through half-closed blinds.  A fan buzzes low.  There’s an empty glass of water on the nightstand.  Gilley is slipping his jeans back on, barefoot, hair wild, grin intact. He’s not sneaking out—he’s **staging an exit.**

The redhead—still in bed, sheet half-draped over her, watching him with amusement and residual afterglow—raises an eyebrow.

**GILLEY**
Hey.

(Beat.)
Quick favor.  Can you, like…**donate your bra to the cause?**

(She blinks.)

**REDHEAD**
That bra cost me fifteen bucks.

**GILLEY**
Right. And it’s about to be **immortalized**.

(He turns, arms out.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
I’ve got a point to make.  Somewhere. To someone.

(Shrugs.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
A symbolic gesture.

**REDHEAD**
Of what?

**GILLEY**
Victory. Freedom. Maybe pettiness.  Maybe all three.

(She just stares.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
Look—I’ll write you a song.

(Beat.)

When I get famous?  You’ll be track five.  You’ll be the hook that *lingers.*

(He grins.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
Fair trade.

(Beat.)

**REDHEAD** (sighs, amused)
You are such a ridiculous bastard.

(She throws the bra at him.)

**GILLEY** (holding it like a trophy)
And now, I’m a ridiculous *legend.*

*FADE OUT on Gilley striding barefoot through her apartment, bra in hand, already writing his headline—because if tonight was about sex, the morning is about narrative.*

---

## **INT.  REDHEAD’S BEDROOM – 4:10 A.M. – POST-TROPHY ACQUISITION**

Gilley holds the bra up to the light, turning it like a rare artifact.  The redhead watches from the bed, arms folded, amused.  He reads the tag.

**GILLEY**
Thirty-two A.

(Half a frown. Beat.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
Huh.

(He turns, looks at her square in the eye.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
You’re charming.

(Shrugs, tucks the bra into his back pocket like a pressed flower.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
She’s bigger.  But the point will be made.

(He scribbles something on a scrap receipt near her nightstand. Tears it off. Hands it to her.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
Here’s my number.

(Starts backing toward the door. One last grin.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
By the way—

(pauses)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
Name’s Jeremy.

*FADE OUT on the door clicking shut, her laughter soft behind it, and Gilley walking barefoot into the pre-dawn air like a man who just signed his name at the end of a very strange, very intentional chapter.*

---

## **EXT.  I-70 EASTBOUND – 4:22 A.M. – SOMEWHERE BETWEEN DAYTON AND DONNELSVILLE**

Gilley drives with the windows down.  The air is cool and thick with morning fog.  His shirt’s still unbuttoned.  The radio hums static between half-found FM signals.  He’s not listening.  One hand on the wheel. The other fishing something out of his back pocket.

**The bra.**

Still crumpled. White. Delicate.  He holds it up for a second—flicks it like a handkerchief.
Grins to himself.

**GILLEY**
Point made.

(And with that—)

He tosses it out the window.  No ceremony. No regret.  It flutters for a moment—brief and weightless—then disappears into the shoulder grass as the taillights pull ahead.  **Gilley doesn’t look back.**

*FADE OUT on the road stretching ahead, Gilley’s engine low and steady, and the symbolic proof of the night left behind like a wrapper from a firecracker.*

---

## **INT. ESPICH HOUSE – BASEMENT ROOM – 4:31 A.M. – PRE-DAWN SILENCE**

The Espich House is dark and quiet, the kind of quiet that feels protective.  Downstairs in the basement, the low hum of the water heater is the only sound.  **Kathy is done for the night.**  Her hair is damp, still curling at the ends.  She smells like soap and clean cotton.
She’s already in her **safe, comfy, warm inner PJs**—the ones that barely exist outside this room.

She’s already eaten her ice cream sandwich.  Already tasted something simple and sweet, the only indulgence she allowed herself tonight.

She moves slowly—no more urgency.  She brushes her teeth. Folds the towel that was still around her shoulders. Turns off the light. Then she climbs into bed.

Beneath the quilt, her body exhales for her.  Everything releases. The notebook stays shut on the nightstand.  The guitar stays leaned in the corner.  Everything important has been deferred to tomorrow.  She stares at the ceiling, then lets her eyes close.

*FADE OUT on Kathy in perfect stillness—clean, full, warm, safe. For tonight, there’s nothing left to do. For tonight, she is allowed to simply be.*

---

# **CHAPTER SEVEN: THE SONG ABOUT THE KNIFE**

---
## **INT. AUDIOLOGY CLINIC – 9:12 A.M. – SPRINGFIELD, OHIO**

Bright lights. Beige carpet. The kind of place that smells like vinyl chairs and antiseptic wipes.  Jeff sits in the waiting room with **a clipboard in his lap**, filling out the same form he filled out last year.  Same questions.  Same dread.

He taps his pen against the line that reads:

**“Describe your current hearing concerns.”**

He doesn’t write *“everything.”*  He writes **“right ear worsening.”**

Last summer, he got through it.  **Tympanoplasty on the left side.**  A whole new eardrum.  Middle ear bones replaced with **coiled titanium wire**.  It felt like turning into a machine. But it worked.

Mostly.

Now the right one’s going.  He **knows** it.  The same distortion. The same flat spots in conversation. The same phantom echo during practice.  He already knows what today’s test will show.

**NURSE (O.S.)**
Jeff Evans?

He stands. Pockets the paperwork. Doesn’t smile.

*FADE OUT on Jeff following her down the hallway, into the soundproof booth, heart sinking not from fear of surgery—but from the slow, inevitable knowledge that his ears may not always be there to catch the music.*

---

## **INT. SOUNDPROOF BOOTH – 9:26 A.M. – AUDIOLOGY CLINIC**

Jeff sits alone in the booth.  Headphones on.  Button box in his lap, but they’re not using the button today.

**Old-school test.**  Raise your hand if you hear the tone.

He gives a thumbs-up to the glass. The audiologist on the other side nods once, then looks down at her screen.  He waits.

The room is dead silent.  No fans. No outside noise.  **Only the hiss of his own blood in his head.**

A faint tone?

He thinks so. He raises his hand.

Nothing happens.  The audiologist types something.

Another beep—maybe.  Or maybe not.  He raises his hand again.

Across the glass, she gives the smallest nod. But her **eyes** tell the story: **Concern masked behind professionalism.**

Jeff knows that look.  It’s the same one they gave him last year—before the first surgery.
He exhales through his nose.  Closes his eyes.

**Another tone.**  But maybe not.  He raises his hand anyway.

This time, the audiologist doesn’t react.  Phantom.  Jeff opens his eyes. His hand slowly lowers.  He says nothing.  He sits back.  And waits for the silence to end.

*FADE OUT on Jeff in the booth, surrounded by sound he can’t hear, and haunted by tones that may never have existed. The music is still alive in him—but the receiver is failing.*
