Thank you. Finally some respect for the fuzz.

**GILLEY**
So we’re talking Big Muff fuzz? Or that weird pedal you modded with the foil?

**JEREMY**
She’s a Wiccan. She gets the boutique treatment.

---

## **INT. GILLEY GARAGE – 4:20 P.M. – PEAK STUPIDITY, PEAK TRUTH**

Jeremy, deadpan and proud:

**JEREMY**
She’s a Wiccan. She gets the **boutique treatment.**

For half a second—**silence**.

Then—

**The garage explodes.**

**JIM** drops a drumstick and doubles over.

**BILL** collapses onto a milk crate, cackling like a hyena.

**GILLEY** lets out a *screamed* laugh and starts pounding his knee.

**KATHY** stumbles backward with her hands over her face, howling.

**JEFF** just nods solemnly, straight-faced, like he’s watching chaos unfold exactly as predicted.

**JEFF**
That’s the line that’s gonna make us famous.

**KATHY**
(still laughing)
God, I *hate* how good that is.

**JIM**
This is the stupidest, smartest band on the goddamn planet.

**BILL**
I’m not even stoned and this is a top ten moment in my life.

**JEREMY**
Boutique fuzz, bitches. Christine deserves nothing less.

*FADE OUT on the band in complete hysterics, tears on cheeks, stomachs hurting, minds blown—not by the lyric anymore, but by the unholy fusion of sex, witchcraft, and pedalboard fidelity. This is how Commuted makes a legend—by laughing their way into the abyss.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY GARAGE – 4:23 P.M. – LAUGHTER FADING, TITLE DEBATE IGNITES**

They’re still recovering from the fuzz line when Gilley suddenly snaps his fingers.

**GILLEY**
Okay, I don’t like the name.

Everyone turns.

**KATHY**
What name?

**GILLEY**
*“Next to the Ice Cream Shop.”*

**JIM**
It’s literally the first line.

**GILLEY**
Yeah. And I’m not feelin’ it.

**JEFF**
Got a suggestion?

**GILLEY**
*“Beside the Ice Cream Shop.”*

(Beat.)

**BILL**
You changed **one** word.

**KATHY**
Why?

**GILLEY**
Because the last parlor I visited?

(He shrugs, totally deadpan.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
It was beside the ice cream shop. That’s why.

**JEREMY**
Which shop?

**GILLEY**
Graeter’s.

**KATHY**
(rolling her eyes)
Oh my God.

**JEFF**
So… you want us to rename the song based on *your personal map of Dayton sex commerce.*

**GILLEY**
I’m just saying—accuracy matters.

*FADE OUT on the band groaning and giggling again, Jeff shaking his head, and Gilley already reaching for a Sharpie like he's going to retitle it anyway. Because this is Commuted: precision in the lyrics, chaos in the metadata.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY GARAGE – 4:24 P.M. – THE GRAMMAR LINE IN THE SAND**

Gilley holds up his Sharpie, triumphant.

**GILLEY**
I’m telling you—*beside* sounds classier.

**KATHY**
No.

(Silence.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
It’s *next to*. These sorts of details **matter**.

**GILLEY**
It’s literally the same thing.

**KATHY**
No. It’s *not*.

(She walks over, snatches the Sharpie out of his hand.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
I am willing to commit many atrocities—

(Motions to the lyrics)
—clearly.  But I will **not** commit an atrocity against the **English language.**

**JEFF**
Can confirm. She once threw a thesaurus at me for misusing “ironic.”

**JIM**
Was it… ironic?

**JEFF**
Not at all. It hurt.

**KATHY**
(firm)
It’s *Next to the Ice Cream Shop*.  Final. Period. Cement it in blood if you have to.

**GILLEY**
(grinning)
Damn. Remind me never to mess up a semicolon around you.

*FADE OUT on Kathy turning away victorious, title preserved, grammar defended, and the Sharpie safely returned to the drawer. Commuted may bend reality, but it **obeys syntax.***

---

## **INT. GILLEY GARAGE – 4:26 P.M. – KATHY ASCENDS**

Kathy practically leaps into the air, bouncing on the balls of her feet, notebook flapping in her hand.

**KATHY**
This is it! This is it! This is what I’ve been *waiting for*!

**BILL**
Jesus, you okay?

**KATHY**
I want to **inmanentize the eschaton**!

(Everyone blinks.)

**JIM**
That sounds like something you’d get arrested for.

**KATHY**
No, no, no—listen!

(She points to the lyric sheet, then to the amps, then to herself.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
We have the power now. The songs. The sex. The symbols. We’re not just making music—

**JEFF**
—we're *channeling doctrine.*

**KATHY**
Exactly! We’re **restructuring reality through lyrical invocation**!

**JEREMY**
Okay, but are we gonna tune first?

**GILLEY**
Let her cook.

**KATHY**
We’re going to take all this filth, all this unspoken **glory**, and we’re going to blast it at the audience like a sacrament shot out of a T-shirt cannon!

**BILL**
That’s… honestly a great visual.

**JEFF**
And if we do it right?

**KATHY**
(smiling, breathless)
The veil rips. The end begins.  And it's gonna have **killer vocals** and **guitar fuzz like pubic thunder.**

*FADE OUT on the band watching Kathy spin in a circle like a manic prophet in cutoff shorts, high on vision, soaked in purpose. Because now? Now they know: this band isn’t just going places. **This band is a spell.***

---

## **INT. GILLEY GARAGE – 4:28 P.M. – BECOMING THE CULT**

Kathy, still buzzing, breathes it out like a virgin touched for the very first time:

**KATHY**
I’ve been reading subversive literature.

(She glances around like she's about to get caught.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
*The Illuminatus!* Trilogy. Shea and Wilson.

**JEFF** (sits upright)
That explains so much.

(Beat.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
This input?  It inspires me.

(Beat.)

But it’s going to **terrify** most of the audience.

**GILLEY** (grinning like a devil)
Good.

(Shrugs.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
Let them try to keep up, Jeff.  The rest of the world might think we’re writing about a **trip to the massage parlor**…

(He leans forward.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
…but *we* will know better.

**JIM** (slowly, rubbing his chin)
You know what?

(Pause.)

I’m actually thinking about supporting this.

(Everyone turns.)

**JIM (CONT’D)**
Because it sounds **crazier** than anything the Sex Pistols ever did.

**BILL** (quietly)
Even Ozzy?

**JIM**
Even Ozzy.

(Beat.)

**JIM (CONT’D)**
He bit the head off a bat. We’re about to bite the head off *reality.*

*FADE OUT on the band locking eyes across the garage—not with fear, but with the gleaming certainty that they are no longer a band. They are a **coded transmission. A living heresy. A manifesto wrapped in a melody.***

---

## **INT. GILLEY GARAGE – 4:32 P.M. – THE PROPHECY GOES COMMERCIAL**

They’re all sitting now. Beat up. Flushed. Buzzing.

**JEFF**
We’ve gotta put this on **vinyl**.

Everyone looks up—nobody argues.

**KATHY**
Vinyl or nothing. Digital can’t hold it.

**JIM**
It needs to hiss. It needs to *rumble*.

**BILL**
Tape saturation. 180 gram. Full frequency spectrum. No compression.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
Okay, but… that means we gotta start, like… actually making music **off** our music.

(Beat.)

**JEREMY (EVANS) (CONT’D)**
I mean, making **money** off our music.

**GILLEY** (grinning, leaning back like a villain with a plan)
Leave that to me.

**KATHY**
Oh no.

**GILLEY**
I’ll figure out how to sell this shit.

(Beat.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
Hell, I’ll sell *ten copies* to your grandma, Jeremy. She’ll thank me for the fuzz.

**JIM**
And that’s when the lawsuits begin.

**GILLEY**
Or the merch drops.

*FADE OUT on the band laughing again—but now with purpose, with direction, and with the terrifying realization that their first full piece of original art is a Wiccan sex rite committed to fuzz pedal and wax—and they’re about to sell it to Ohio.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY GARAGE – 4:34 P.M. – THE BRAND STRATEGY QUESTION**

Everyone’s still reeling from the decision to go vinyl, Gilley already dreaming about marketing schemes.

**BILL** (raises a hand like it’s a board meeting)
Quick clarification.

(Everyone turns.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
So… just so I understand the direction:

**Commuted** now means **subversive lyrics**,  **absolute bangers**,  *and yet*—zero on the actual presentation of sex appeal?

(Beat.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
No leather, no abs, no sweaty thirst traps?

**KATHY** (flat)
You want a thirst trap, Bill?

**BILL**
I just wanna know what’s expected of me.  Am I wearing mesh? Am I *not* wearing mesh?

**JIM**
That is a serious question.

**GILLEY**
Guys. Focus. We’re not porn stars.

**KATHY**
Speak for yourself.

**JEFF**
The *lyrics* are the sex.

**BILL**
Okay but like… the visuals?

**KATHY**
Disgusting. Stark. Mundane.  Like a kitchen table with a used towel on it.

**JEREMY (EVANS)**
That’s so gross.

**KATHY**
Exactly.

*FADE OUT on Bill slowly nodding, half-horrified, half-inspired, already imagining the band’s first album cover featuring nothing but a crumpled paper napkin and a Polaroid of an outlet mall.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY GARAGE – 4:36 P.M. – JEFF EXPLAINS THE ORIGIN**

The conversation has drifted into merch and aesthetics. Gilley’s sketching logos. Kathy’s talking about typography. Jeff interrupts.

**JEFF**
Just so everyone understands—

(Beat.)

The song I wrote?  It’s a consequence of my **morning masturbation session.**

(Dead silence.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
I was lying there, staring at the ceiling.  Covered.  Cum splatter on my chest. Some hit the blanket. Some caught the edge of the page of a book.

(He pauses, searching for the right tone.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
And I thought… *this is so narratively empty in modern media.*

**JIM** (gagging)
Oh my God.

**BILL**
Shut up. Shut. Up.

**JEFF**
No one talks about the **physical presence**.  The **viscosity.**  The **aftermath.**  It’s always just cut to black, fade to credits, giggle giggle. But what about the guy lying there wondering why he bothered?

**JEREMY**
Jeff, you’re describing *jism*.

**JEFF**
I’m describing **texture**.

**GILLEY** (half-laughing, half-horrified)
This is worse than I imagined, and I *already* imagined you jerking off while writing lyrics.

**KATHY** (flatly, but not surprised)
This is what separates him from other writers.

**JEFF**
Thank you.

(Beat.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
The song came from that moment.  Not the orgasm— but the **dissatisfaction** with how it would be **dismissed** by the culture.

*FADE OUT on the band staring at him, some in awe, some in disgust, and one or two—very likely Kathy—beginning to realize that Jeff isn’t writing lyrics. **He’s exorcising cultural denial. Through cum.***

---

## **INT. GILLEY GARAGE – 4:38 P.M. – KATHY THROWS THE GAUNTLET**

Jeff finishes his monologue about masturbation and modern media.

The band is in stunned, disturbed silence.

**KATHY** (quiet, ominous)
You just wait, gentlemen.

(She paces once. Looks at each of them.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
You think this is the ceiling?

(She taps the lyric sheet.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
She’ll top them.

**JIM**
Please don’t.

**KATHY**
She’ll top them, and you’ll all see.

**BILL**
Is that a threat? A prophecy?

**GILLEY**
It’s a **promise**, bro.

**KATHY**
I’ll write it overnight.  And it’ll **slay**.

(She’s not smiling.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
You’re gonna beg me to record it.  You’re gonna weep for it to exist on vinyl.

**JEREMY**
I’m scared.

**JEFF** (grinning, sincere)
I’m excited.

**JIM**
I’m reconsidering my entire relationship to songwriting.

**KATHY**
Good.

(She walks to the door, notebook under her arm.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
I’m going home.  Don’t call me. Don’t text me.  I’ll be busy becoming **unstoppable.**

*FADE OUT on the boys exchanging terrified glances—because Kathy isn’t bluffing. And tomorrow? Tomorrow she returns with fire, filth, and divinity inked in her own hand.*

---

# **CHAPTER NINE: TURNING ALL THE NIGHT TIME INTO THE DAY**

---

## **EXT. THE ESPICH HOUSE – BACKYARD – 5:12 P.M.**

The sun is warm. The crickets are humming.  The below-ground pool gurgles gently in the background. Kathy is sprawled on a **chase chair**, wearing a **two-piece bikini**, hair still damp from a quick rinse, towel folded behind her neck. Her legs are tan. Her body at rest.  But her **brain is on fire.** She stares up at the sky, jaw tight, notebook unopened in her lap.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
What the hell am I gonna write about?

(Pause. Her fingers tap the notebook once.)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
How does *he* do it?

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**
That nerdy fuck. No emotion. No fear.  Just shoots cum on his stomach and comes up with a fucking *masterpiece.*

She exhales sharply. Sits up halfway. Adjusts her top. Scowls.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
And me? I’m the one with the *ovaries*. I’m the one who’s lived through every type of pain, every disappointment, every goddamn myth about what it means to be a woman in this cracked-out culture.

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**
He doesn’t even care.

(She glares at her notebook.)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
I care too much.

(Silence.)

Then—she smiles. Just a little.

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**
Okay, bitch. Let’s see what that gets you.

(She clicks her pen. Opens to a fresh page.)

*FADE OUT on Kathy in the sun, bikini-clad, sun-warmed, and ready to carve her name into the same ledger Jeff just defiled. Because she’s coming for blood—and she’s gonna look radiant doing it.*

---

## **EXT. ESPICH BACKYARD – LATE AFTERNOON SUN**

The notebook is open. The pen’s in her hand.  But Kathy hasn’t written a word yet. She chews the cap.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Write what you know.  Write what you know.  Jesus Christ, what do I even *know*? She stares at the pool water, eyes narrowing.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
I know I deal with sons of bitches.  I know **men**.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
But not the kind that fuck you good and ghost you.  The kind that **sigh at the counter** because their **balance is short** and they **blame you.** She sighs.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
I know **fake empathy**. I know how to smile and say *“I’m so sorry to hear that”* like a goddamn algorithm. I know the exact weight of a thousand dollars in twenties.  I know which regulars try to flirt with me using their social security check. I know **how to hand people their own money** and still have them think I owe them something. She scribbles a phrase.

*“Your balance is not sufficient, sir.”*

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Maybe that's the chorus.

She snorts.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
*‘Insufficient Funds.’*  Is that a title? A threat? A prophecy?

She starts writing faster.

*“He walks in like the vault owes him tribute.*
*He leaves without looking back.*
*I count his ones, his sighs, his expectations.*
*And all he wants is change.”*

Kathy smiles now. A different kind of smile.  **Sharp. Honest. Lethal.**

---

## **EXT. ESPICH BACKYARD – 5:44 P.M. – THE NAME HITS**

Kathy’s pen stops moving mid-sentence.  She blinks. A shadow moves across her face—not the sun. A memory.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Flyboy.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
A nickname.  A *spit-laced*, *derisive* nickname.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Flyboy.

(She taps the pen on the edge of the notebook.)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Air National Guard. Springfield.  He looked good in the uniform.  Not so much out of it. She writes the name at the top of the page. All caps.

**FLYBOY.**

**KATHY (V.O.)**
The one I fucked last summer.  The one who had the *temerity*—  to **critique my head game.**

(Beat.)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Flyboy.

She underlines it once.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
The one who *tried to dominate me* with a grunt and a grimace,  then had the balls to *complain.*

(She’s sitting up straighter now. Her jaw’s set.)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Flyboy. The one I kicked out of bed without warning.  No shoes, no ride, no goodbye.  Just “Get the fuck out,”  and the slamming of the door. She starts writing again.

*“Flyboy came to land but I gave him sky.*
*Tried to call it turbulence, but I knew it was just weak thrust.”*

Her lips curl into a grin.  This won’t be a sad song. It’s going to be **a drag strip execution.**

*FADE OUT on Kathy underlining Flyboy again, her pen gouging the paper, legs crossed, ink flying, and her smile saying: Jeff may have written about sex—but I’m writing about war.**

---

## **EXT. ESPICH BACKYARD – 5:47 P.M. – THE CRYSTALIZATION**

Kathy flips to a clean page.  She’s still thinking about him.  His awkward rhythm. His critical tone.  The way he acted like *he* was the prize.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
What a dumbass.

That’s it.

Not “he hurt me.”  Not “he made me question myself.”  Just—

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**
*What a dumbass.*

She writes it down.  Bottom of the page. All caps.

**WHAT A DUMBASS.**

That might be the chorus.

*FADE OUT on Kathy with sunglasses now slid down her nose, grinning like a girl who just pulled the pin out of the next song and is letting it cook.*

---

## **EXT. ESPICH BACKYARD – 5:51 P.M. – RHYME-HUNTING RAGE**

Kathy’s scribbling across the top margin of the page.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Dumbass in my bed.

(Beat.)

Needs to rhyme with **giving head.**

She taps her pen furiously.

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**
This would be easier if I had *half a lobotomy and a Y chromosome.*

(Beat.)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Jeff makes this look way too easy.

(Beat. Then—)

She jots:

*“Dumbass in my bed / talkin’ shit ‘bout givin’ head / like he earned the crown and the thread / but couldn’t keep time if I counted instead.”*

She blinks. Then grins.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Oh.  Oh we’re *cooking* now.

---

## **EXT. ESPICH BACKYARD – 6:42 P.M. – EARLY EVENING, FULL SUNLIGHT**

The sky is still wide open, sun blazing low but **nowhere near gone**.  The air has thickened—**evening humidity rolling in**, but the light is clear, golden, and endless. Kathy stretches one leg out on the vinyl of the chase chair, squinting into the still-hot sky.

Her notebook is full of fire:  **Verses jagged, honest, brutal.**  Flyboy has been torn to pieces, line by line.

But in the middle of the page— **a blank spot.**

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Still no chorus.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**
Sun’s still high.  Plenty of light.  But nothing’s landing.

She scribbles a line. Crosses it out.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
I’ve written about his thrust.  His grunt. His goddamn tactical vest.  But the hook—that thing that drills into your chest?  Still missing. She leans her head back. Eyes closed.  The wind moves the maple leaves. Her thighs are damp from the chair.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Maybe it’s not clever.  Maybe it’s just *true.*

She jots something quick. Unpolished.

**“Don’t come back. / I’m not your barracks.”**

She stares at it.

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**
…Maybe.

*FADE OUT on Kathy leaning forward again, golden light striping her skin, her pen beginning to move—because the night isn’t even close yet, and she’s not done swinging.*

---

## **EXT. ESPICH BACKYARD – 6:51 P.M. – MID-SUMMER HUMIDITY**

Kathy’s leaning forward in the lounge chair, writing fast now.  Notebook half full. Bikini straps slightly shifted. Pen gripped like a knife. Then—**the screen door slides open**.

**JO AN DEMME:** (cheerfully)
You’re gonna burn, baby.

Kathy doesn’t look up.

**KATHY**
I’m fine.

**JO AN DEMME:**
You’re not. You’re medium-rare already.

She steps out barefoot, wearing her own **bikini**, towel draped over her shoulder, sunglasses on, wisps of pubic hair out. She grabs the bottle of suntan lotion from the side table Fairand tosses it to Kathy.

**JO AN DEMME (CONT’D)**
Put that on before you look like a lobster.

Kathy rolls her eyes *so hard it’s audible*.

**KATHY**
You treat me like I’m a kid.

**JO AN DEMME:**
That’s because you **are** a kid.

(She sits down with a sigh.)

**JO AN DEMME (CONT’D)**
Now lube up before your shoulders blister and you can’t play your guitar.

Kathy mutters something under her breath but **uncaps the bottle anyway**. As she slathers it on, her notebook sticks briefly to her thigh.  She peels it off, frowning.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
How the hell am I supposed to write a feminist war cry when I’m being told to moisturize?

Her mom adjusts her sunglasses.

**JO AN DEMME:**
You working on another one of your songs?

**KATHY**
Yeah.

**JO AN DEMME:**
Make sure it doesn’t sound like screaming this time.  Your Aunt Dee thought y’all were summoning Satan.

**KATHY** (smiling despite herself)
That’s the point.

*FADE OUT on two generations in bikinis—one plotting lyrical vengeance, the other preventing sunburn. Because even a revolutionary lives at home sometimes.*

---

## **EXT. ESPICH BACKYARD – 7:04 P.M. – MOTHER AND DAUGHTER, LOTION AND LYRICS**

Kathy reclines again, notebook resting on her stomach.
She hums something. Then sings a bar out loud—gritty, raw, full of spite.

**KATHY** (singing)
*Dumbass in my bed, talkin’ shit ‘bout givin’ head—*

**JO AN DEMME:** (stopping her mid-bar)
Okay, okay.

(She waves a hand like fanning off heat.)

**JO AN DEMME (CONT’D)**
Where’s the **poetry**, baby?

Kathy blinks.

**KATHY**
The poetry?

**JO AN DEMME:**
Where’s the **imagery**? The **metaphor**?  You’re just blasting through it like you’re trying to *run through a brick wall*.

(She sits up, towel on her lap.)

**JO AN DEMME (CONT’D)**
I didn’t raise a **bulldozer** for nothing.  You're going to that fancy **Clark Tech**, right?

**KATHY**
Community college, Mom.

**JO AN DEMME:**
Still costs money. You’re learning something, aren’t you?

(She taps the notebook.)

**JO AN DEMME (CONT’D)**
Then **show it off.**  Don’t just tell me he’s a dumbass.  Make me **see** it. Make me **feel** it.  Twist the knife with something pretty.

Kathy stares at her, quiet now.

**KATHY**
You actually want me to make it worse?

**JO AN DEMME:**
I want you to make it **art**.

*FADE OUT on Kathy turning her head back to the notebook, eyes sharp now. Because maybe her mom's not just the sunscreen enforcer—maybe she’s the unexpected editor she needed.*

---

## **EXT. ESPICH BACKYARD – 7:11 P.M. – REAL TALK, SPF 50 EDITION**

Kathy is scribbling again—redrafting the verse with a little more grace, a little more dagger. Her mother watches for a second, then quietly speaks.

**JO AN DEMME:**
Flyboy, huh?

Kathy freezes mid-stroke.

**KATHY**
I didn’t say his name.

**JO AN DEMME:**
You didn’t have to.  *“Air National Guard in Springfield, last summer, dress blues, thinks he’s God’s gift to women”…*

(She shrugs.)

**JO AN DEMME (CONT’D)**
I can connect the dots.

**KATHY**
I didn’t think it mattered.

**JO AN DEMME:**
Well, it does.  And this is the first I’m hearing about this Flyboy prick.

(She sits upright, more serious now.)

**JO AN DEMME (CONT’D)**
And if I’d known last year?  Maybe I would’ve said something.

(Beat.)

**JO AN DEMME (CONT’D)**
Because you live under **my roof**, young lady.  And if you’re gonna keep parading your sexual escapades through my pool, my kitchen, my laundry room—

**KATHY**
Mom!

**JO AN DEMME:**
—then I’d appreciate being kept in the **loop.**

(She gives Kathy the look. The full mom stare.)

**JO AN DEMME (CONT’D)**
My house.  My rules.  My roof.

(She raises an eyebrow.)

**JO AN DEMME (CONT’D)**
Like it or leave.

Kathy exhales sharply through her nose.  Then flips to a fresh page.

**KATHY**
I’m keeping that line.

**JO AN DEMME:**
Which one?

**KATHY**
*“My house, my rules, my roof.”*
It’s perfect.

*FADE OUT on mother and daughter in the golden July light—one crossing her arms with practiced authority, the other weaponizing maternal boundaries into future lyrics. Because Kathy may be the one holding the pen, but **her mom just handed her the hook.***

---

## **EXT. ESPICH BACKYARD – 7:41 P.M. – THE WALL HITS**

Kathy hasn’t moved in half an hour. The sun is still bright.  The notebook is still open.  But the pen? It’s been chewing on the same half-rhyme since 7:12. She exhales loudly. Frustrated.

**KATHY**
Ugh. Nothing’s landing.  It’s like my brain is *jammed.*

**JO AN DEMME:** (calmer than the lawn)
That’s probably because you’re in your right mind.

Kathy looks over.

**KATHY**
Excuse me?

**JO AN DEMME:** (tilting her sunglasses down)
Well, maybe if you got yourself a **wine cooler** and just… *relaxed a little*—it might loosen your **tongue**.  And maybe even loosen your **quill**.

**KATHY** (suspiciously)
Do you speak from experience, Mom?

Her mom smiles.

**JO AN DEMME:**
It also kind of loosens your **zipper control**, but we’re not gonna talk about that.

**KATHY** (groaning)
MOM!

**JO AN DEMME:** (tipping her shades back up)
I’m just saying. Passion and prose go down smoother with peach mango and a little bad decision-making.

Kathy finally laughs.

**KATHY**
You’re the weirdest muse in the tri-county area.

*FADE OUT on the lawn bathed in gold, a half-open notebook still waiting for ink, and a woman who might just hit lyrical genius if she lets Seagram’s guide her hand.*

---

## **EXT. ESPICH BACKYARD – 7:52 P.M. – PEACH MANGO REVELATION**

The bottle’s cold in her hand. The sky is glowing with that late-July haze.
Kathy takes a long swig of her first **Peach Mango Seagram’s Escape**, grimaces, and sets it down beside the chair.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
My gift was diminished.

(She scrawls it. Underlines it.)

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**
That sounds… cool. Kinda broken. Kinda dramatic. Yeah.

She leans into the page.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
*Flyboy, so lordly.*
*Dumbass in my bed.*

(Pause.)

She puts her pen down.

**KATHY**
Oh, Jesus H. Christ, this is hard.

Her mom looks over, bemused.

**JO AN DEMME:**
How’s the wine cooler treating you?

**KATHY**
It’s **not writing the chorus for me**, that’s for damn sure.

**JO AN DEMME:**
It’s a wine cooler, honey. Not a ghostwriter.

**KATHY** (half-laughing)
Ugh.

(She picks up the bottle. Takes another swig.)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
*Flyboy, so lordly.*
That’s something. There’s *judgment* in that. *Tone*. Maybe that's the entry point.

She writes again. Faster now. The wine cooler **isn't magic**, but it’s **just enough to let her stop thinking about Jeff.**

*FADE OUT on Kathy slumped in the chair, bare feet brushing the warm concrete, notebook tilted just right, the first hint of the chorus cracking through like thunder on the horizon.*

---

## **EXT. ESPICH BACKYARD – 8:07 P.M. – THE CHORUS LANDS**

Kathy’s foot is bouncing. Her eyes wide. Bottle half-empty.

She’s scribbling faster now, ink smearing slightly on the page.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
*Flyboy, so lordly.*
*Dumbass in my bed.*
*Moment of delight, after we finished.*
*Now it feels like my gift was diminished.*

She stares at it.  It holds.

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**
That’s it.  That’s my chorus.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Now I’m just missing… I don’t know.  Three verses and the **truth**?

She reads the chorus under her breath, lips barely moving.

**JO AN DEMME:** (from her chair)
What on earth are you writing about?

Kathy freezes.  Staring down at her words.

**KATHY**
Nothing.

**JO AN DEMME:**
That didn’t sound like nothing.

Kathy sits up, brushing her hair back, flushed—not from the sun.

**KATHY**
It’s… just something from last year.

**JO AN DEMME:**
Flyboy?

**KATHY**
Yeah.

**JO AN DEMME:**
The one who—

**KATHY** (interrupting)
Yeah.

(She looks away.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
I’m trying to turn it into something that doesn’t feel so… stupid.  Something I can hold. That’s mine.

Her mom tilts her head. Watches her for a moment. Then nods.

**JO AN DEMME:**
Well, keep going.  Because right now?

(Beat.)

**JO AN DEMME (CONT’D)**
It sounds like it’s finally starting to sound like *you.*

*FADE OUT on Kathy lowering her head back to the page, pen in hand, the chorus humming in her skull, the shame receding just enough to let her keep digging.*

---

## **EXT. ESPICH BACKYARD – 8:15 P.M. – THE STRATEGIC RUG DOCTRINE**

Kathy is staring at her notebook. The chorus is tight.  But the verses still feel flat. Her mother, reclined in her chair, watches her daughter wrestle with the page.

**JO AN DEMME:**
You want some imagery?

**KATHY** (sighing)
Yeah, sure. Enlighten me.

Her mom sips her drink, then sets it down.

**JO AN DEMME:**
Picture this:  Your own kitchen. One day, when you're rich and famous.  Nice place. Sunlight. Big windows. Fancy cabinets.  And right in the middle?

(Pause.)

**JO AN DEMME (CONT’D)**
A beautiful rug. Plush. Clean. Comfortable.  Something soft. For your knees.

Kathy looks up, slightly horrified.

**KATHY**
Mom—

**JO AN DEMME:**
You get down on your knees, baby.  Give him everything.  Make him feel like the center of the goddamn universe.

(Pause.)

**JO AN DEMME (CONT’D)**
And *then*—he disrespects you.

(She leans forward, eyes gleaming.)

**JO AN DEMME (CONT’D)**
That’s when you grab the edge of the rug— and yank.

(Beat.)

**JO AN DEMME (CONT’D)**
He goes **ass-over-teakettle**.  Dick out. Ego shattered. Knees skinned.

Kathy is halfway between choking and laughing.

**KATHY**
That is *so fucked up.*

**JO AN DEMME:**
That’s **life**.

(She raises her bottle.)

**JO AN DEMME (CONT’D)**
Men have all these ideas, honey.  Fake skin. Fake tits. Fake moans.  Fake forgiveness.

**KATHY**
And fake control.

**JO AN DEMME:**
Exactly.

(She reclines again.)

**JO AN DEMME (CONT’D)**
You want a verse? There’s your **carpet scene.**

*FADE OUT on Kathy scribbling “knees, rug, yank” in bold strokes across the top of a clean page, and her mother watching, victorious. Because the rug isn’t just furniture—it’s a trap. And she taught her daughter how to set it.*

---

## **EXT. ESPICH BACKYARD – 8:18 P.M. – THE T.M.I. BOMB DROPS**

Kathy is furiously writing now. She’s got a title. She’s got a chorus. She’s got a **revenge carpet metaphor** dripping with genius. Her mother sips the last of her wine cooler and sighs, satisfied.

**JO AN DEMME:**
You know…a well-timed rug yank can really clear up a misunderstanding.

Kathy glances over warily.

**KATHY**
Mom—

**JO AN DEMME:**
I mean, *I* wouldn’t know anything about that *personally*, of course.  But… let’s just say your father wasn’t the first man to find himself **horizontal and humbled**.

(Pause.)

**MRS. ESPICH (CONT’D)**
Back in my day.

Kathy slaps the notebook closed.

**KATHY**
NOPE. Nope. We are not doing this.  We’re not going down *memory lane, vagina edition.*

**JO AN DEMME:** (casual)
I’m just saying, honey—*history repeats.*

**KATHY**
Yeah, and if you don’t stop talking, I’m going to carve mine into your rug.

**JO AN DEMME:** (as she stands, stretching)
That’s the spirit.

*FADE OUT on Kathy muttering “Jesus Christ” as she reopens her notebook, trying to shake the image of her mother weaponizing sexuality in the Reagan years—while secretly knowing she’s going to use that exact rug metaphor in verse two.*

---

# **CHAPTER TEN: VIOLENCE & DOUBLE TALK**

---
## **INT. KATHY’S BEDROOM – 1:41 A.M. – CRISIS MODE**

Kathy is curled up on her bed, legs under a twisted blanket, notebook tossed half-shut beside her.  The light from the bedside lamp is warm and dim, and she looks **wrecked.**

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Still up. Still failing.

(Beat.)

She stares at the ceiling.

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**
Jeff probably wrote three more songs by now.  With his eyes closed.  Dick in hand.  On a fucking unicycle.

She groans and covers her face.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Okay. Okay.  Who can help?

She flips through mental images of her bandmates.

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**
Not Jeremy. God, no.  Not Jim. He’d panic.  Not Gilley—he’d *use it against me.*

(Beat.)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Bill.

(Another pause.)

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**
Why Bill?

She reaches for her phone, already dialing.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Because Bill’ll keep his motherfuckin' fuckin' motherfuckin' motherfuckin' fuckin' motherfuckin' mouth **shut** if I ask him nicely.

The line starts ringing.

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**
Grit your teeth. Be kind.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Otherwise, this is gonna be a really short **fucking** call.

She swallows hard.

**KATHY (out loud)**
Be cool, Espich. Just be cool.

*FADE OUT on the ringing tone, her hand clenched tight around the phone, knowing full well that **Bill’s not her first choice—but he’s her only shot.***

---

## **INT. BILL’S ROOM – 1:42 A.M. – PHONE CALL, DARKNESS, ONE EAR OPEN**

The room is mostly dark, just a lava lamp pulsing slowly in the corner. Bill is shirtless, curled in a tangle of flannel sheets, glasses still on, Walkman headphones around his neck, not even playing. The phone rings again. He groans.

**BILL**
Jesus.

(He picks up, eyes half-open.)

**BILL**
Yeah?

**KATHY (PHONE, RASPY)**
Hey. Sorry. I know. Late. It’s late. I know.

**BILL**
It’s **tomorrow**. What’s up?

**KATHY (PHONE)**
I’ve been at it for **seven hours**.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (PHONE)**
Seven. Fucking. Hours.

Bill rubs his eyes.

**BILL**
And?

**KATHY (PHONE)**
All I’ve got is the chorus. And everything else feels like garbage.  The verses won’t breathe.  They don’t move.  It’s just anger and carpet metaphors.

**BILL** (deep sigh)
Well… give me the chorus.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (PHONE)**
You promise not to laugh?

**BILL**
Kathy.

(Beat.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
I’m half-naked, half-asleep, and legally bound not to mock you past midnight.  Now give me the chorus.

*FADE OUT on Kathy taking a breath, about to read the one part of the song that’s worked—because Bill’s not judging, he’s listening. And **this might be the moment it all clicks.***

---

## **INT. BILL’S ROOM – 1:45 A.M. – CHORUS DELIVERY**

Bill sits up now, propped on an elbow, sheets kicked off, phone cradled between shoulder and jaw.

**KATHY (PHONE)**
Okay.  You asked for it.

(She takes a breath. And then—sings.)

**KATHY (singing, low and sharp):**
*Flyboy, so lordly.*
*Dumbass in my bed.*
*Moment of delight, after we finished.*
*Now it feels like my gift was diminished.*

The line crackles with cheap phone static. There’s a pause.

Then:

**BILL**
That’s… pretty good.

(Beat.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
I mean, I can **tell** you’re pissed.

(Another pause.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
…By the way—Who the fuck is **Flyboy**?

*FADE OUT on Kathy sitting cross-legged on her bed, lit only by a desk lamp and bad choices, holding the phone like it might burst into flames, trying to decide whether to tell him the truth or just say it’s a composite. Meanwhile, Bill leans back into the pillow, smiling faintly, because for all her pain, **that was a hell of a chorus.***

---

## **INT. KATHY’S BEDROOM – 1:47 A.M. – NO ROOM FOR QUESTIONS**

Kathy stares at her notebook, the pen resting in the spiral binding. Phone to her ear. Eyes fixed ahead. Bill waits quietly on the other end.

**KATHY (flat, deliberate)**
Flyboy is someone who is never going to stain my sheets ever again.

(Beat.)

**KATHY** (CONT’D)
And I would **prefer** never to have that question asked again.

(Silence.)

Bill breathes once through his nose.  Doesn’t laugh. Doesn’t poke.

**BILL** (gently)
Copy that.

(Beat.)

**BILL** (CONT’D)
Chorus still kicks mucho ass.

*FADE OUT on Kathy closing the notebook, laying back on her bed with her chest rising and falling fast, the chorus looping in her brain, and the line about stained sheets echoing back like a line she’ll never put in the song—but one she’ll never forget.*

---

## **INT. BILL’S BEDROOM – 1:50 A.M. – A HARD TRUTH**

There’s a silence on the line. Kathy hasn’t replied since the “don’t ask me again” declaration. Bill sits back, watching the red numbers on his clock radio tick toward 1:51.
Then he speaks—carefully, but clearly.

**BILL**
Hey, Kathy?

(Pause.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
Are you viewing this as a competition?

(Beat.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
Because if you are— If you’re trying to **beat Jeff**—

(Sighs.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
You’re gonna lose.

(Silence. He keeps going.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
You’re gonna lose every day of the week.  Because Jeff isn’t… *normal.*

**KATHY (PHONE)** (sullen)
Thanks.

**BILL**
No, seriously.  He’s not even *of this world*.

(Beat.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
He’s a **freak**.

**KATHY (PHONE)** (still quiet)
You’re not helping.

**BILL**
I *am* helping.  You’re trying to out-swim a fucking nuclear submarine. That’s not how this works.

(Pause.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
Write the thing only **you** can write.  Not the thing you think’ll *one-up* Jeff.

*FADE OUT on Kathy sitting still in the dim light, processing—not angry, not even hurt, just trying to reroute. Because Bill didn’t say she’s not good enough. He said she’s not him. And that might be exactly what she needed to hear.*

---

## **INT. KATHY’S BEDROOM – 2:09 A.M. – NIGHT BRAIN, FULL SPIN**

The notebook is closed. The lights are off. The ceiling fan spins above her, a lazy click every third rotation. Kathy lies flat on her back, the phone long since hung up, her comforter bunched at her feet. Her eyes are open.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Write what you know.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**
Savage.

No scream. No flourish. No rebellion. Just the sentence.  **The most brutal sentence her English professor ever dropped.**

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Because what do I know?

(Beat.)

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**
Flyboy.  Shit jobs.  Fake smiles.  Being called “feisty” by men twice my age.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
I know how it feels to be reduced.  To be underestimated.  To get praised for resilience like that’s some kind of *prize*. She exhales. Eyes closed now.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Bill’s right.  Jeff’s a *freak*.  He writes like a ghost whispering to himself from another planet.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**
But me? I write like I’ve been ignored in plain sight.

(Pause.)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
And maybe that’s its own kind of magic.

*FADE OUT on Kathy’s breathing slowing, the chorus echoing softly in her mind like a lullaby wrapped in fire. She hasn’t won. But she hasn’t lost either. Tomorrow, the page will still be there. And now, maybe, so will the truth.*

---

## **INT. KATHY’S BEDROOM – 2:23 A.M. – TITLE REVEALED**

She rolls onto her side. The bedsheet tangled between her legs.  Notebook inches away but untouched. She glares into the dark.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
I’m not taking kindly to this advice.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**
It’s not working. Bill meant well.  He always does. But it just…

**KATHY (V.O.)**
It’s not hitting.

She closes her eyes harder, like trying to shut her brain off by force.

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**
Didn’t take kindly to Flyboy either.  Didn’t take kindly to his little review.  Didn’t take kindly to my own failure to deliver.

(Pause.)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Didn’t take kindly to being in a **competition** I never signed up for. Her eyes snap open.  She turns, reaches for the notebook in the dark, flips it open and writes the phrase fast, jagged.

**NOT TAKEN KINDLY**

All caps. No apology. She stares at it.  Breathes.  Smiles.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
That’s the title.

*FADE OUT on Kathy finally turning off her lamp, the words still fresh on the page, ink still wet. She hasn’t written the verses yet—but now she knows what she’s writing toward. It’s not just a breakup song. It’s not just revenge. It’s a line in the dirt:*

**Don’t fuck with me.**  **Because I don’t take kindly.**

---

## **INT. KATHY’S BEDROOM – 3:14 A.M. – GOETHE O’CLOCK**

The fan hums. The room is quiet.  Kathy stares at the ceiling like it insulted her family.  She turns. Checks the clock.  

**3:14 a.m.**

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Fuck this.

She throws the blanket off, slides out of bed, and heads to her bookshelf barefoot. Half a dozen dog-eared paperbacks line the shelf—**punk memoirs, Joan Didion, Anne Sexton, Sylvia Plath**—And then…**Johann Wolfgang von Goethe.** *Faust.* The edition with the yellowed pages and her professor’s scrawls in the margins.  She pulls it down.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
If I’m gonna be tortured, I might as well do it with company. She climbs back into bed, lamp on low, and flips to a familiar passage. Her lips move silently as she reads:

“*Two souls, alas, are dwelling in my breast,*
*And each is fain to leave its brother*.”

She exhales.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Yeah. That tracks.

She keeps reading, eyes narrowing, the rhythm of the language beginning to soften her edges. Not lull her. Not yet.  But ground her.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Maybe this is what Bill meant.

*FADE OUT on Kathy curled in bed, one leg half out of the blanket, a highlighter tucked behind her ear, reading Goethe by lamplight like it’s a mixtape only she remembers how to play.*

---

## **INT. KATHY’S BEDROOM – 3:43 A.M. – UNINTENTIONAL POETRY**

Goethe’s open on her lap.  The lamplight is soft. Her legs are curled under her comforter now, body finally beginning to relax. She grabs the notebook. Not with purpose—just instinct.  Scrawls a few lines without thinking.

*I remember that summer.*
*The spark in the air.*
*No worries. No care.*

(Beat.)

*Now, it’s just silence.*
*A chasm so wide.*
*Can we find that rhythm?*
*Or… do I just hide?*

She stares at it.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Maybe this shit is that easy.

She squints.

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**
No metaphor. No climax.  No blood on the carpet. Just… longing.

(Beat.)

And it works. She sighs and flops back into her pillows, annoyed and impressed at herself.

**KATHY**
I hate when I’m good on accident.

*FADE OUT on her notebook lying open, the page half-filled with a ghost of something tender, something real. No fire. No vengeance. Just a memory and a question—and maybe that’s enough.*

---

## **INT. KATHY’S BEDROOM – 4:01 A.M. – CHORUS (VERSION 2.0)**

Kathy’s back upright in bed, one leg hanging off, her notebook now littered with crossed-out fragments and rising confidence. She whispers it aloud, half-rapping, half-spitting, pen tapping the paper.

**KATHY (whispering)**
*Post-nut clarity.*
*You don't like my head?*
*Flyboy, so lordly.*
*Dumbass in my bed.*

(Beat.)

*Moment of delight.*
*After we finished—*
*Now it feels like my gift was diminished.*

She pauses. Eyes wide.  Smiles.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
This is starting to cook.

She reads it again. This time with venom. And rhythm. And **grimace.**

**KATHY (V.O.)**
This is me.

Not trying to be Jeff.  Not trying to win.  Just telling the **ugly, mean, hilarious truth**.
She underlines “Post-nut clarity.” Twice.

*FADE OUT on Kathy sitting up straighter, sheet wrapped around her, notebook like a sword in her lap, and the sun just barely teasing at the edge of the blinds.*

---

## **INT. KATHY’S BEDROOM – 4:14 A.M. – THE SECOND LINE CRISIS**

Kathy’s hair is a mess. One strap of her tank top is off her shoulder. The lamp’s still on, and her pen is tapping the page like a metronome trying to beat her into submission.  She murmurs the line to herself.

**KATHY (muttering)**
*So here I am, panting.*
*Cum just swallowed.*

(Beat.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
*Boggled so deeply.*
*Bitter words…*

(She stares.)

**KATHY**
…Swallowed.

(Dead pause.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Goddamn it.

She slaps the notebook lightly.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
I can’t use *swallowed* twice. That’s lazy. That's the freshman tier.

She rewinds.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
“Bitter words… followed?”

(Tries it aloud.)

**KATHY**
No. Sounds like I’m marching behind a parade of insults.

She flips to a margin and scribbles alternates.

* Muffled
* Choked
* Recoiled
* Curled
* Engraved
* **Echoed?**

She groans.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Shoot.  Jeff makes this so easy.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
He'd just *see* the line. Like it's written in fog. Then read it back like a fucking oracle. She leans back.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Okay. Okay.  I’ll find the word.  But it won’t be *swallowed*. She draws a line through it. Firm. Violent.  Then immediately writes it again in the margin.

*FADE OUT on Kathy swearing at verbs, chasing meter through fatigue, and refusing to let this line go unfinished. Because this song is going to hurt—but it's going to be **perfect**.*

---

## **INT. KATHY’S BEDROOM – 4:31 A.M. – THE OUTRO HITS**

She’s hunched over the notebook again, bare feet planted on the carpet, pen stabbing syllables like a bayonet. And then—She writes it.  Reads it out loud.  Once.

**KATHY (growling, triumphant)**
*“But if I don't thrill you, where's the fun in this fuck?*
*You self-absorbed shit.*
*I leave guys dumbstruck!”*

She stares at the page. Then—grins.

**KATHY**
That’s it.

(She falls back into her pillows.)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
That’s the outro.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Now we just cruise out.  Guitar’s sliding low.  Drums easing off the gas.  Bass line winking goodbye.  Slide right out…

(She smiles.)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Slide right outta someone’s bed.

(She mimics it.)

**KATHY (softly)**
“Get the fuck out, sir.”

(Beat.)

**KATHY**
*That’s the ticket.*

She looks down at her bed, her lap, her floor—**ten pages of handwritten wreckage**, verses and scraps, scratched-out lines and triumphant stanzas.

**KATHY**
Fuck.

She leans over, gathers the pages into a pile, and fans them out like a hand of winning cards.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
I did it.

(Grins wider.)

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**
And it’s *better* than Jeff’s.

(She freezes.)

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**
Okay. Maybe not better.

(Shrugs.)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
But it’s mine.

*FADE OUT on Kathy staring at the final line, feeling the burn of caffeine and spite wear off into a gentle glow. Because she didn’t just write a song—she took back the narrative. She didn’t thrill him?*

**Good.**  **Then she’ll thrill the fucking world.**

---

## **INT. KATHY’S BEDROOM – 4:07 A.M. – CRASH LANDING**

The pages are spread across the bed. Some on the floor.  Her pen rests on the windowsill. Forgotten. She’s staring at the pile of work like it’s something she just coughed up.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Ten pages?

Half-written.  Out of order.  The full song? *Technically, yeah.* But it’s a mess. A fractured, stitched-together, bloody **mess**. She pulls her knees up to her chest, hugging them.

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**
It’s four o’clock in the morning.  My back hurts.  My fingers are ink-stained.  My lips are dry.  My mind’s **fractured.**

(Beat.)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
And how did I get here?

She closes her eyes.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Because I’m in a competition. With **Jeff.**

(Beat.)

With a guy who *jerked off*, wrote a song about it, and **blew everyone’s fucking mind.**

She opens her eyes, cold now.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
And I thought I could top that. I thought I could out-fuck it. Out-write it.  Out-bleed it.  But this?  This isn’t art.

(She looks at the lyrics again.)

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**
This is spite.

She shoves the pages off her lap. They scatter.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
This is a tantrum in verse form.

She turns off the lamp.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
I can’t stand this.  I can’t stand *me*.

(Silence.)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
I’m not better than him.  But I should be better than this.

*FADE OUT on Kathy curling up, turned away from the chaos on the bed, the pages strewn like crime scene debris. No sleep comes. Only silence. The lyrics are written. But her soul’s not in them. Not yet.*

---

## **INT. KATHY’S BEDROOM – 7:00 A.M. – RETURN TO EARTH**

**BEEP BEEP BEEP BEEP.**

The alarm clock explodes into the room, savage and indifferent. Kathy groans—long, deep, sloth-like. Her arm shoots out and slaps the button. Silence returns. She stares at the ceiling. Eyes bloodshot. Barely blinking.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Three hours of sleep.  Maybe.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**
Doesn’t matter.

She sits up like she’s being summoned to the gallows.  The bedsheets are tangled.  Pages of lyrics are half-crumpled on the floor. She ignores them.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
By 8:30, I need to be a **good model citizen**.

She stands slowly. Stretches once, grimacing.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Professionally dressed.  Hair brushed.  Polished flats.  Minimal eyeliner.  Smile that says *“I’m grateful for the opportunity.”*

She looks at herself in the mirror—mascara from last night smeared under one eye.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Bank downtown.  Part-time job.  Thirty-two hours a week to *pretend to care about deposits and withdrawals.*

(Beat.)

She runs a hand through her hair.  Turns her back on the lyrics.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
No one there knows I almost wrote a masterpiece.  Or a disaster.  Or both.

(She pulls open her closet.)

*FADE OUT on Kathy reaching for the sensible work blouse, still exhausted, still hollow, but already sliding the mask back into place. The teller window awaits. And the lyrics? They stay behind—for now.*

# **CHAPTER ELEVEN: YOU'RE SO FAR AWAY FROM ME**

---

## **INT. DOWNTOWN BANK – DRIVE-THRU WINDOW – 10:47 A.M.**

Kathy sits behind bulletproof glass, headset on, lips moving on autopilot.

**KATHY (flat, memorized tone)**
Hi, welcome to Fairway Bank, how can I help you today?

The tube whooshes in. Envelope. Check. ID.  She doesn’t even blink. Types it all with perfect rhythm.

**KATHY (flat)**
Deposit of $287.62. Do you need any cash back?

The man’s voice crackles over the speaker: *“No thanks, just a receipt.”*

**KATHY**
Coming right up.

Her fingers move. Her face doesn’t.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Flyboy, so lordly… dumbass in my bed.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
But what comes *next?*

(Another transaction begins. She doesn’t even look at the driver.)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
I’ve got lines. I’ve got verses. I’ve got venom.  But it’s *disjointed*. It doesn’t land.

She prints a receipt. Slides it into the pneumatic tube.  Hits “SEND.”

**KATHY (V.O.)**
It's not a song yet.  It’s a **riot in fragments**.

The next customer is already pushing the call button.

**CUSTOMER (INTERCOM)**
Hi there! I’ve got a money order and a check I need to cash—

**KATHY**
Just send it through, sir.

Her tone is polite. Her face is a **mask of boredom**. Inside?

**KATHY (V.O.)**
What if the bridge *mirrors* the intro?  What if the outro is just her saying “get the fuck out” like a whispered loop?

She doesn’t even hear the customer thank her.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
None of it fits.  None of it **sticks**.

She sighs, stares out at the line of cars, the dull grey pavement, the vinyl folder beside her cash drawer.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
God, I hate this job.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
I hate that I’m still stuck on him.  That this song—this *almost*-song—still owns me.

She resets the terminal. The printer hums.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
I’m working the drive-thru like an automaton.  Smiling through bulletproof glass.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
And I **can’t** make this song work.

*FADE OUT on Kathy tapping her fingers on the edge of the counter—trying to match the rhythm of her own frustration, silently begging for something to click. But peace? It’s not coming.*

## **INT. DOWNTOWN BANK – DRIVE-THRU WINDOW – 11:38 A.M.**

Kathy resets the drawer, wiping a smudge from the fingerprint scanner. Her headset is starting to itch behind her ear. She hasn’t smiled in over an hour.

**KATHY (V.O.)**

She hears the chime.  New car. New transaction.

**VOICE (INTERCOM)**
Afternoon, Miss Espich.

**KATHY**
Mr. Stevenson!

The pneumatic tube **whooshes in**.

Inside?

* A deposit envelope.
* A folded grocery receipt.
* And an **ice-cold can of Diet Mountain Dew**.

Kathy grins. She grins like a **real person**, not a customer service automaton.

**KATHY (V.O.)**

Every other day, like clockwork.  Never weird. Never gross. Just… observant.

You too, Kathy. You’re sunshine in a headset. The tube whooshes away.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
And just like that, the whole day feels…three percent more survivable.

She exhales. Smiles. Rolls her eyes at herself.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Who the hell writes a revenge anthem fueled by Diet Mountain Dew?

(Beat.)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Apparently, I do.

*FADE OUT on Kathy sipping quietly, her foot tapping again, but this time it’s not frustration—it’s rhythm. Because something in her just reset. Joe didn’t give her inspiration. He gave her **grace**. And maybe that’s the missing beat.*

## **INT. BANK WOMEN’S ROOM – 12:31 P.M. – LUNCH BREAK RESET**

The fluorescent lights buzz faintly.  The tile is too white. Too sterile. Kathy stands in front of the mirror, her hands gripping the edge of the sink. She stares at her reflection—messy ponytail, mascara smudge, the faint line of sweat at her collar.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
This didn't give off a good vibe.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Sharp in the head.  Sharp in the page.  Gotta look sharp too. She exhales. Rolls her shoulders once. And gets to work. **Fast. Precise. Quiet.** She pulls a comb from her purse. Tightens the ponytail.  Pats down the flyaways with a splash of cold water.  She touches up her eyeliner with the tiniest flick.  Wipes her neck with a paper towel. Dabs perfume from the sample vial she’s kept hidden in her wallet. Switches out the earrings.  Straightens her blouse.  Adjusts her posture. She steps back. Looks at herself again.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Better. Not perfect. Not glamorous. But **collected**.

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**
If I’m going to fight to feel like a woman—I should at least look like I meant it.

She gives her reflection a single nod.

*FADE OUT as she leaves the women’s room not in a hurry, not in a slump—but upright, present, and yes—**sharp.***

## **INT. BANK WOMEN’S ROOM – 12:33 P.M. – BUTTONED STRATEGY**

Button up.  Best foot forward.  Reduce the cleavage—reduce the commentary.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Maybe.

## **INT. BANK HALLWAY – 12:36 P.M. – THE MADONNA DAYDREAM**

Kathy walks back to her station, heels muted on the industrial carpet.  Her blouse is buttoned. Her hair is neat. Her badge reads “K. Espich.”  She passes a coworker—older man, same smile as always.  He doesn't say a word, but his eyes linger. Kathy doesn’t flinch. She keeps walking. But her thoughts flare.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Men don’t button up for safety.  They don’t filter their identity for comfort. They just *show up*.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**

(She smiles.)

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Just like **Madonna.***The* Madonna.  The black-and-white Playboy spread from a few years ago.  Unapologetic. Full bush. Full woman. **Full power.*

Just to say: **this is mine.**  And if that makes you uncomfortable?  **Good.**

*FADE OUT on Kathy shifting in her chair, the headset crackling back to life, her thoughts still lingering somewhere between the teller drawer and a studio spotlight. Because under the business casual? Kathy Espich is still a fucking icon in waiting.*

## **INT. DOWNTOWN BANK – DRIVE-THRU WINDOW – 1:02 P.M.**

## **INT. BANK INTERIOR – 2:11 P.M. – SUPERVISOR’S OFFICE**

Kathy walks up the hallway, tension in every step. She adjusts her blouse collar. Checks her badge. Breathes once. Her boss—**Tammy, mid-40s, blunt bob, eternal beige cardigan**—is standing in the doorway, **grinning like she just won something on the radio.**

**TAMMY**
Kathy! Step in here, hon. Got a moment?

Kathy enters. Guarded. Polite. Braced for hell.

**KATHY**
Yes, ma’am?

Tammy gestures for her to sit.  Kathy doesn’t.

**TAMMY**
You’re gonna love this.  Our secret shopper came through the drive-thru today.

Kathy blinks. Mind racing.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Oh god. Which customer? Was I rude? Did I swear out loud?

**TAMMY (CONT’D)**
And guess what?

(Leans forward.)

**TAMMY (CONT’D)**
She gave you a **perfect score.**

Kathy stares.

Wait…what?

**TAMMY**
Said she was helped by one **Miss Cassie Espich**—I assume that’s a typo on her form, but she said you were “courteous, efficient, and displayed professionalism beyond expectation.”

Kathy blinks twice.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
While mentally assembling a manifesto.

Tammy pulls a little envelope out of her drawer and hands it over with a flourish.

**TAMMY**
So we’re giving you an on-the-spot award.

**KATHY**
Oh?

**TAMMY**
One paid hour off. Starting now if you want it. You can clock out and go home, Kathy. You earned it.

(Beat.)

**TAMMY (CONT’D)**
On the clock.

Kathy stares at her. Then smiles.

**KATHY**
Yes, ma’am. I think I will.

**TAMMY**
We love having you here. You’re a great presence.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
You have **no idea**.

*FADE OUT on Kathy walking to the break room with a lightness she hasn’t felt all day. Lyrics can wait. Practice is coming. And she’s walking out the front door like a queen with sixty free minutes and vengeance on her breath.*

## **INT. KATHY’S BATHROOM – 3:12 P.M. – THE RESET**

The bathroom is filled with steam, the mirror fogged over. The tub overflows with bubbles, the water just shy of scalding. Kathy sinks deeper, the heat enveloping her. She closes her eyes, letting the warmth seep into her bones.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
This is more than a bath. This is a baptism.

She reaches for her razor, methodically shaving her legs. Each stroke is deliberate, a ritual of renewal.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Not for them. For me.

She stands, water cascading down her body, and wraps herself in a towel. She catches her reflection in the mirror, a smile playing on her lips.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Horny? Sure. But this energy isn't for a quick fix. It's for creation.

She strides into her room, drops the towel, and sits at her desk. A blank sheet of paper awaits. She picks up her pen, the ink flowing as effortlessly as the ideas in her mind.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Time to write. Time to channel this fire into words.

*FADE OUT as Kathy begins to write, the room silent except for the scratch of her pen and the distant hum of possibility.*

## **INT. KATHY'S BEDROOM – LATE AFTERNOON**

The room is quiet, save for the soft rustle of paper and the occasional creak of the floorboards. Kathy's pen dances across the page, each word a deliberate stroke of defiance and self-realization.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
I'm not just a teller, a daughter, a bandmate. I'm all of them and none. I'm the sum of my choices, my desires, my regrets. She writes:

**(Verse 1)**
*In the heat of the night, we’re tangled and tried,*
*Passion burning like a fire, can’t let it slide.*
*Licking up his shaft, oh, I’m right on track,*
*Need it in my mouth, no way I'm turning back.*

**(Pre-Chorus)**
*His voice like honey, yet sharp like a knife,*
*I felt so sexy, lost in this life.*
*"O please baby, let me finish you off,"*
*He pulls my head up, clearly growing soft*

**(Chorus)**
*Post-nut clarity, "you don't like my head?",*
*Flyboy so lordly, dumbass in my bed.*
*Moment of delight, after we finished,*
*Now it feels like my gift was diminished.*

**(Verse 2)**
*Late nights in the kitchen, humping on the floor,*
*Whispers and secrets, we both wanted more.*
*But the moments turned sour, the passion ran dry,*
*Got me questioning us, asking myself "why?"*

**(Pre-Chorus)**
*His cock was electric, now it feels like a chore,*
*"Can you do better next time?" echoes my core.*
*Each kiss, a reminder of what we’ve been through,*
*But I’m feeling like a stranger, not quite sure what to do.*

**(Chorus)**
*Post-nut clarity, "you don't like my head?",*
*Flyboy so lordly, dumbass in my bed.*
*Moment of delight, after we finished,*
*Now it feels like my gift was diminished.*

**(Bridge)**
*I remember that summer, the spark in the air,*
*Caught up in passion, no worries, no care.*
*Now it’s just silence, a chasm so wide,*
*Can we find that rhythm, or do I just hide?*

**(Chorus)**
*Post-nut clarity, "you don't like my head?",*
*Flyboy so lordly, dumbass in my bed.*
*Moment of delight, after we finished,*
*Now it feels like my gift was diminished.*

**(Outro)**
*So here I am panting, cum just swallowed,*
*Boggled so deeply, bitter words followed.*
*But if I don't thrill you, where's the fun in this fuck?*
*You self-absorbed shit, I leave guys dumbstruck.*

---

**KATHY (V.O.)**
This isn't just a song. It's a reckoning. A declaration. A mirror held up to the faces that tried to define me.

She sets down her pen, the page now filled with her truth. The sun dips below the horizon, casting a golden hue over her words.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Tonight, I bring this to the band. Not for approval, but for acknowledgment. This is me. Unfiltered. Unapologetic.

## **INT. KATHY'S BEDROOM – LATE AFTERNOON**

Kathy sits on her bed, her guitar resting on her lap. She strums a few chords, experimenting with different techniques to find the perfect snarling tone.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
I need this guitar to speak the same truth as my lyrics. No more playing it safe.

She recalls techniques that can add grit to her sound:

* **Pick Attack**: She adjusts her picking hand, striking the strings with more force to produce a sharper, more aggressive tone.
* **Palm Muting**: She experiments with palm muting, adding a percussive element that tightens up her sound.
* **EQ Adjustments**: She tweaks her amp settings, boosting the midrange frequencies to add growl and presence to her tone.

---

## **INT. KATHY'S BEDROOM – LATE AFTERNOON**

Kathy sits on her bed, the rotary phone cradled between her shoulder and ear. She listens to the ringing, tapping her fingers anxiously on her knee.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Come on, Jeremy. Pick up.

After a few rings, a click.

**JEREMY (O.S.)**
Hello?

**KATHY**
Hey, Jeremy. It's Kathy. I have something I want to run by you before practice tonight. Think we could meet up a bit early?

**JEREMY (O.S.)**
Sure, what's up?

**KATHY**
I've been working on a new song. It's… intense. I want to make sure the guitar parts match the energy of the lyrics. I could use your input.

**JEREMY (O.S.)**
Sounds intriguing. Meet me at the garage an hour before practice?

**KATHY**
Perfect. Thanks, Jeremy.

She hangs up, a mix of nerves and excitement bubbling within her.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
This is going to be a game-changer.

## **INT. GILLEY GARAGE – 5:01 P.M. – EARLY SUMMER HEAT, THE CONFRONTATION**

The garage is half-lit, half-organized. Empty McDonald’s cup in the corner.  Amp buzz faintly audible. Practice is still 30 minutes away. Kathy arrives, guitar case in hand, sweat on her brow, hair tied up like she means business. Jeremy is already there, sitting backward on a folding chair, arms draped over the top, pick tucked behind his ear. Grinning like the bastard little brother he is.

**JEREMY**
All right, Kathy.  Disgust me.

(Grin.)

**JEREMY (CONT’D)**
Let’s hear it.  You said you’ve got something that’s gonna blow my brother’s ass out of the water.

(He leans forward, eyes glittering.)

**JEREMY (CONT’D)**
I don’t think you can do it.

(Beat.)

**JEREMY (CONT’D)**
Not because you’re a girl.

**KATHY** (quiet, dangerous)
Good save.

**JEREMY**
Because you’re not Jeff.

(Silence.)

Kathy doesn’t flinch. She sets the guitar case down. Unsnaps it. Slowly.

**KATHY**
You think I care?

**JEREMY**
I think you *burned* for it.

**KATHY**
Maybe.

(She pulls the guitar out. Plugs in. No sound yet. Just motion.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
You want a show, Jeremy?

**JEREMY**
I want to be convinced.

(Beat.)

**KATHY**
Then shut the fuck up.

(She strums one chord. It snarls.)

*FADE OUT on the amp finally spitting to life, Jeremy leaning forward, and Kathy with one foot planted like she’s about to declare war. This isn’t just song two. This is a challenge.*

## **INT. GILLEY GARAGE – 5:04 P.M. – THE GAUNTLET**

Jeremy raises an eyebrow. Leans further forward.

**JEREMY**

(Shrugs.)

**JEREMY (CONT’D)**
Let me see your inner Shakespeare.

(Kathy is still tuning—cool, quiet, indifferent.)

**JEREMY (CONT’D)**
Come on. Pull your panties down and let me see your Shakespeare there.

That gets her attention. Her head cocks.  She doesn’t blink. She smiles.

**KATHY**
You want my inner Shakespeare?

(She flips to the first page of her lyrics, all clean lines, all blood.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
You really want to see what a bitch with a pen and too much bubble bath is capable of?

**JEREMY**
Oh, I'm **begging**.

She dead-eyes him.

**KATHY**
Then shut up and listen.  And try not to cry when your dick shrinks from secondhand embarrassment.

(Beat.)

She starts playing. A single riff.  Snarling. Low.  Not elegant—**mean.**

Then—her voice:

**KATHY (singing, dry, venomous):**
*Post-nut clarity—“you don’t like my head?”*
*Flyboy, so lordly. Dumbass in my bed…*

Jeremy’s face changes.

*FADE OUT on him sitting bolt upright, mouth just slightly parted, while Kathy rides the rhythm like a whipcrack. She didn’t pull her panties down. She pulled a **scalpel**—and Jeremy just realized he might be the one bleeding.*

## **INT. GILLEY GARAGE – 5:09 P.M. – RECONSTRUCTION MODE**

The last word of Kathy’s chorus echoes against the drywall. Jeremy exhales like he’s been hit in the stomach.

**JEREMY**
Fuck, Kathy.

(Beat.)

**JEREMY (CONT’D)**
I mean, **fuck**.

He’s pacing now, restless, holding his guitar like it’s too light.

**JEREMY (CONT’D)**
That was awesome.  My **God**, that was awesome.

(He stops, spins toward her.)

**JEREMY (CONT’D)**
But you’re playing the guitar part all wrong.

Kathy raises an eyebrow. Not defensive; **curious**.

**KATHY**
Wrong?

**JEREMY**
Yeah, you’ve got it **reversed**.

You’re **hitting it too hard at the top**.  What it needs is **tension**.

(Slaps his palm with his fist.)

**JEREMY (CONT’D)**
Start **fragile.**  You tiptoe in. One note at a time.

He mimes it on his strings—low, deliberate single-note phrases.

**JEREMY (CONT’D)**
The rhythm guitar tiptoes, **like the first moment of heat**, the spark. Like you’re about to fuck him but you’re still deciding whether you should slit his throat or not.

**KATHY** (quietly)
That’s not a bad read.

**JEREMY**

**KATHY**
And Jeff?

**JEREMY** (eyes wild)
We **ask** Jeff to move the room.  **Shake the foundation** with the bass.  Make it quake. Like it’s **ripping through the walls.**

(Beat.)

**JEREMY (CONT’D)**
God, this is gonna work. He’s practically vibrating with excitement. Kathy just watches him—half-exhausted, half-stunned, but starting to smile.

**KATHY**
You’re sweating.

**JEREMY**
Hella yeah! I’m **alive**.

(Beat.)

**JEREMY (CONT’D)**
Let’s make this song **fuck the world up.**

*FADE OUT on Jeremy plugging in, Kathy stepping into his rhythm, both of them now **co-conspirators**, stitching the structure that’s going to turn “Post-Nut Clarity” from a journal entry into a **supernova**.*
