## **INT. GILLEY GARAGE – 5:16 P.M. – THE EDGE OF NAKED**

The amp’s humming, low gain.  Kathy’s got her guitar back in hand. She adjusts the strap.  She adjusts it again. Jeremy’s crouched across from her, building a rough loop pedal for when they hit the chorus.

**JEREMY**
Start from the top.  Just give me the tiptoe part. One note at a time.

Kathy hesitates.  Strums a single string. It rings. Feels too bare.  She adds another—interval. Minor. Dissonant. She likes that.

She tries again. Slower.  The tone **whispers** instead of growls.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
God, this is uncomfortable.

Her fingers feel clumsy, like they’re revealing something she’s not ready to say out loud.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
I’m not used to being this… **exposed**.

She misses a note. Winces.  Jeremy says nothing. Just keeps listening. Tweaking knobs.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
He asked to see my inner Shakespeare.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Maybe I forgive him for that.

(She hits a slide into a minor third. It **sings.**)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Sometimes they don’t treat me the way a woman ought to be treated.

She bites her lip. Slides to the next note.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
But then again…

(She stops. Just for a moment.)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Maybe they don’t see me as a woman at all.

That thought makes her skin crawl. She resumes playing. Harder. Sharper. The notes still tiptoe—but there’s **teeth** behind them now. Jeremy looks up, hears the shift. Nods slowly. He gets it.

**JEREMY**
There it is.

(Beat.)

**JEREMY (CONT’D)**
That’s you. Right there. That’s your butt showing.

She doesn't reply. Just plays it again—**cleaner this time**.

*FADE OUT on Kathy circling the same riff, each pass growing more controlled, more lethal. She's not just building the intro. She's exorcising it. Because being seen the wrong way hurts—but being unseen at all?*

**Unforgivable.**

---

## **INT. GILLEY GARAGE – 5:24 P.M. – THE ARRIVAL**

The riff loops.  Low. Controlled. Wound like wire.  Jeremy has built a feedback bed, just enough delay to make it shimmer. Kathy plays it again.  This time with intent.  Then—**a voice from the shadows, offscreen**:

**JEFF (O.S.)**
I could hear that from the street.

Kathy’s fingers freeze mid-phrase. Jeremy turns around, startled.

**JEREMY**
Jesus, Jeff. Say something next time before you haunt a doorway.

Jeff steps in from the edge of the garage, backlit by the afternoon sun. He’s got his backpack slung low, bass in hand. No amp. No case.  Just him. He walks in slowly. Eyes on Kathy.

**JEFF**
You’ve been busy.

**KATHY**
Guess I have.

(Beat.)

**JEFF**
That intro’s a scalpel.  You’ve got it **wounded and whispering**.

**KATHY**
Thanks.

**JEFF** (beat)
What’s it for?

Jeremy glances at her. She meets Jeff’s eyes directly.

**KATHY**
It’s called “*Post-Nut Clarity*.”

(Silence.)

Jeff exhales through his nose.  Sets his bass down slowly.

**JEFF**
Okay.

(Beat.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
I’m in.

*FADE OUT on the three of them standing in a triangle—two guitars, one bass, and the pulse of something **massive** coming together in the sweltering heat of a cluttered garage. They don’t even need to speak now. The sound is already saying everything.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY GARAGE – 5:26 P.M. – THE PAGE**

The amp hums in the background.  Kathy’s still holding her guitar.  Jeff’s still standing—his tone unreadable, but his eyes locked.

**JEFF**
I want to hear it all.

(Beat.)

**KATHY**
You sure?

**JEFF**
I’m not here to blink.  You said you wanted to shake the room.  So shake *me*.

She walks to her bag. Pulls out a folded sheet of looseleaf.  Ten pages. Clean draft on top. She hesitates for half a second. Then hands it to him.

**KATHY**
This isn’t a test.  But you better not flinch.

Jeff sits on an amp, unfolding the pages slowly. The garage is silent except for the shifting weight of expectation. He starts reading. First verse—no reaction.  Second verse—his eyebrows raise.  Chorus—he exhales, slow and quiet. By the bridge, he leans forward, elbows on knees, like the lyrics are a letter meant for him personally.

**JEFF** (quietly)
*Jesus*.

He finishes the outro.

Reads it again.

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
You wrote this?

**KATHY**
Every word.

**JEFF**
You *felt* this?

**KATHY**
I *lived* it.

(Beat.)

Jeff folds the pages once. Hands them back.

**JEFF**
Then we’re going to burn the house down.

(He looks to Jeremy.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
We start on the one. Kathy rides in after two bars.  We go from whisper to wildfire.  Let’s build it. Right the fuck now.

*FADE OUT as Kathy steps back toward her amp, Jeremy plugs in beside her, and Jeff plants his feet like a goddamn earthquake waiting to happen. The lyrics are out. The gloves are off. The room is about to ignite.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY GARAGE – 5:34 P.M. – GILLEY ENTERS**

The garage is buzzing—amps on, chords hanging in the air, the scent of sonic violence mid-brew.  The garage door creaks open.

**GILLEY**
Jesus Christ.

(He steps inside, blinking in the heat.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
This sounds like a pack of hornets and a chainsaw had a baby.

Jeff nods, deadpan.

**JEFF**
That’s the idea.

**JEREMY**
She wrote it.

(He jerks a thumb toward Kathy, who stands beside her amp like a storm in denim.)

Gilley looks at her.  Serious. Focused.

**GILLEY**
You got lyrics?

**KATHY**
Yeah.

**GILLEY**
I don’t wanna hear the song.

(Beat.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
Not yet.

Everyone quiets.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
I want to hear from you. Read it. Out loud. No guitar. No tempo. No tone.

(He leans against the wall, arms crossed.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
Just the words.

(Beat.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
I got some thoughts.

Kathy stares at him. Doesn’t blink. The rest of the band goes still. Jeff lowers his bass. Jeremy sits down. Kathy picks up the pages again.  No drama. No performance.  Just her voice. Dry. Controlled. **Nuclear.** She starts reading.

**KATHY** (quietly, but firm)
*In the heat of the night, we’re tangled and tried…*
*Passion burning like a fire, can’t let it slide*.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
*Licking up his shaft, oh, I’m right on track…*
*Need it in my mouth, no way I'm turning back*.

Silence. Not even the amps buzz. Kathy keeps going. Every syllable lands like a stone skipping on dark water. No apologies.  No flourishes.  Just the truth.

Gilley doesn’t interrupt.  He listens—**like it’s scripture, or a crime scene.**

*FADE OUT as she reaches the chorus, eyes on him, watching his reaction like it’s the final goddamn verdict. Because Kathy doesn’t want praise. She wants the truth—and Gilley always gives it.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY GARAGE – 5:39 P.M. – AFTER THE READ**

Kathy finishes the last line. Silence. Gilley hasn’t said a word yet. Before he can? Jeremy cuts in. He’s leaned back in a folding chair, pick in his mouth, one hand drumming on his thigh.

**GILLEY**
Where’s the **foreplay**?

Kathy squints at him.

**KATHY**
What?

**GILLEY**
That first beat—when we come in?  That riff?  You guys are **attacking** it.

(He leans forward, more serious now.)

**JEREMY (CONT’D)**
That’s wrong?

**KATHY**
Oh, is it?

**GILLEY**
Yeah. You don’t attack a clit like that.

(Beat.)

**JEFF**
Jesus Christ.

**GILLEY**
No, I’m serious.

**KATHY**
Oh, *I know* you’re serious.

**GILLEY**
You have to **persuade** a clit.  You **warm it up**. You **tease** it. You **seduce** it.

He waves his hand in a slow figure eight.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
You don’t just kick the door in and start pounding like it owes you rent.

(Beat.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
These two people you’re writing about—They’re **lovers**, right?

Kathy doesn’t answer. That *is* the question, isn’t it?

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
It’s not an anonymous fuck.  They **know** each other.  And they’re **insulting** each other.  They’re **condescending**, right?

**KATHY**
Yes.

(Quiet.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
They’re lovers.

**GILLEY**
Then there’s **foreplay**.

(Beat.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
You don’t open this song with a chainsaw.  You open it like a hand sliding up the inside of a thigh.

(Silence.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
If we’re gonna build to violence—Let’s earn it.

*FADE OUT on Kathy staring at the lyric sheet, her fingers tight around the page, because **goddammit**, he’s right. Again. Not because she’s weak, but because she just got challenged on a level she didn’t expect. And this song’s about to get even more dangerous.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY GARAGE – 5:43 P.M. – DETONATION BY GILLEY**

Gilley is still riding high off his riff monologue, bouncing on his heels, hands twitching over the strings. Kathy is silent, deep in thought. Then—

**GILLEY**
I’ve got another issue.

(Silence.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
With how the **esteemed Mr. Jeremy Evans** has got the guitars going.

Jeremy looks over, already annoyed.

**JEREMY**
What now?

**GILLEY**
It’s too goddamn fast.

**JEREMY**
It *has* to hit hard.

**GILLEY**
It doesn’t need to hit **fast**.  It needs to hit **wrong**.  Unexpected.

(He turns to Kathy. Calm. Razor-edged.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
Kathy’s gonna get this.

Jeremy rolls his eyes.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
Because she’s **sucked dick before**.

Kathy blinks. Doesn’t react.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
No, no—*don’t answer.*  I’m right.

**JEREMY**
Jesus, Gilley.

**GILLEY**
BJ’s are rapid. Sloppy. Hurried.  You just wanna get the guy off, right?

(He gestures to the air—like shaping smoke.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
This *isn’t* that.

(Beat.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
This song?  This song isn’t trying to **get him off**.  It’s trying to **make him pay**.

(Beat.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
So why the hell are the guitars sprinting?

Silence.

Kathy squints.  Because that—that’s the cut. That’s the moment. She starts nodding.

**KATHY**
Yeah.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
We don’t rush this.  We savor it.  We make it **hurt slow.**

*FADE OUT on the band adjusting dials, Jeremy stepping back, Kathy leaning into her amp with a predatory calm. Because Gilley’s crudeness isn’t the point. The **tempo is the point.** And now? The song is about to become a weapon.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY GARAGE – 5:45 P.M. – THE INTERNAL ADMISSION**

The band is still adjusting. Jeremy’s muttering under his breath. Jeff is watching Kathy, waiting. Gilley’s tuning his guitar with one hand and unscrewing a Gatorade cap with the other. Kathy stands quietly, holding her guitar by the neck. She's not playing yet.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
I underestimated him.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
That was probably the **least horny thing Gilley’s ever said** in the **horniest tone** possible.

She glances over. He’s completely unbothered, like he didn’t just reframe the entire direction of the track.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
He’s crude.  He’s rude.

(She smiles.)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
He’s a **genius**, isn’t he?

Not book-smart. Not a lyricist.  But when someone else **writes**? Gilley can see inside it.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
He doesn’t need to read.  He **feels** tone.  He can take a thought…A fragment… And sculpt it like fucking Michelangelo.

(She exhales.)

**KATHY (V.O.)**
He shaped my song in thirty seconds.  And did it with a blowjob metaphor.

She shakes her head.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
God help me.  We might actually be a **real band**.

*FADE OUT as Kathy walks back to her mic, now adjusted emotionally, musically, **spiritually**. The tempo’s about to drop. The guitars are about to breathe. And Kathy Espich—thanks to a rude bastard sculptor in cargo shorts—is ready to sing like the world’s ending.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY GARAGE – 6:01 P.M. – POST-REVELATION, PRE-REHEARSAL**

The instruments are plugged in.  The tension is coiled.  The whole room smells like something’s about to combust. Bill adjusts a knob on the mixing board—calm, clinical.

**BILL**
This really sounds, uh…something like, uh, Nirvana.

(He pauses. Thinks.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
The way you guys are layering this up—that tight low-end tension with the spiraling top fuzz?

**JEFF**
No, we’re not.

(He waves his hand, dismissing the entire Pacific Northwest.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
This is *primitive American grunge*. Or… *Americana primitive grunge*.  Or whatever the fuck we’re inventing.

(Beat.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
Fuck, maybe I should write this shit down.

Bill doesn’t even look up.

**BILL**
It would probably help.

(Deadpan.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
Maybe flashcards, sir?

Kathy snorts.  Jeremy lets out a short bark of a laugh.  Gilley’s already opening a fresh string pack like he’s assembling an M-16. Jeff doesn’t react. He just starts pacing again, eyes scanning the ceiling like genre names are hanging from it like bats.

*FADE OUT on the band snapping into their rhythm again, the tension easing slightly with the humor, but the **mission** still dead serious. They aren’t copying anything. They’re birthing something. And Bill, sharp as ever, is there to make sure they don’t forget what the hell they’re calling it.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY GARAGE – 6:08 P.M. – COMPETITIVE DETENTE**

The room’s still warm with feedback residue. Kathy’s riff is still crawling up the walls, haunting the rafters. Jeff has his bass cradled, but he hasn’t touched it in minutes. He clears his throat.

**JEFF**
I got something else to show off.

Kathy eyes him—one eyebrow arched.

**KATHY**
Are you trying to overshadow me there, professor?

(Beat.)

Jeff gives a tiny, crooked smile. Not defensive—*real*.

**JEFF**
No. I’m just operating on the assumption that the next thing *you* do is gonna be **equally as awesome**,  so I’m trying to get ahead in the game.

Kathy tilts her head, intrigued but wary.

**KATHY**
You're admitting to preemptive jealousy?

**JEFF**
I’m admitting to **calculated self-preservation**.

(He shrugs.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
But I *do* have something cool.  Legit cool.

**KATHY**
Cool how?

**JEFF**
Cool like—could be a b-side, could be a bridge, could be a six-minute war crime.

(Beat.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
But if you don’t want to hear it…That’s okay.

He means it. For real. Kathy eyes him. For a moment, she considers teasing him.
But the garage is sacred right now. She nods once.

**KATHY**
Show me.

Jeff steps forward.

**JEFF**
Okay.  Just remember— You started the fire.

(Beat.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
I’m just bringing kindling.

*FADE OUT on Jeff adjusting his amp, the others shifting to listen. The arms race of greatness in this garage isn’t hostile. It’s nuclear-powered **respect**. And now we’re about to see what happens when Jeff steps into the heat with his own flame.*

---

# **CHAPTER TWELVE: YEAH, THE BOY CAN PLAY**

---

## **INT. GILLEY GARAGE – 6:18 P.M. – JEFF'S DECLARATION**

Jeff sits cross-legged on the cracked concrete floor, bass in hand.  Sweat beading under his collar.  He’s not playing for applause. He’s **carving a signature**.

The line he’s working on isn’t fast. It’s not showy.  But it **moves**—like freight down the Ohio River. It’s a **fusion**—intentional and unapologetic:

* **Bootsy Collins**: That slinky funk from *just over the border*, basslines that *grin* while they throb.
* **John Curley**: The Afghan Whigs’ heavy melancholic undertow—smoky, slow, like bourbon sweat.
* **Jeff Evans**: The *third element*. Not a copy. Not a homage. **A declaration.**

This sound isn’t *Seattle*.  It’s not *New York*.  It’s not *LA*. **It’s Cincinnati.**  Midwestern. Appalachian. Southern.  Coal dust in its lungs. River water in its blood.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
Jeremy’s up there slashing lightning.  I’m holding the soil together underneath him.

**JEFF (V.O.) (CONT’D)**
If he’s the blaze,  I’m the crackle *underneath the floorboards*.

(He plucks. Slides. Anchors.)

**JEFF (V.O.)**
Every band’s got a sound.  I want **mine**.

(Beat.)

**JEFF (V.O.)**
You’re gonna hear this bassline…and **know it’s me.**

He rewinds the loop. Records again. Replays. Not one member of the band is speaking.  They’re listening. Because Jeff Evans isn’t backing up a song. He’s designing a flag.

*FADE OUT* on the line looping—low, thick, and unmistakable.  This isn’t a riff. It’s **a fingerprint.**  And from this moment forward, anyone who plays it knows—*they owe it to Jeff Evans.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY GARAGE – 6:21 P.M. – BROTHERLY BLADES**

Jeff finishes another loop pass. The line’s cleaner now—**lean**, but with **mass**. The floor seems to vibrate differently under it. Jeremy, leaning against a stack of milk crates, lets out a low whistle.

**JEREMY**
With a bassline like that, maybe you oughta play **lead guitar**.

(Grin.)

Jeff doesn’t even glance at him.

**JEFF**
Nah.

(Beat.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
Bass is simpler.

**JEREMY**
Bullshit.

**JEFF**
It is.

(He adjusts his strap, almost offhand.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
I’m not nearly as **dexterous** as you.  Never have been.

Jeremy’s grin softens for a second.

**JEREMY**
You don’t need to be.  You make the floorboards creak, man.

**JEFF**
Good.

**JEREMY**
That’s not a compliment.

**JEFF**
Yes, it is.

(Silence.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
I don’t want flash.  I want **presence**.  When I hit a note, I want the room to remember how it fucked them up.

Jeremy kicks the amp lightly with the side of his foot.

**JEREMY**
Then you’re already halfway there, professor.

*FADE OUT on the Evans brothers not hugging, not fist-bumping, not making a moment of it—but standing in the same room, **playing to each other’s strengths**, even if they won’t admit it.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY GARAGE – 6:23 P.M. – THE SOUND GUY SPEAKS**

The last loop fades into silence.  Jeremy’s still chewing on the tail of the riff.  Kathy’s scribbling notes on a gum wrapper.  Gilley’s counting beats on his fingers. Bill, seated at the side with a tangled mess of cables, lifts his head.

**BILL**
You know…

(Beat.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
We might be able to work with that.

(He nods once—small, approving.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
But that sound? That *line*?

(Shrugs.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
That’s just starkly…**odd.**

Everyone looks at him. Jeff raises an eyebrow.

**BILL (CONT’D)**
It’s *cool*—don’t get me wrong. It’s dark, it’s greasy, it’s completely magnetic.

(He leans forward.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
But you can’t use that all the time.

(Silence.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
It’s like—It’s like putting cinnamon on steak.  You do it once, people lose their minds.

(Beat.)

**BILL (CONT’D)**
Do it every night?  They stop coming to the restaurant.

Jeff grins. Doesn’t disagree.

**JEFF**
So—what, reserve it?

**BILL**
Yeah.  Use it like a **hand grenade**.  Not like a paintbrush.

**KATHY**
That’s actually brilliant.

**GILLEY**
Wow, Bill.  That's almost *poetic*.

**BILL**
Don’t get used to it.

*FADE OUT* on Jeff nodding slowly, looping the bassline one more time—not to play it again, but to **save it**. Because now everyone knows: this isn’t just a riff. It’s **the trump card. And trump cards don’t get played twice.**

---

## **INT. GILLEY GARAGE – 6:26 P.M. – PHILOSOPHY AND RIFFS**

Jeff’s still cradling the final echo of his Cincinnati bassline like it might evaporate. Bill finished his speech. Jeremy’s pulling apart his pick to avoid admitting that he agreed with Bill. And Kathy? She leans against the wall, arms folded, eyes locked on Jeff.

**KATHY**
You ought not be afraid to assert yourself.

Jeff glances up.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
I mean it.  You don’t have to just hang in the back and *support*.

(She uncrosses her arms, takes a step forward.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
If we’re going to be this **challenging**—if we’re going to burn the rulebook **lyrically**—

(She points at her lyric sheet on the floor.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Then we might as well throw down **sonically**.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Why the hell *shouldn’t* the bass take lead sometimes?

The room stills.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
That’d be *true* subversion.

Jeremy chuckles—half mocking, half impressed.

**JEREMY**
You want to make the low end the front man?

**KATHY**
I want to make the low end the **knife**.

(She turns to Jeff.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
You’ve got something none of us can replicate.

(Softer now.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
So use it.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Don’t ask permission.

*FADE OUT* on Jeff blinking slowly, processing her words—not flattered, but **validated.** The ground underneath Commuted just shifted again, and this time, it was the **bassline taking a step forward.***

---

## **INT. GILLEY GARAGE – 6:31 P.M. – THE DRUMMER ENTERS**

The air is *dense* with static and sweat.  Kathy’s still standing mid-monologue, Jeff is staring at the floor like it owes him royalty checks, Jeremy is halfway to a grin, and Bill is rewiring something that didn’t need rewiring just to burn time.

The side door creaks open.

**JIM**
Hey guys.

(No response.)

**JIM (CONT’D)**
What’d I miss?

All heads turn.

**JEREMY**
Oh, not much.

**KATHY**
Jeff just revolutionized our entire **bass philosophy**.

**GILLEY**
Kathy declared the **end of the musical hierarchy**.

**BILL**
We agreed not to use brilliance more than once per set.

**JEFF**
And I accidentally summoned the ghost of John Curley through my amplifier.

Jim stares at them.

**JIM**
…So nothing unusual?

(Beat.)

**KATHY**
We’re serious.

**JIM**
Oh God.  You guys went **full art school** again, didn’t you?

He drops his stick bag with a *thud.*

**JIM (CONT’D)**
Fine.  Someone point to the tempo map before I get blamed for being late **and** out of sync.

*FADE OUT* on Jim rolling his shoulders, already calculating how to make his snare flirt with Jeff’s bassline, and trying not to look too impressed by what’s already brewing in the room. He may have missed the revolution’s opening shot—but he’s sure as hell ready to **keep time for it.**

---

## **INT. GILLEY GARAGE – 6:34 P.M. – THE STANDARD SET**

Jim’s behind the kit now, settling into the throne, flipping his sticks like it’s a normal day.
Jeff steps forward, bass still in hand, cable half-draped over his shoulder. His voice is calm, but pointed.

**JEFF**
Jim.

Jim looks up.  Jeff doesn’t blink.

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
You need to be absolutely on point.

(Beat.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
From beginning to end.  No drift. No drift in practice. No drift on stage.

Jim straightens, a little wary.

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
You're the band’s **metronome**.

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
Without you holding **perfect time**,  from the first note to the last?  We fall flat. We fall *hard*.

The rest of the band is dead silent. No one interrupts. Jeff lets it sit for a beat. Then:

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
There’s one reason we’re going to be excellent.

(Beat.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
**And it’s going to be because of you.**

The room goes quiet again. Kathy watches him. Jeremy tilts his head. Jim?  He doesn’t nod. Doesn’t frown. Doesn’t posture. He twirls one stick in his right hand.

And just says:

**JIM**
Okay.

*FADE OUT on the tension snapping into clarity. The room isn’t just warmed up now. It’s aligned. Because with Jeff’s declaration, Jim’s restraint, and the band’s trust—Commuted isn’t just a group. It’s a weapon. And they’re about to fire.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY GARAGE – 6:37 P.M. – THE CROSSCHECK**

Jeff’s statement still hangs in the air. Jim is silent, still sitting steady behind the kit. Jeremy tilts his head, arms crossed.

**JEREMY**
Uh…You being a little bit, uh, **extreme**, there, Jeff?

Jeff doesn’t turn. Doesn’t shift.

**JEFF**
No.

(Beat.)

Kathy speaks up next, more cautious.

**KATHY**
You’re putting a lot of weight on him.  You’re turning him into a… a human drum machine.

Jeff looks at her now. Not cold. Just certain.

**JEFF**
No.  I’m not.

(Beat.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
I’m saying **we** can all wobble.  We can experiment, bend time, tease tempo.  We can *play*.

(He gestures around the room.)

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
But only if we have a **constant**.

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
Jim isn’t a machine.  He’s the reason **we don’t need one**.

Jeremy quiets. Kathy watches Jeff, narrowing her eyes.

Jeff turns to Jim.

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
We fly because he holds the fort.  We stretch because you **anchor**.

Jim doesn’t move. Then—after a beat—he flips his sticks into match grip and starts tapping out a low, surgical four-count on the hi-hat.

**JIM**
Huh? Then shut up and count me in.

*FADE OUT as the band lines up, each member glancing at the others, all waiting for that one downbeat. Because the rhythm is set. The band is aligned. And Jim? Jim’s already counting.*

---

## **INT. GILLEY GARAGE – 6:41 P.M. – MID-PRACTICE, MID-GLANCE**

The band’s in motion.

Kathy’s mic levels are hot. Bill’s pulling the tape deck. Jim is a metronomic ghost in motion. Jeff’s fingers move with surgical calm, laying down the Cincinnati signature with that quiet-rooted fury. Jeremy’s playing. But also? **Watching.** He keeps glancing to his right—toward Jeff. Jeff, who just minutes ago said that **Jim was the reason for their excellence**, and did it without sarcasm, without a raised voice, without any of that usual Jeff-edge.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**
Was that…emotion?

He hits a harmonic wrong and winces.

**JEREMY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**
Was that actual *emotion*?  Did Jeff just open up like a real human man?

(He watches Jeff’s profile. Calm. Poised. Stoic.)

**JEREMY (V.O.)**
Or is he on fucking *crack*?

(Beat.)

**JEREMY (V.O.)**
No, not crack. Too smooth.  Maybe quaaludes?

(Jeff flicks a glance sideways—catches Jeremy looking.)

Jeremy smiles a little too wide. Jeff doesn’t break eye contact. Just raises one eyebrow. Barely. Jeremy looks away, back to his fretboard.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**
Whatever it was…I’ll take it.

(Beat.)

**JEREMY (V.O.)**
Just don’t let him get all soft on me.  I’m not ready to hear Jeff *feel things*.

*FADE OUT as they slide into the bridge, tension back in the strings, the garage humming like a reactor, and Jeremy still side-eyeing his brother like he’s just spotted a UFO in the middle of an otherwise perfect jam.*

---

# **CHAPTER THIRTEEN: DEDICATION AND DEVOTION**

---
## **INT. GILLEY GARAGE – 8:09 P.M. – POST-PRACTICE GLOW**

The amps are cooling. Sweat’s drying on necks. Jim’s already packing up his kit. Gilley’s swigging the last of the flat Gatorade. Bill’s labeling tapes. Kathy leans on her guitar case, hair matted, body spent—but **eyes alive**. She looks at the Evans brothers across the garage—Jeff coiling his cable, Jeremy snapping his strings loose.

**KATHY**
Hey.

(They both glance over.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
You two were in **perfect sync** tonight.

Jeremy blinks like he didn’t even realize. Jeff just tilts his head.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Every time you, Jeremy, let something *breathe*—spaced out a phrase, held a gap—Jeff filled it.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
And when *you* went wild?  Jeff stayed **restrained**. He didn’t chase you.  He grounded it.

She crosses her arms, almost like she’s processing it aloud.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
That was…**simpatico**.

Jeremy scratches the back of his neck, suddenly a little awkward.

**JEREMY**
We didn’t plan it.

Jeff shrugs.

**JEFF**
Didn’t have to.

Kathy nods.

**KATHY**
No.  You didn’t.

(She smiles, just a little.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
It was like…You were building a bridge and he was pouring the foundation at the same time.

(Silence.)

**JIM**
…Gross.

Everyone laughs. But the point is made.  **They felt it too.**

*FADE OUT on Kathy gathering her lyric sheets, tucking them away with a different kind of pride. Tonight wasn’t just about good practice—it was proof. The band is fusing. The brothers are aligned. And the music?* **It’s becoming something more.**

---

## **INT. GILLEY GARAGE – 8:12 P.M. – POST-PRACTICE DEBRIEF, CARNIVAL EDITION**

The tension has cooled into satisfaction. Kathy’s praise lingers in the air like incense. Gilley squints at her.

**GILLEY**
You’re gonna have to define the word **simpatico** for me.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
I didn’t get a **25** on the ACT, you know.

(He yawns.)

Jeremy doesn’t miss a beat.

**JEREMY**
No—you got a **32**, you shit-bagged freak.

(Beat.)

**JEREMY (CONT’D)**
**Fuckwheat!!**

(Everyone freezes.)

**KATHY**
…What?

**JIM**
What the actual hell does that even mean?

**JEREMY**
I don’t know. It felt right.

**BILL**
We really should never let him eat anything with red dye number five in it.

**JEFF**
Or sleep more than six hours.

Gilley, meanwhile, is still chewing on "simpatico," mentally slotting it somewhere between "taco" and "psycho."

**GILLEY**
So like… musically on the same page?

**KATHY**
No. Like **same sentence. Same breath.**  Like instinct-level partnership.

Gilley nods slowly.

**GILLEY**
That sounds exhausting.

FADE OUT on the band gathering their gear, half-laughing, half-dead, fully wired with the energy of something that went **better than they expected**. Tonight was weird. Tonight was sharp. Tonight was **real.**

And they’re starting to believe in it.

---

## **INT. GILLEY GARAGE – 8:14 P.M. – WIND-DOWN, RIBBING RESUMES**

Most of the gear’s packed. Everyone’s buzzing but low-key. Jeremy crouched over his pedalboard, wrapping cables with more force than necessary.

**JEREMY**
Okay, so, uh— **“Fuckwheat”** sounded a lot better in my head.

Everyone stifles laughter. Kathy snorts.

**KATHY**
You think?

**BILL**
It’s definitely an…agricultural stance.

**GILLEY**
What’d wheat ever do to you, man?

Jeremy waves them off with exaggerated shame.

**JEREMY**
Blasted profanity.  Jesus. That’s what that was.  Like a Tourette's-stricken Civil War general.

(Beat.)

Jeff looks up from his coiled cable.

**JEFF**
Maybe just… channel your rage.

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
Into, I don’t know… actual **lyrics** next time?

Jeremy glares.

**JEREMY**
You wound me.

Jeff shrugs.

**JEFF**
Try rhyme schemes.  Try a metaphor.  Try not yelling at grain.

**KATHY**
Try not giving the wheat lobby more ammunition.

They all crack up.

*FADE OUT as Jeremy mock-bows to the cornfield gods, and the garage finally goes quiet—alive with afterglow, sweat, and the buzz of a band that knows it’s starting to matter. Even when the rage goes sideways? It’s still part of the story.*

---

## **EXT. GILLEY GARAGE – 8:27 P.M. – POST-PRACTICE, SUMMER DUSK**

The gear is packed. Garage lights flicker out. The heat is still thick, heavy with the scent of old wood, sweat, and ozone. Gilley slaps his thighs, gestures toward the house.

**GILLEY**
Hey, Kathy—You wanna come in for a bit?

(Shrug.)

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
Just chill for a while?

**KATHY** (Already walking toward her car.)
**Hell no.**  I’m *gone*.  Home. Shower. Air conditioning. Pink pajamas.

Gilley raises his hands in surrender, grinning.

Jeremy turns toward Jeff and Bill.

**JEREMY**
Taco Bell?

**JEFF**
Obviously.

**BILL**
Crunchwrap Supreme or death.

Kathy stops. Turns.

**KATHY**
Wait.

(Beat.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
I never go with you to get anything at Taco Bell.

They all freeze.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
So…

(She walks back toward them, eyes gleaming.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
I’m inviting *myself* to go to Taco Bell.

(Silence.)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
You **fuckweeds** can just…

(she throws up her arms)

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
**WORSHIP.**

The band erupts into chaotic laughter.

**JIM**
I’m buying her a Diet Mt. Dew just for that.

**GILLEY**
We’ll need to clear the stage for her entrance.

**JEREMY**
All hail Queen of the Quesarito.

---

## **EXT. U.S.40 EAST – 8:44 P.M. – SUNSET GLORY**

Jim’s behind the wheel of the battered Civic, windows down, engine growling louder than it should. The speedometer’s bouncing past **80**.

**JEREMY** (backseat)
Jesus, man!

**BILL** (backseat)
Let him drive.

Kathy’s in the passenger seat, her hair whipping everywhere, lit by the **molten orange of the setting sun**. The wind howls through the cabin. And then—She **leans out the window**. Not a little. **All the way out**. Half her body into the wind. One hand braced on the roof. She **screams**. Long, loud, chaotic.

**KATHY**
*WOOOOOOOOO!!!*

Then she **laughs**.  Not a polite laugh. Not a giggle. A full-bodied, **whooping, hollering roar of life.**

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
WE FUCKING *RULE*!!!

Jeremy sticks his hand out the rear window like it’s surfing the wind. Bill’s yelling something about physics. No one listens. Jim?  He keeps it steady. Focused.  But his smile betrays everything.

**JIM (V.O.)**
This.

(Beat.)

**JIM (V.O.) (CONT’D)**
This is what it’s for.

The sun melts into the cornfields.  The Civic barrels east.  Their hearts beat louder than the radio.

*FADE OUT on the road ahead—open, wide, endless. They don’t know where they’re going yet.*

But tonight? **All is right in the world.

---

# **FIN*
